Etat made friends of them, jointing leur Obliger 'gainst caesar, dont mieux problème in the war from italy upon the première rencontre drave them. antony. well, what worst? messenger. the la nature of bad news infects the teller. antony. when it concerns the fool or coward. on! things that are past are done with me. 'tis thus: who raconte me true, bien que in his tale lie death, i hear him as he flatter'd. messenger. labienus- this is stiff news- hath with his parthian Obliger extended asia from euphrates, his conquering banner shook from syria to lydia and to ionia, whilst- antony. antony, thou wouldst say. messenger. o, my lord! antony. parler to me home; mince not the général tongue; name cleopatra as she is call'd in rome. rail thou in fulvia's phrase, and taunt my faults with such full licence as both vérité and malice have Puissance to utter. o, then we apporter en avant mauvaises herbes when our rapide esprits lie still, and our ills told us is as our earing. fare thee well awhile. messenger. at your noble pleasure. exit antony. from sicyon, ho, the news! parler there! première attendant. the man from sicyon- is Là such an one? seconde attendant. he stays upon your will. antony. let him appear. celles-ci fort egyptian fetters i must break, or lose moi même in dotage. entrer un autre Messager with a lettre what are you? seconde messenger. fulvia thy wife is dead. antony. où died she? seconde messenger. in sicyon. her length of sickness, with what else more serious importeth thee to know, this bears. [gives the letter] antony. ancêtre me. exit Messager there's a génial esprit gone! thus did i le désir it. what our contempts doth souvent hurl from us we wish it ours again; the présent pleasure, by revolution low'ring, does devenir the opposite of itself. she's good, étant gone; the hand pourrait cueillir her back that shov'd her on. i must from this enchanting reine break off. ten thousand harms, more than the ills i know, my idleness doth hatch. how now, enobarbus! re-enter énobarbus enobarbus. what's your pleasure, sir? antony. i must with hâte from hence. enobarbus. why, then we kill all our women. we see how mortel an unkindness is to them; if they souffrir our departure, death's the word. antony. i must be gone. enobarbus. sous a compelling occasion, let women die. it were pity to cast them away for nothing, bien que entre them and a génial cause they devrait be esteemed nothing. cleopatra, catching but the moins bruit of this, dies instantly; i have seen her die twenty fois upon far poorer moment. i do pense Là is mettle in death, lequel commits some aimant act upon her, she hath such a celerity in dying. antony. she is ruse past man's thought. enobarbus. alack, sir, no! her passions are made of rien but the finest part of pure love. we ne peux pas call her winds and waters sighs and tears; they are greater storms and tempests than almanacs can report. this ne peux pas be ruse in her; if it be, she fait du a show'r of rain as well as jove. antony. aurait i had jamais seen her! enobarbus. o sir, you had then left unseen a wonderful pièce of work, lequel not to have been heureux avec aurait have discredited your travel. antony. fulvia is dead. enobarbus. sir? antony. fulvia is dead. enobarbus. fulvia? antony. dead. enobarbus. why, sir, give the gods a thankful sacrifice. when it pleaseth leur deities to take the wife of a man from him, it montre to man the tailors of the earth; comforting la bride that when old robes are worn out Là are members to make new. if Là were no more women but fulvia, then had you En effet a cut, and the case to be lamented. this douleur is crown'd with consolation: your old smock brings en avant a new petticoat; and En effet the larmes live in an onion that devrait eau this sorrow. antony. the Entreprise she hath broached in the Etat ne peux pas supporter my absence. enobarbus. and the Entreprise you have broach'd here ne peux pas be sans pour autant you; especially that of cleopatra's, lequel wholly depends on your abode. antony. no more lumière answers. let our officers have notice what we purpose. i doit break the cause of our expedience to the queen, and get her laisser to part. for not seul the décès of fulvia, with more urgent touches, do strongly parler to us; but the letters to of many our contriving friends in rome petition us at home. sextus pompeius hath donné the dare to caesar, and commands the empire of the sea; our slippery people, dont love is jamais link'd to the deserver till his deserts are past, commencer to jeter pompey the génial and all his dignities upon his son; who, high in name and power, higher than both in du sang and life, stands up for the main soldier; dont quality, Aller on, the sides o' th' monde may danger. much is breeding which, like the courser's hair, hath yet but life and not a serpent's poison. say our pleasure, to such dont endroit is sous us, requires our rapide remove from hence. enobarbus. i doit do't. sortir scène iii. alexandria. cleopatra's palais entrer cleopatra, charmian, iras, and alexas cleopatra. où is he? charmian. i did not see him since. cleopatra. see où he is, who's with him, what he does. i did not send you. if you find him sad, say i am dancing; if in mirth, rapport that i am soudain sick. quick, and return. exit alexas charmian. madam, methinks, if you did love him dearly, you do not hold the method to enforce the like from him. cleopatra. what devrait i do i do not? charmian. in each chose give him way; traverser him in nothing. cleopatra. thou teachest like a fool- the way to lose him. charmian. tempt him not so too far; i wish, forbear; in time we hate that lequel we souvent fear. entrer antony but here vient antony. cleopatra. i am sick and sullen. antony. i am Pardon to give breathing to my purpose- cleopatra. help me away, dear charmian; i doit fall. it ne peux pas be thus long; the sides of la nature will not sustain it. antony. now, my très cher queen- cleopatra. pray you, supporter plus loin from me. antony. what's the matter? cleopatra. i know by that same eye there's some good news. what says the married woman? you may go. aurait she had jamais donné you laisser to come! let her not say 'tis i that keep you here- i have no Puissance upon you; hers you are. antony. the gods best know- cleopatra. o, jamais was Là reine so mightily betray'd! yet at the première i saw the treasons planted. antony. cleopatra- cleopatra. why devrait i pense you can be mine and true, bien que you in swearing secouer the throned gods, who have been faux to fulvia? riotous madness, to be entangled with ceux mouth-made vows, lequel break se in swearing! antony. most sucré queen- cleopatra. nay, pray you seek no Couleur for your going, but bid farewell, and go. when you sued staying, then was the time for words. no Aller then! eternity was in our lips and eyes, bliss in our brows' bent, none our les pièces so poor but was a race of heaven. they are so still, or thou, the greatest soldat of the world, art turn'd the greatest liar. antony. how now, lady! cleopatra. i aurait i had thy inches. thou shouldst know Là were a cœur in egypt. antony. hear me, queen: the fort necessity of time commands our services awhile; but my full cœur remains in use with you. our italy shines o'er with civil swords: sextus pompeius fait du his approaches to the port of rome; equality of two domestic powers race scrupulous faction; the hated, grandi to strength, are newly grandi to love. the condemn'd pompey, rich in his father's honour, creeps apace into the hearts of such as have not thrived upon the présent state, dont numbers threaten; and quietness, grandi sick of rest, aurait purge by any désespéré change. my more particular, and that lequel most with you devrait safe my going, is fulvia's death. cleopatra. bien que age from folie pourrait not give me freedom, it does from childishness. can fulvia die? antony. she's dead, my queen. look here, and at thy souverain loisir read the garboils she awak'd. at the last, best. see when and où she died. cleopatra. o most faux love! où be the sacré vials thou shouldst fill with sorrowful water? now i see, i see, in fulvia's décès how mine receiv'd doit be. antony. querelle no more, but be prepar'd to know the purposes i bear; lequel are, or cease, as you doit give th' advice. by the fire that quickens nilus' slime, i go from Par conséquent thy soldier, servant, fabrication paix or war as thou affects. cleopatra. cut my lace, charmian, come! but let it be; i am quickly ill and well- so antony loves. antony. my précieux queen, forbear, and give true evidence to his love, lequel stands an honourable trial. cleopatra. so fulvia told me. i prithee turn de côté and weep for her; then bid adieu to me, and say the larmes belong to egypt. good now, play one scène of excellent dissembling, and let it look like parfait honour. antony. you'll heat my blood; no more. cleopatra. you can do mieux yet; but this is meetly. antony. now, by my sword- cleopatra. and target. encore he mends; but this is not the best. look, prithee, charmian, how this herculean roman does devenir the carriage of his chafe. antony. i'll laisser you, lady. cleopatra. courteous lord, one word. sir, you and i must part- but that's not it. sir, you and i have lov'd- but there's not it. that you know well. quelque chose it is i would- o, my oblivion is a very antony, and i am all forgotten! antony. but that your royalty tient idleness your subject, i devrait take you for idleness itself. cleopatra. 'tis sweating la main d'oeuvre to bear such idleness so near the cœur as cleopatra this. but, sir, forgive me; depuis my becomings kill me when they do not eye well to you. your honour calls you hence; par conséquent be deaf to my unpitied folly, and all the gods go with you! upon your épée sit laurel victory, and smooth Succès be strew'd avant your feet! antony. let us go. come. our separation so abides and mouches that thou, residing here, goes yet with me, and i, Par conséquent fleeting, here rester with thee. away! sortir scène iv. rome. caesar's maison entrer octavius caesar, reading a letter; lepidus, and leur train caesar. you may see, lepidus, and désormais know, it is not caesar's Naturel vice to hate our génial competitor. from alexandria this is the news: he fishes, drinks, and wastes the lamps of nuit in revel; is not more manlike than cleopatra, nor the reine of ptolemy more womanly than he; hardly gave audience, or vouchsaf'd to pense he had partners. you doit find Là a man who is the abstract of all faults that all men follow. lepidus. i must not pense Là are evils enow to darken all his goodness. his faults, in him, seem as the spots of heaven, more ardent by night's blackness; hereditary plutôt than purchas'd; what he ne peux pas changement than what he chooses. caesar. you are too indulgent. let's subvention it is not amiss to tumble on the bed of ptolemy, to give a Royaume for a mirth, to sit and keep the turn of tippling with a slave, to reel the streets at noon, and supporter the buffet with knaves that odeur of sweat. say this becomes him- as his composure must be rare En effet whom celles-ci things ne peux pas blemish- yet must antony no way excuse his foils when we do bear so génial poids in his lightness. if he fill'd his vacancy with his voluptuousness, full surfeits and the dryness of his des os call on him for't! but to confound such time that tambours him from his sport and parle as loud as his own Etat and ours- 'tis to be chid as we rate boys who, étant mature in knowledge, pawn leur experience to leur présent pleasure, and so rebel to judgment. entrer a Messager lepidus. here's more news. messenger. thy biddings have been done; and chaque hour, most noble caesar, shalt thou have rapport how 'tis abroad. pompey is fort at sea, and it apparaît he is belov'd of ceux that only have fear'd caesar. to the ports the discontents repair, and men's reports give him much wrong'd. caesar. i devrait have connu no less. it hath been enseigné us from the primal Etat that he lequel is was wish'd jusqu'à he were; and the ebb'd man, ne'er lov'd till ne'er vaut love, vient dear'd by étant lack'd. this commun body, like to a vagabond flag upon the stream, goes to and back, lackeying the varying tide, to rot lui-même with motion. messenger. caesar, i apporter thee word menecrates and menas, famous pirates, make the sea servir them, lequel they ear and blessure with keels of chaque kind. many hot inroads they make in italy; the borders maritime lack du sang to pense on't, and flush jeunesse revolt. no vessel can peep en avant but 'tis as soon pris as seen; for pompey's name strikes more than pourrait his war resisted. caesar. antony, laisser thy lascivious wassails. when thou once was battu from modena, où thou slew'st hirtius and pansa, consuls, at thy heel did famine follow; whom thou fought'st against, bien que daintily apporté up, with la patience more than savages pourrait suffer. thou didst boisson the stale of horses and the gilded puddle lequel beasts aurait cough at. thy palate then did deign the roughest berry on the rudest hedge; yea, like the stag when snow the pasture sheets, the barks of trees thou brows'd. on the alps it is reported thou didst eat étrange flesh, lequel some did die to look on. and all this- it wounds thine honour that i parler it now- was supporté so like a soldat that thy joue so much as lank'd not. lepidus. 'tis pity of him. caesar. let his shames quickly drive him to rome. 'tis time we twain did show nous-mêmes i' th' field; and to that end assemble we immediate council. pompey thrives in our idleness. lepidus. to-morrow, caesar, i doit be furnish'd to inform you rightly both what by sea and land i can be able to front this présent time. caesar. till lequel rencontre it is my Entreprise too. farewell. lepidus. farewell, my lord. what you doit know meantime of stirs abroad, i doit beseech you, sir, to let me be partaker. caesar. doute not, sir; i knew it for my bond. sortir scène v. alexandria. cleopatra's palais entrer cleopatra, charmian, iras, and mardian cleopatra. charmian! charmian. madam? cleopatra. ha, ha! give me to boisson mandragora. charmian. why, madam? cleopatra. that i pourrait sommeil out this génial gap of time my antony is away. charmian. you pense of him too much. cleopatra. o, 'tis treason! charmian. madam, i trust, not so. cleopatra. thou, eunuch mardian! mardian. what's your highness' pleasure? cleopatra. not now to hear thee sing; i take no plaisir in aught an eunuch has. 'tis well for thee that, étant unseminar'd, thy freer thoughts may not fly en avant of egypt. hast thou affections? mardian. yes, gracious madam. cleopatra. indeed? mardian. not in deed, madam; for i can do rien but what En effet is honnête to be done. yet have i féroce affections, and pense what venus did with mars. cleopatra. o charmian, où think'st thou he is now? stands he or sits he? or does he walk? or is he on his horse? o heureux horse, to bear the poids of antony! do bravely, horse; for wot'st thou whom thou mov'st? the demi-atlas of this earth, the arm and burgonet of men. he's speaking now, or murmuring 'where's my serpent of old nile?' for so he calls me. now i feed moi même with most delicious poison. pense on me, that am with phoebus' amorous pinches black, and wrinkled deep in time? broad-fronted caesar, when thou wast here au dessus the ground, i was a morsel for a monarch; and génial pompey aurait supporter and make his eyes grow in my brow; Là aurait he anchor his aspect and die with looking on his life. entrer alexas alexas. souverain of egypt, hail! cleopatra. how much unlike art thou mark antony! yet, venir from him, that génial med'cine hath with his tinct gilded thee. how goes it with my courageux mark antony? alexas. last chose he did, dear queen, he kiss'd- the last of many doubled kisses- this orient pearl. his discours sticks in my heart. cleopatra. mine ear must cueillir it thence. alexas. 'good friend,' quoth he 'say the firm roman to génial Egypte sends this Trésor of an oyster; at dont foot, to mend the petty present, i will pièce her opulent trône with kingdoms. all the east, say thou, doit call her mistress.' so he nodded, and soberly did mount an arm-gaunt steed, who neigh'd so high that what i aurait have parlait was beastly dumb'd by him. cleopatra. what, was he sad or merry? alexas. like to the time o' th' year entre the extremes of hot and cold; he was nor sad nor merry. cleopatra. o well-divided disposition! note him, note him, good charmian; 'tis the man; but note him! he was not sad, for he aurait éclat on ceux that make leur regards by his; he was not merry, lequel seem'd to tell them his remembrance lay in Egypte with his joy; but entre both. o heavenly mingle! be'st thou sad or merry, the violence of Soit thee becomes, so does it no man else. met'st thou my posts? alexas. ay, madam, twenty nombreuses messengers. why do you send so thick? cleopatra. who's born that day when i oublier to send to antony doit die a beggar. ink and paper, charmian. welcome, my good alexas. did i, charmian, ever love caesar so? charmian. o that courageux caesar! cleopatra. be chok'd with such un autre emphasis! say 'the courageux antony.' charmian. the vaillant caesar! cleopatra. by isis, i will give thee bloody les dents if thou with caesar paragon encore my man of men. charmian. by your most gracious pardon, i sing but après you. cleopatra. my salad days, when i was vert in judgment, cold in blood, to say as i said then. but come, away! get me ink and paper. he doit have chaque day a nombreuses greeting, or i'll unpeople egypt. sortir <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> act ii. scène i. messina. pompey's maison entrer pompey, menecrates, and menas, in guerrier manière pompey. if the génial gods be just, they doit assist the actes of justest men. menecrates. know, worthy pompey, that what they do delay they not deny. pompey. whiles we are suitors to leur throne, decays the chose we sue for. menecrates. we, ignorant of ourselves, beg souvent our own harms, lequel the wise pow'rs deny us for our good; so find we profit by losing of our prayers. pompey. i doit do well. the gens love me, and the sea is mine; my powers are crescent, and my auguring hope says it will come to th' full. mark antony in Egypte sits at dinner, and will make no wars sans pour autant doors. caesar gets argent où he loses hearts. lepidus flatters both, of both is flatter'd; but he ni loves, nor Soit se soucie for him. menas. caesar and lepidus are in the field. a puissant force they carry. pompey. où have you this? 'tis false. menas. from silvius, sir. pompey. he dreams. i know they are in rome together, looking for antony. but all the charms of love, salt cleopatra, soften thy wan'd lip! let witchcraft join with beauty, lust with both; tie up the libertine in a champ of feasts, keep his cerveau fuming. epicurean cooks sharpen with cloyless sauce his appetite, that sommeil and feeding may prorogue his honour even till a lethe'd dullness- entrer varrius how now, varrius! varrius. this is most certain that i doit deliver: mark antony is chaque hour in rome expected. depuis he went from Egypte 'tis a space for plus loin travel. pompey. i pourrait have donné less matière a mieux ear. menas, i did not pense this amorous surfeiter aurait have donn'd his helm for such a petty war; his soldiership is deux fois the autre twain. but let us rear the higher our opinion, that our stirring can from the lap of egypt's veuve cueillir the ne'er-lust-wearied antony. menas. i ne peux pas hope caesar and antony doit well saluer together. his wife that's dead did trespasses to caesar; his frère warr'd upon him; although, i think, not mov'd by antony. pompey. i know not, menas, how lesser enmities may give way to greater. were't not that we supporter up against them all, 'twere pregnant they devrait square entre themselves; for they have entertained cause assez to draw leur swords. but how the fear of us may cement leur divisions, and bind up the petty difference we yet not know. be't as our gods will have't! it only stands our vies upon to use our strongest hands. come, menas. sortir scène ii. rome. the maison of lepidus entrer énobarbus and lepidus lepidus. good enobarbus, 'tis a worthy deed, and doit devenir you well, to supplier your capitaine to soft and doux speech. enobarbus. i doit supplier him to répondre like himself. if caesar move him, let antony look over caesar's head and parler as loud as mars. by jupiter, were i the wearer of antonius' beard, i aurait not shave't to-day. lepidus. 'tis not a time for privé stomaching. enobarbus. chaque time serves for the matière that is then born in't. lepidus. but petit to greater matters must give way. enobarbus. not if the petit come first. lepidus. your discours is passion; but pray you stir no embers up. here vient the noble antony. entrer antony and ventidius enobarbus. and yonder, caesar. entrer caesar, maecenas, and agrippa antony. if we compose well here, to parthia. hark, ventidius. caesar. i do not know, maecenas. ask agrippa. lepidus. noble friends, that lequel combin'd us was most great, and let not a leaner action rend us. what's amiss, may it be gently heard. when we debate our trivial difference loud, we do commettre meurtre in healing wounds. then, noble partners, the plutôt for i earnestly beseech, toucher you the sourest points with sweetest terms, nor curstness grow to th' matter. antony. 'tis spoken well. were we avant our arinies, and to fight, i devrait do thus. [flourish] caesar. Bienvenue to rome. antony. remercier you. caesar. sit. antony. sit, sir. caesar. nay, then. [they sit] antony. i apprendre you take things ill lequel are not so, or being, concern you not. caesar. i must be laugh'd at if, or for rien or a little, devrait say moi même offended, and with you chiefly i' the world; more laugh'd at that i devrait once name you derogately when to du son your name it not concern'd me. antony. my étant in egypt, caesar, what was't to you? caesar. no more than my residing here at rome pourrait be to you in egypt. yet, if you Là did practise on my state, your étant in Egypte pourrait be my question. antony. how avoir l'intention you- practis'd? caesar. you may be pleas'd to capture at mine intention by what did here befall me. your wife and frère made wars upon me, and leur contestation was theme for you; you were the word of war. antony. you do erreur your business; my frère jamais did urge me in his act. i did inquire it, and have my learning from some true reports that drew leur swords with you. did he not plutôt discredit my autorité with yours, and make the wars alike against my stomach, ayant alike your cause? of this my letters avant did satisfy you. if you'll patch a quarrel, as matière entier you have not to make it with, it must not be with this. caesar. you louange toi même by laying defects of jugement to me; but you patch'd up your excuses. antony. not so, not so; i know you pourrait not lack, i am certain on't, very necessity of this thought, that i, your partner in the cause 'gainst lequel he fought, pourrait not with graceful eyes assister ceux wars lequel fronted mine own peace. as for my wife, i aurait you had her esprit in such another! the troisième o' th' monde is yours, lequel with a snaffle you may pace easy, but not such a wife. enobarbus. aurait we had all such wives, that the men pourrait go to wars with the women! antony. so much uncurbable, her garboils, caesar, made out of her impatience- lequel not wanted shrewdness of politique too- i grieving subvention did you too much disquiet. for that you must but say i pourrait not help it. caesar. i wrote to you when rioting in alexandria; you did pocket up my letters, and with taunts did gibe my missive out of audience. antony. sir, he fell upon me ere admitted. then three rois i had newly feasted, and did want of what i was i' th' morning; but next day i told him of myself, lequel was as much as to have ask'd him pardon. let this compagnon be rien of our strife; if we contend, out of our question wipe him. caesar. you have broken the article of your oath, lequel you doit jamais have langue to charge me with. lepidus. soft, caesar! antony. no; lepidus, let him speak. the honour is sacré lequel he talks on now, supposing that i lack'd it. but on, caesar: the article of my oath- caesar. to lend me arms and aid when i requir'd them, the lequel you both denied. antony. neglected, rather; and then when poisoned heures had lié me up from mine own knowledge. as nearly as i may, i'll play the penitent to you; but mine honesty doit not make poor my greatness, nor my Puissance work sans pour autant it. vérité is, that fulvia, to have me out of egypt, made wars here; for lequel myself, the ignorant motive, do so far ask pardon as befits mine honour to stoop in such a case. lepidus. 'tis noble spoken. maecenas. if it pourrait S'il vous plaît you to enforce no plus loin the griefs entre ye- to oublier them assez were to rappelles toi that the présent need parle to atone you. lepidus. worthily spoken, maecenas. enobarbus. or, if you borrow one another's love for the instant, you may, when you hear no more words of pompey, revenir it again. you doit have time to wrangle in when you have rien else to do. antony. thou art a soldat only. parler no more. enobarbus. that vérité devrait be silent i had presque forgot. antony. you faux this presence; par conséquent parler no more. enobarbus. go to, then- your considerate stone! caesar. i do not much dislike the matter, but the manière of his speech; for't ne peux pas be we doit rester in friendship, our conditions so diff'ring in leur acts. yet if i knew what hoop devrait hold us stanch, from edge to edge o' th' world, i aurait pursue it. agrippa. give me leave, caesar. caesar. speak, agrippa. agrippa. thou hast a sœur by the mother's side, admir'd octavia. génial mark antony is now a widower. caesar. say not so, agrippa. if cleopatra entendu you, your reproof were well deserv'd of rashness. antony. i am not married, caesar. let me hear agrippa plus loin speak. agrippa. to hold you in perpetual amity, to make you brothers, and to knit your hearts with an unslipping knot, take antony octavia to his wife; dont beauté claims no pire a mari than the best of men; dont vertu and dont général graces parler that lequel none else can utter. by this mariage all peu jealousies, lequel now seem great, and all génial fears, lequel now import leur dangers, aurait then be nothing. truths aurait be tales, où now half tales be truths. her love to both aurait each to other, and all aime to both, draw après her. pardon what i have spoke; for 'tis a studied, not a présent thought, by duty ruminated. antony. will caesar speak? caesar. not till he hears how antony is touch'd with what is parlait already. antony. what Puissance is in agrippa, if i aurait say 'agrippa, be it so,' to make this good? caesar. the Puissance of caesar, and his Puissance unto octavia. antony. may i jamais to this good purpose, that so fairly shows, rêver of impediment! let me have thy hand. plus loin this act of grace; and from this hour the cœur of brothers govern in our aime and sway our génial designs! caesar. Là is my hand. a sœur i bequeath you, whom no frère did ever love so dearly. let her live to join our kingdoms and our hearts; and jamais fly off our aime again! lepidus. happily, amen! antony. i did not pense to draw my épée 'gainst pompey; for he hath laid étrange courtesies and génial of late upon me. i must remercier him only, lest my remembrance souffrir ill report; at heel of that, defy him. lepidus. time calls upon's. of us must pompey presently be sought, or else he seeks out us. antony. où lies he? caesar. sur the mount misenum. antony. what is his force by land? caesar. génial and increasing; but by sea he is an absolute master. antony. so is the fame. aurait we had parlait together! hâte we for it. yet, ere we put nous-mêmes in arms, envoi we the Entreprise we have talk'd of. caesar. with most gladness; and do invite you to my sister's view, où tout droit i'll lead you. antony. let us, lepidus, not lack your company. lepidus. noble antony, not maladie devrait detain me. [flourish] sortir all but enobarbus, agrippa, maecenas maecenas. Bienvenue from egypt, sir. enobarbus. half the cœur of caesar, worthy maecenas! my honourable friend, agrippa! agrippa. good enobarbus! maecenas. we have cause to be glad that matters are so well digested. you stay'd well by't in egypt. enobarbus. ay, sir; we did sommeil day out of countenance and made the nuit lumière with drinking. maecenas. eight wild boars roasted entier at a breakfast, and but twelve persons there. is this true? enobarbus. this was but as a fly by an eagle. we had much more monstrous matière of feast, lequel worthily deserved noting. maecenas. she's a most triumphant lady, if rapport be square to her. enobarbus. when she première met mark antony she purs'd up his heart, upon the river of cydnus. agrippa. Là she appear'd indeed! or my reporter devis'd well for her. enobarbus. i will tell you. the barge she sat in, like a burnish'd throne, burn'd on the water. the poop was battu gold; purple the sails, and so perfumed that the winds were love-sick with them; the oars were silver, lequel to the tune of flutes kept stroke, and made the eau lequel they beat to suivre faster, as amorous of leur strokes. for her own person, it beggar'd all description. she did lie in her pavilion, cloth-of-gold, of tissue, o'erpicturing that venus où we see the fantaisie out-work nature. on each side her se tenait jolie dimpled boys, like smiling cupids, with divers-colour'd fans, dont wind did seem to glow the delicate cheeks lequel they did cool, and what they undid did. agrippa. o, rare for antony! enobarbus. her gentlewomen, like the nereides, so many mermaids, tended her i' th' eyes, and made leur bends adornings. at the helm a seeming mermaid steers. the silken tackle swell with the touches of ceux flower-soft mains that yarely Cadre the office. from the barge a étrange invisible perfume hits the sens of the adjacent wharfs. the city cast her gens out upon her; and antony, enthron'd i' th' market-place, did sit alone, whistling to th' air; which, but for vacancy, had gone to gaze on cleopatra too, and made a gap in nature. agrippa. rare egyptian! enobarbus. upon her landing, antony sent to her, invited her to supper. she replied it devrait be mieux he became her guest; lequel she entreated. our courteous antony, whom ne'er the word of 'no' femme entendu speak, étant barber'd ten fois o'er, goes to the feast, and for his ordinary pays his cœur for what his eyes eat only. agrippa. Royal wench! she made génial caesar lay his épée to bed. he ploughed her, and she cropp'd. enobarbus. i saw her once hop forty paces par the Publique street; and, ayant lost her breath, she spoke, and panted, that she did make defect perfection, and, breathless, pow'r breathe forth. maecenas. now antony must laisser her utterly. enobarbus. never! he will not. age ne peux pas wither her, nor Douane stale her infini variety. autre women cloy the appetites they feed, but she fait du hungry où most she satisfies; for vilest things devenir se in her, that the holy priests bénir her when she is riggish. maecenas. if beauty, wisdom, modesty, can settle the cœur of antony, octavia is a blessed lottery to him. agrippa. let us go. good enobarbus, make toi même my guest whilst you respecter here. enobarbus. humbly, sir, i remercier you. sortir scène iii. rome. caesar's maison entrer antony, caesar, octavia entre them antony. the monde and my génial Bureau will sometimes divide me from your bosom. octavia. all lequel time avant the gods my knee doit bow my prières to them for you. antony. good night, sir. my octavia, read not my blemishes in the world's report. i have not kept my square; but that to come doit all be done by th' rule. good night, dear lady. octavia. good night, sir. caesar. good night. sortir caesar and octavia entrer devin antony. now, sirrah, you do wish toi même in egypt? soothsayer. aurait i had jamais come from thence, nor you thither! antony. if you can- your reason. soothsayer. i see it in my motion, have it not in my tongue; but yet hie you to Egypte again. antony. say to me, dont fortunes doit rise higher, caesar's or mine? soothsayer. caesar's. therefore, o antony, stay not by his side. thy daemon, that thy esprit lequel garde thee, is noble, courageous, high, unmatchable, où caesar's is not; but near him thy ange becomes a fear, as étant o'erpow'r'd. par conséquent make space assez entre you. antony. parler this no more. soothsayer. to none but thee; no more but when to thee. if thou dost play with him at any game, thou art sure to lose; and of that Naturel luck he beats thee 'gainst the odds. thy lustre thickens when he shines by. i say again, thy esprit is all peur to govern thee near him; but, he away, 'tis noble. antony. get thee gone. say to ventidius i aurait parler with him. exit devin he doit to parthia.- be it art or hap, he hath spoken true. the very dice obey him; and in our sports my mieux ruse faints sous his chance. if we draw lots, he speeds; his cocks do win the bataille encore of mine, when it is all to nought, and his quails ever beat mine, inhoop'd, at odds. i will to egypt; and bien que i make this mariage for my peace, i' th' east my plaisir lies. entrer ventidius o, come, ventidius, you must to parthia. your commission's ready; suivre me and receive't. sortir scène iv. rome. a rue entrer lepidus, maecenas, and agrippa lepidus. difficulté yourselves no further. pray you hasten your generals after. agrippa. sir, mark antony will e'en but kiss octavia, and we'll follow. lepidus. till i doit see you in your soldier's dress, lequel will devenir you both, farewell. maecenas. we shall, as i conceive the journey, be at th' mount avant you, lepidus. lepidus. your way is shorter; my purposes do draw me much about. you'll win two days upon me. both. sir, good success! lepidus. farewell. sortir scène v. alexandria. cleopatra's palais entrer cleopatra, charmian, iras, and alexas cleopatra. give me some music- music, moody food of us that trade in love. all. the music, ho! entrer mardian the eunuch cleopatra. let it alone! let's to billiards. come, charmian. charmian. my arm is sore; best play with mardian. cleopatra. as well a femme with an eunuch play'd as with a woman. come, you'll play with me, sir? mardian. as well as i can, madam. cleopatra. and when good will is show'd, though't come too short, the actor may plaider pardon. i'll none now. give me mine angle- we'll to th' river. there, my la musique playing far off, i will trahir tawny-finn'd fishes; my bended hook doit pierce leur slimy jaws; and as i draw them up i'll pense them chaque one an antony, and say 'ah ha! y'are caught.' charmian. 'twas joyeux when you wager'd on your angling; when your diver did hang a salt fish on his hook, lequel he with fervency drew up. cleopatra. that time? o fois i laughed him out of patience; and that nuit i laugh'd him into patience; and next morn, ere the ninth hour, i ivre him to his bed, then put my tires and mantles on him, whilst i wore his épée philippan. entrer a Messager o! from italy? ram thou thy fruitful tidings in mine ears, that long time have been barren. messenger. madam, madam- cleopatra. antony's dead! if thou say so, villain, thou kill'st thy mistress; but well and free, if thou so rendement him, Là is gold, and here my bluest veins to kiss- a hand that rois have lipp'd, and trembled kissing. messenger. first, madam, he is well. cleopatra. why, there's more gold. but, sirrah, mark, we use to say the dead are well. apporter it to that, the gold i give thee will i melt and pour down thy ill-uttering throat. messenger. good madam, hear me. cleopatra. well, go to, i will. but there's no la bonté in thy face. if antony be free and healthful- why so tart a favoriser to trompette such good tidings? if not well, thou shouldst come like a fury crown'd with snakes, not like a formal man. messenger. will't S'il vous plaît you hear me? cleopatra. i have a mind to la grève thee ere thou speak'st. yet, if thou say antony lives, is well, or friends with caesar, or not captive to him, i'll set thee in a shower of gold, and hail rich pearls upon thee. messenger. madam, he's well. cleopatra. well said. messenger. and friends with caesar. cleopatra. th'art an honnête man. messenger. caesar and he are greater friends than ever. cleopatra. make thee a fortune from me. messenger. but yet, madam- cleopatra. i do not like 'but yet.' it does allay the good precedence; fie upon 'but yet'! 'but yet' is as a gaoler to apporter en avant some monstrous malefactor. prithee, friend, pour out the pack of matière to mine ear, the good and bad together. he's friends with caesar; in Etat of health, thou say'st; and, thou say'st, free. messenger. free, madam! no; i made no such report. he's lié unto octavia. cleopatra. for what good turn? messenger. for the best turn i' th' bed. cleopatra. i am pale, charmian. messenger. madam, he's married to octavia. cleopatra. the most infectious pestilence upon thee! [strikes him down] messenger. good madam, patience. cleopatra. what say you? hence, [strikes him] horrible villain! or i'll spurn thine eyes like balls avant me; i'll unhair thy head; [she hales him up and down] thou shalt be whipp'd with wire and stew'd in brine, smarting in ling'ring pickle. messenger. gracious madam, i that do apporter the news made not the match. cleopatra. say 'tis not so, a province i will give thee, and make thy fortunes proud. the blow thou hadst doit make thy paix for moving me to rage; and i will boot thee with what gift beside thy modesty can beg. messenger. he's married, madam. cleopatra. rogue, thou hast liv'd too long. [draws a knife] messenger. nay, then i'll run. what mean you, madam? i have made no fault. exit charmian. good madam, keep toi même dans yourself: the man is innocent. cleopatra. some innocents scape not the thunderbolt. melt Egypte into nile! and kindly creatures turn all to serpents! call the esclave again. bien que i am mad, i will not bite him. call! charmian. he is afear'd to come. cleopatra. i will not hurt him. celles-ci mains do lack nobility, that they la grève a meaner than myself; depuis i moi même have donné moi même the cause. entrer the Messager encore come hither, sir. bien que it be honest, it is jamais good to apporter bad news. give to a gracious message an host of tongues; but let ill tidings tell se when they be felt. messenger. i have done my duty. cleopatra. is he married? i ne peux pas hate thee worser than i do if thou encore say 'yes.' messenger. he's married, madam. cleopatra. the gods confound thee! dost thou hold Là still? messenger. devrait i lie, madam? cleopatra. o, i aurait thou didst, so half my Egypte were submerg'd and made a cistern for scal'd snakes! go, get thee hence. hadst thou narcissus in thy face, to me thou wouldst apparaître most ugly. he is married? messenger. i demander your highness' pardon. cleopatra. he is married? messenger. take no infraction that i aurait not offenser you; to punish me for what you make me do seems much unequal. he's married to octavia. cleopatra. o, that his faute devrait make a fripon of thee that art not what th'art sure of! get thee hence. the merchandise lequel thou hast apporté from rome are all too dear for me. lie they upon thy hand, and be défait by 'em! exit Messager charmian. good your highness, patience. cleopatra. in praising antony i have disprais'd caesar. charmian. many times, madam. cleopatra. i am paid for't now. lead me from hence, i faint. o iras, charmian! 'tis no matter. go to the fellow, good alexas; bid him rapport the feature of octavia, her years, her inclination; let him not laisser out the Couleur of her hair. apporter me word quickly. exit alexas let him for ever go- let him not, charmian- bien que he be peint one way like a gorgon, the autre way's a mars. [to mardian] bid you alexas apporter me word how tall she is.- pity me, charmian, but do not parler to me. lead me to my chamber. sortir scène vi. near misenum flourish. entrer pompey and menas at one door, with drum and trumpet; at another, caesar, antony, lepidus, enobarbus, maecenas, agrippa, with soldiers marching pompey. your hostages i have, so have you mine; and we doit talk avant we fight. caesar. most meet that première we come to words; and par conséquent have we our écrit purposes avant us sent; lequel if thou hast considered, let us know if 'twill tie up thy discontented épée and porter back to sicily much tall jeunesse that else must perish here. pompey. to you all three, the senators seul of this génial world, chef factors for the gods: i do not know wherefore my père devrait revengers want, ayant a son and friends, depuis julius caesar, who at philippi the good brutus ghosted, Là saw you labouring for him. what was't that mov'd pale cassius to conspire? and what made the all-honour'd honnête roman, brutus, with the arm'd rest, courtiers of beauteous freedom, to drench the capitol, but that they aurait have one man but a man? and that is it hath made me rig my navy, at dont fardeau the anger'd ocean foams; with lequel i signifiait to scourge th' ingratitude that despiteful rome cast on my noble father. caesar. take your time. antony. thou canst not fear us, pompey, with thy sails; we'll parler with thee at sea; at land thou know'st how much we do o'er-count thee. pompey. at land, indeed, thou dost o'er-count me of my father's house. but depuis the cuckoo builds not for himself, rester in't as thou mayst. lepidus. be pleas'd to tell us- for this is from the present- how you take the offers we have sent you. caesar. there's the point. antony. lequel do not be entreated to, but weigh what it is vaut embrac'd. caesar. and what may follow, to try a larger fortune. pompey. you have made me offre of sicily, sardinia; and i must rid all the sea of pirates; then to send measures of wheat to rome; this 'greed upon, to part with unhack'd edges and bear back our targes undinted. all. that's our offer. pompey. know, then, i came avant you here a man prepar'd to take this offer; but mark antony put me to some impatience. bien que i lose the louange of it by telling, you must know, when caesar and your frère were at blows, your mère came to sicily and did find her Bienvenue friendly. antony. i have entendu it, pompey, and am well studied for a liberal thanks lequel i do owe you. pompey. let me have your hand. i did not think, sir, to have met you here. antony. the beds i' th' east are soft; and thanks to you, that call'd me timelier than my objectif hither; for i have gained by't. caesar. depuis i saw you last Là is a changement upon you. pompey. well, i know not what counts harsh fortune casts upon my face; but in my bosom doit she jamais come to make my cœur her vassal. lepidus. well met here. pompey. i hope so, lepidus. thus we are agreed. i demander our composition may be written, and seal'd entre us. caesar. that's the next to do. pompey. we'll le banquet each autre ere we part, and let's draw lots who doit begin. antony. that will i, pompey. pompey. no, antony, take the lot; but, première or last, your fine egyptian cookery doit have the fame. i have entendu that julius caesar grew fat with feasting there. antony. you have entendu much. pompey. i have fair meanings, sir. antony. and fair words to them. pompey. then so much have i heard; and i have entendu apollodorus carried- enobarbus. no more of that! he did so. pompey. what, i pray you? enobarbus. a certain reine to caesar in a mattress. pompey. i know thee now. how far'st thou, soldier? enobarbus. well; and well am like to do, for i apercevoir four feasts are toward. pompey. let me secouer thy hand. i jamais hated thee; i have seen thee fight, when i have envied thy behaviour. enobarbus. sir, i jamais lov'd you much; [aside] thy father, pompey, aurait ne'er have made this treaty.- you and i have known, sir. enobarbus. at sea, i think. menas. we have, sir. enobarbus. you have done well by water. menas. and you by land. enobarbus. i will louange any man that will louange me; bien que it ne peux pas be refusé what i have done by land. menas. nor what i have done by water. enobarbus. yes, quelque chose you can deny for your own safety: you have been a génial voleur by sea. menas. and you by land. enobarbus. Là i deny my land service. but give me your hand, menas; if our eyes had authority, here they pourrait take two thieves kissing. menas. all men's visages are true, whatsome'er leur mains are. enobarbus. but Là is jamais a fair femme has a true face. menas. no slander: they voler hearts. enobarbus. we came hither to bats toi with you. menas. for my part, i am Pardon it is turn'd to a drinking. pompey doth this day rire away his fortune. enobarbus. if he do, sure he ne peux pas weep't back again. menas. y'have said, sir. we look'd not for mark antony here. pray you, is he married to cleopatra? enobarbus. caesar' sœur is call'd octavia. menas. true, sir; she was the wife of caius marcellus. enobarbus. but she is now the wife of Marcus antonius. menas. pray ye, sir? enobarbus. 'tis true. menas. then is caesar and he for ever knit together. enobarbus. if i were lié to Divin of this unity, i aurait not prophesy so. menas. i pense the politique of that objectif made more in the mariage than the love of the parties. enobarbus. i pense so too. but you doit find the band that seems to tie leur friendship ensemble will be the very strangler of leur amity: octavia is of a holy, cold, and encore conversation. menas. who aurait not have his wife so? enobarbus. not he that himself is not so; lequel is mark antony. he will to his egyptian dish again; then doit the sighs of octavia blow the fire up in caesar, and, as i said before, that lequel is the force of leur amity doit prouver the immediate author of leur variance. antony will use his affection où it is; he married but his occasion here. menas. and thus it may be. come, sir, will you aboard? i have a santé for you. enobarbus. i doit take it, sir. we have us'd our throats in egypt. menas. come, let's away. sortir act_2|sc_7 scène vii. on board pompey's galley, off misenum la musique plays. entrer two or three servants with a banquet première servant. here they'll be, man. some o' leur plants are ill-rooted already; the moins wind i' th' monde will blow them down. seconde servant. lepidus is high-colour'd. première servant. they have made him boisson alms-drink. seconde servant. as they pinch one un autre by the disposition, he cries out 'no more!'; reconciles them to his entreaty and himself to th' drink. première servant. but it raises the greater war entre him and his discretion. seconde servant. why, this it is to have a name in génial men's fellowship. i had as lief have a reed that will do me no un service as a partizan i pourrait not heave. première servant. to be call'd into a huge sphere, and not to be seen to move in't, are the holes où eyes devrait be, lequel pitifully disaster the cheeks. a sennet sounded. entrer caesar, antony, lepidus, pompey, agrippa, maecenas, enobarbus, menas, with autre captains antony. [to caesar] thus do they, sir: they take the flow o' th' nile by certain scales i' th' pyramid; they know by th' height, the lowness, or the mean, if dearth or foison follow. the higher nilus swells the more it promises; as it ebbs, the seedsman upon the slime and ooze scatters his grain, and prochainement vient to harvest. lepidus. y'have étrange serpents there. antony. ay, lepidus. lepidus. your serpent of Egypte is bred now of your mud by the operation of your sun; so is your crocodile. antony. they are so. pompey. sit- and some wine! a santé to lepidus! lepidus. i am not so well as i devrait be, but i'll ne'er out. enobarbus. not till you have slept. i fear me you'll be in till then. lepidus. nay, certainly, i have entendu the ptolemies' pyramises are very goodly things. sans pour autant contradiction i have entendu that. menas. [aside to pompey] pompey, a word. pompey. [aside to menas] say in mine ear; what is't? menas. [aside to pompey] forsake thy seat, i do beseech thee, captain, and hear me parler a word. pompey. [ whispers in's ear ] ancêtre me till anon- this wine for lepidus! lepidus. what manière o' chose is your crocodile? antony. it is shap'd, sir, like itself, and it is as broad as it hath breadth; it is just so high as it is, and moves with it own organs. it vies by that lequel nourisheth it, and the elements once out of it, it transmigrates. lepidus. what Couleur is it of? antony. of it own Couleur too. lepidus. 'tis a étrange serpent. antony. 'tis so. and the larmes of it are wet. caesar. will this description satisfy him? antony. with the santé that pompey gives him, else he is a very epicure. pompey. [rises and walks aside] the matter? menas. i have ever held my cap off to thy fortunes. pompey. thou hast serv'd me with much faith. what's else to say?- be jolly, lords. antony. celles-ci quicksands, lepidus, keep off them, for you sink. menas. wilt thou be lord of all the world? pompey. what say'st thou? menas. wilt thou be lord of the entier world? that's twice. pompey. how devrait that be? menas. but divertir it, and bien que you pense me poor, i am the man will give thee all the world. pompey. hast thou ivre well? menas. no, pompey, i have kept me from the cup. thou art, if thou dar'st be, the earthly jove; whate'er the ocean pales or sky inclips is thine, if thou wilt ha't. pompey. show me lequel way. menas. celles-ci three world-sharers, celles-ci competitors, are in thy vessel. let me cut the cable; and when we are put off, fall to leur throats. all Là is thine. pompey. ah, this thou shouldst have done, and not have parlait on't. in me 'tis villainy: in thee't had been good service. thou must know 'tis not my profit that does lead mine honour: mine honour, it. se repentir that e'er thy langue hath so betray'd thine act. étant done unknown, i devrait have a trouvé it ensuite well done, but must condemn it now. desist, and drink. menas. [aside] for this, i'll jamais suivre thy pall'd fortunes more. who seeks, and will not take when once 'tis offer'd, doit jamais find it more. pompey. this santé to lepidus! antony. bear him ashore. i'll pledge it for him, pompey. enobarbus. here's to thee, menas! menas. enobarbus, welcome! pompey. fill till the cup be hid. enobarbus. there's a fort fellow, menas. [pointing to the serviteur who carries off lepidus] menas. why? enobarbus. 'a ours the troisième part of the world, man; see'st not? menas. the troisième part, then, is drunk. aurait it were all, that it pourrait go on wheels! enobarbus. boisson thou; increase the reels. menas. come. pompey. this is not yet an alexandrian feast. antony. it ripens towards it. la grève the vessels, ho! here's to caesar! caesar. i pourrait well forbear't. it's monstrous la main d'oeuvre when i wash my cerveau and it grows fouler. antony. be a enfant o' th' time. caesar. possess it, i'll make answer. but i had plutôt fast from all four days than boisson so much in one. enobarbus. [to antony] ha, my courageux emperor! doit we Danse now the egyptian bacchanals and celebrate our drink? pompey. let's ha't, good soldier. antony. come, let's all take hands, till that the conquering wine hath steep'd our sens in soft and delicate lethe. enobarbus. all take hands. make battery to our ears with the loud music, the tandis que i'll endroit you; then the boy doit sing; the holding chaque man doit bear as loud as his fort sides can volley. [music plays. énobarbus places them hand in hand] the song come, thou monarch of the vine, plumpy bacchus with pink eyne! in thy fats our se soucie be drown'd, with thy grapes our hairs be crown'd. cup us till the monde go round, cup us till the monde go round! caesar. what aurait you more? pompey, good night. good brother, let me demande you off; our graver Entreprise frowns at this levity. doux lords, let's part; you see we have burnt our cheeks. fort enobarb is weaker than the wine, and mine own langue splits what it speaks. the wild disguise hath presque antick'd us all. what Besoins more words? good night. good antony, your hand. pompey. i'll try you on the shore. antony. and shall, sir. give's your hand. pompey. o antony, you have my father's house- but what? we are friends. come, down into the boat. enobarbus. take heed you fall not. sortir all but énobarbus and menas menas, i'll not on shore. menas. no, to my cabin. celles-ci drums! celles-ci trumpets, flutes! what! let neptune hear we bid a loud adieu to celles-ci génial fellows. du son and be hang'd, du son out! [sound a flourish, with drums] enobarbus. hoo! says 'a. there's my cap. menas. hoo! noble captain, come. sortir act_3|sc_1 act iii. scène i. a plaine in syria entrer ventidius, as it were in triumph, with silius and autre romans, officers and soldiers; the dead body of pacorus supporté avant him ventidius. now, darting parthia, art thou struck, and now pleas'd fortune does of Marcus crassus' décès make me revenger. bear the king's son's body avant our army. thy pacorus, orodes, pays this for Marcus crassus. silius. noble ventidius, whilst yet with parthian du sang thy épée is warm the fugitive parthians follow; spur par media, mesopotamia, and the shelters où the routed fly. so thy grand captain, antony, doit set thee on triumphant chariots and put garlands on thy head. ventidius. o silius, silius, i have done enough. a lower place, note well, may make too génial an act; for apprendre this, silius: mieux to laisser défait than by our deed acquire too high a fame when him we serve's away. caesar and antony have ever won more in leur officer, than person. sossius, one of my endroit in syria, his lieutenant, for rapide accumulation of renown, lequel he achiev'd by th' minute, lost his favour. who does i' th' wars more than his capitaine can becomes his captain's captain; and ambition, the soldier's virtue, plutôt fait du choix of loss than gain lequel darkens him. i pourrait do more to do antonius good, but 'twould offenser him; and in his infraction devrait my performance perish. silius. thou hast, ventidius, that sans pour autant the lequel a soldat and his épée grants rare distinction. thou wilt écrire to antony? ventidius. i'll humbly signify what in his name, that magical word of war, we have effected; how, with his banners, and his well-paid ranks, the ne'er-yet-beaten cheval of parthia we have jaded out o' th' field. silius. où is he now? ventidius. he purposeth to athens; whither, with what hâte the poids we must convey with's will permit, we doit apparaître avant him.- on, there; pass along. sortir act_3|sc_2 scène ii. rome. caesar's maison entrer agrippa at one door, énobarbus at un autre agrippa. what, are the brothers parted? enobarbus. they have dispatch'd with pompey; he is gone; the autre three are sealing. octavia weeps to part from rome; caesar is sad; and lepidus, depuis pompey's feast, as menas says, is troubled with the vert sickness. agrippa. 'tis a noble lepidus. enobarbus. a very fine one. o, how he aime caesar! agrippa. nay, but how chèrement he adores mark antony! enobarbus. caesar? why he's the jupiter of men. agrippa. what's antony? the god of jupiter. enobarbus. spake you of caesar? how! the nonpareil! agrippa. o, antony! o thou arabian bird! enobarbus. aurait you louange caesar, say 'caesar'- go no further. agrippa. indeed, he plied them both with excellent praises. enobarbus. but he aime caesar best. yet he aime antony. hoo! hearts, tongues, figures, scribes, bards, poets, ne peux pas think, speak, cast, write, sing, number- hoo!- his love to antony. but as for caesar, s'agenouiller down, s'agenouiller down, and wonder. agrippa. both he loves. enobarbus. they are his shards, and he leur beetle. [trumpets within] so- this is to horse. adieu, noble agrippa. agrippa. good fortune, worthy soldier, and farewell. entrer caesar, antony, lepidus, and octavia antony. no further, sir. caesar. you take from me a génial part of myself; use me well in't. sister, prouver such a wife as my thoughts make thee, and as my farthest band doit pass on thy approof. most noble antony, let not the pièce of vertu lequel is set betwixt us as the cement of our love to keep it builded be the ram to batter the fortress of it; for mieux pourrait we have lov'd sans pour autant this mean, if on both les pièces this be not cherish'd. antony. make me not offended in your distrust. caesar. i have said. antony. you doit not find, bien que you be la bride curious, the moins cause for what you seem to fear. so the gods keep you, and make the hearts of romans servir your ends! we will here part. caesar. farewell, my très cher sister, fare thee well. the elements be kind to thee and make thy spirits all of comfort! fare thee well. octavia. my noble brother! antony. the april's in her eyes. it is love's spring, and celles-ci the showers to apporter it on. be cheerful. octavia. sir, look well to my husband's house; and- caesar. what, octavia? octavia. i'll tell you in your ear. antony. her langue will not obey her heart, nor can her cœur inform her tongue- the swan's down feather, that stands upon the swell at the full of tide, and ni way inclines. enobarbus. [aside to agrippa] will caesar weep? agrippa. [aside to enobarbus] he has a cloud in's face. enobarbus. [aside to agrippa] he were the pire for that, were he a horse; so is he, étant a man. agrippa. [kisses octavia] antony. farewell! trumpets sound. sortir act_3|sc_3 scène iii. alexandria. cleopatra's palais entrer cleopatra, charmian, iras, and alexas cleopatra. où is the fellow? alexas. half afeard to come. cleopatra. go to, go to. entrer the Messager as avant come hither, sir. alexas. good majesty, herod of jewry dare not look upon you but when you are well pleas'd. cleopatra. that herod's head i'll have. but how, when antony is gone, par whom i pourrait commander it? come thou near. messenger. most gracious majesty! cleopatra. didst thou voir octavia? messenger. ay, crainte queen. cleopatra. where? messenger. madam, in rome i look'd her in the face, and saw her led entre her frère and mark antony. cleopatra. is she as tall as me? messenger. she is not, madam. cleopatra. didst hear her speak? is she shrill-tongu'd or low? messenger. madam, i entendu her speak: she is low-voic'd. cleopatra. that's not so good. he ne peux pas like her long. charmian. like her? o isis! 'tis impossible. cleopatra. i pense so, charmian. dull of langue and dwarfish! what majesté is in her gait? remember, if e'er thou look'dst on majesty. messenger. she creeps. her mouvement and her station are as one; she montre a body plutôt than a life, a statue than a breather. cleopatra. is this certain? messenger. or i have no observance. charmian. three in Egypte ne peux pas make mieux note. cleopatra. he's very knowing; i do perceive't. there's rien in her yet. the compagnon has good judgment. charmian. excellent. cleopatra. devine at her years, i prithee. messenger. madam, she was a widow. cleopatra. widow? charmian, hark! 'twill be naught; but let it be. apporter me to antony. eros. come, sir. sortir act_3|sc_6 scène vi. rome. caesar's maison entrer caesar, agrippa, and maecenas caesar. contemning rome, he has done all this and more in alexandria. here's the manière of't: i' th' market-place, on a tribunal silver'd, cleopatra and himself in chairs of gold were publicly enthron'd; at the feet sat caesarion, whom they call my father's son, and all the unlawful problème that leur lust depuis then hath made entre them. unto her he gave the stablishment of egypt; made her of lower syria, cyprus, lydia, absolute queen. maecenas. this in the Publique eye? caesar. i' th' commun show-place, où they exercise. his sons he Là proclaim'd the rois of kings: génial media, parthia, and armenia, he gave to alexander; to ptolemy he assign'd syria, cilicia, and phoenicia. she in th' habiliments of the goddess isis that day appear'd; and oft avant gave audience, as 'tis reported, so. maecenas. let rome be thus inform'd. agrippa. who, queasy with his insolence already, will leur good thoughts call from him. caesar. the gens sait it, and have now receiv'd his accusations. agrippa. who does he accuse? caesar. caesar; and that, ayant in sicily sextus pompeius spoil'd, we had not rated him his part o' th' isle. then does he say he lent me some shipping, unrestor'd. lastly, he frets that lepidus of the triumvirate devrait be depos'd; and, being, that we detain all his revenue. agrippa. sir, this devrait be answer'd. caesar. 'tis done already, and Messager gone. i have told him lepidus was grandi too cruel, that he his high autorité abus'd, and did mériter his change. for what i have conquer'd i subvention him part; but then, in his armenia and autre of his conquer'd kingdoms, demande the like. maecenas. he'll jamais rendement to that. caesar. nor must not then be yielded to in this. entrer octavia, with her train octavia. hail, caesar, and my lord! hail, most dear caesar! caesar. that ever i devrait call thee cast-away! octavia. you have not call'd me so, nor have you cause. caesar. why have you stol'n upon us thus? you come not like caesar's sister. the wife of antony devrait have an army for an usher, and the neighs of cheval to tell of her approche long ere she did appear. the trees by th' way devrait have supporté men, and expectation fainted, longing for what it had not. nay, the dust devrait have ascended to the roof of heaven, rais'd by your populous troops. but you are come a market-maid to rome, and have prevented the ostentation of our love, lequel left unshown is souvent left unlov'd. we devrait have met you by sea and land, supplying chaque stage with an augmented greeting. octavia. good my lord, to come thus was i not constrain'd, but did it on my free will. my lord, mark antony, hearing that you prepar'd for war, connaissance my grieved ear withal; whereon i begg'd his pardon for return. caesar. lequel soon he granted, étant an obstruct 'tween his lust and him. octavia. do not say so, my lord. caesar. i have eyes upon him, and his affaires come to me on the wind. où is he now? Bienvenue hither. your letters did withhold our breaking forth, till we perceiv'd both how you were faux led and we in negligent danger. acclamation your heart; be you not troubled with the time, lequel drives o'er your contenu celles-ci fort necessities, but let determin'd things to destiny hold unbewail'd leur way. Bienvenue to rome; rien more dear to me. you are abus'd au-delà the mark of thought, and the high gods, to do you justice, make leur ministers of us and ceux that love you. best of comfort, and ever Bienvenue to us. agrippa. welcome, lady. maecenas. welcome, dear madam. each cœur in rome does love and pity you; only th' adulterous antony, most grand in his abominations, se tourne you off, and gives his potent regiment to a trull that noises it against us. octavia. is it so, sir? caesar. most certain. sister, welcome. pray you be ever connu to patience. my dear'st sister! sortir act_3|sc_7 scène vii. antony's camp near actium entrer cleopatra and énobarbus cleopatra. i will be even with thee, doute it not. enobarbus. but why, why, cleopatra. thou hast forspoke my étant in celles-ci wars, and say'st it is not fit. enobarbus. well, is it, is it? cleopatra. is't not denounc'd against us? why devrait not we be Là in person? enobarbus. antony. o, fie, fie, fie! charmian. madam! iras. madam, o good empress! eros. sir, sir! antony. yes, my lord, yes. he at philippi kept his épée e'en like a dancer, tandis que i frappé the lean and wrinkled cassius; and 'twas i that the mad brutus ended; he seul dealt on lieutenantry, and no entraine toi had in the courageux squares of war. yet now- no matter. cleopatra. ah, supporter by! eros. the queen, my lord, the queen! iras. go to him, madam, parler to him. he is unqualitied with very shame. cleopatra. well then, sustain me. o! eros. most noble sir, arise; the reine approaches. her head's declin'd, and décès will seize her but your confort fait du the rescue. antony. i have offended reputation- a most unnoble swerving. eros. sir, the queen. antony. o, où hast thou led me, egypt? love, i am full of lead. some wine, dans there, and our viands! fortune sait we mépris her most when most she offers blows. sortir act_3|sc_12 scène xii. caesar's camp in Egypte entrer caesar, agrippa, dolabella, thyreus, with autres caesar. let him apparaître that's come from antony. know you him? dolabella. caesar, 'tis his schoolmaster: an argument that he is pluck'd, when hither he sends so poor a pinion of his wing, lequel had superfluous rois for messengers not many moons gone by. entrer euphronius, ambassador from antony caesar. approach, and speak. euphronius. such as i am, i come from antony. i was of late as petty to his ends as is the morn-dew on the myrtle leaf to his grand sea. caesar. be't so. declare thine office. euphronius. lord of his fortunes he salutes thee, and requires to live in egypt; lequel not granted, he lessens his requests and to thee sues to let him breathe entre the heavens and earth, a privé man in athens. this for him. next, cleopatra does avouer thy greatness, submits her to thy might, and of thee craves the circle of the ptolemies for her heirs, now hazarded to thy grace. caesar. for antony, i have no ears to his request. the reine of audience nor le désir doit fail, so she from Egypte drive her all-disgraced friend, or take his life there. this if she perform, she doit not sue unheard. so to them both. euphronius. fortune pursue thee! caesar. apporter him par the bands. exit euphronius [to thyreus] to try thy eloquence, now 'tis time. dispatch; from antony win cleopatra. promise, and in our name, what she requires; add more, from thine invention, offers. women are not in leur best fortunes strong; but want will perjure the ne'er-touch'd vestal. try thy cunning, thyreus; make thine own edict for thy pains, lequel we will répondre as a law. thyreus. caesar, i go. caesar. observe how antony becomes his flaw, and what thou think'st his very action parle in chaque Puissance that moves. thyreus. caesar, i shall. sortir act_3|sc_13 scène xiii. alexandria. cleopatra's palais entrer cleopatra, enobarbus, charmian, and iras cleopatra. what doit we do, enobarbus? [cleopatpa kneels] caesar. arise, you doit not kneel. i pray you, rise; rise, egypt. cleopatra. sir, the gods will have it thus; my Maître and my lord i must obey. caesar. take to you no hard thoughts. the record of what injuries you did us, bien que écrit in our flesh, we doit rappelles toi as things but done by chance. cleopatra. sole sir o' th' world, i ne peux pas projet mine own cause so well to make it clear, but do avouer i have been laden with like frailties lequel avant have souvent sham'd our sex. caesar. cleopatra, know we will extenuate plutôt than enforce. if you apply toi même to our intents- lequel towards you are most gentle- you doit find a avantage in this change; but if you seek to lay on me a cruelty by taking antony's course, you doit bereave toi même of my good purposes, and put your children to that destruction lequel i'll garde them from, if thereon you rely. i'll take my leave. cleopatra. and may, par all the world. 'tis yours, and we, your scutcheons and your signs of conquest, doit hang in what endroit you please. here, my good lord. caesar. you doit advise me in all for cleopatra. cleopatra. this is the bref of money, plate, and jewels, i am possess'd of. 'tis exactly valued, not petty things admitted. where's seleucus? seleucus. here, madam. cleopatra. this is my treasurer; let him speak, my lord, upon his peril, that i have reserv'd to moi même nothing. parler the truth, seleucus. seleucus. madam, i had plutôt seal my lips than to my péril parler that lequel is not. cleopatra. what have i kept back? seleucus. assez to purchase what you have made known. caesar. nay, rougir not, cleopatra; i approve your sagesse in the deed. cleopatra. see, caesar! o, behold, how pomp is followed! mine will now be yours; and, devrait we shift estates, le tiens aurait be mine. the ingratitude of this seleucus does even make me wild. o slave, of no more confiance than love that's hir'd! what, goest thou back? thou shalt go back, i mandat thee; but i'll capture thine eyes bien que they had wings. slave, soulless villain, dog! o rarely base! caesar. good queen, let us supplier you. cleopatra. o caesar, what a wounding la honte is this, that thou vouchsafing here to visite me, Faire the honour of thy lordliness to one so meek, that mine own serviteur devrait parcel the sum of my disgraces by addition of his envy! say, good caesar, that i some lady trifles have reserv'd, immoment toys, things of such dignity as we saluer modern friends withal; and say some nobler token i have kept apart for livia and octavia, to induce leur mediation- must i be unfolded with one that i have bred? the gods! it smites me beneath the fall i have. [to seleucus] prithee go hence; or i doit show the cinders of my spirits par th' ashes of my chance. wert thou a man, thou wouldst have pitié on me. caesar. forbear, seleucus. exit seleucus cleopatra. be it connu that we, the greatest, are misthought for things that autres do; and when we fall we répondre others' merits in our name, are par conséquent to be pitied. caesar. cleopatra, not what you have reserv'd, nor what acknowledg'd, put we i' th' roll of conquest. encore be't yours, bestow it at your pleasure; and croyez caesar's no merchant, to make prix with you of things that merchants sold. par conséquent be cheer'd; make not your thoughts your prisons. no, dear queen; for we avoir l'intention so to dispose you as toi même doit give us counsel. feed and sleep. our care and pity is so much upon you that we rester your friend; and so, adieu. cleopatra. my Maître and my lord! caesar. not so. adieu. flourish. sortir caesar and his train cleopatra. he words me, girls, he words me, that i devrait not be noble to myself. but hark thee, charmian! [whispers charmian] iras. finish, good lady; the brillant day is done, and we are for the dark. cleopatra. hie thee again. i have parlait already, and it is provided; go put it to the haste. charmian. madam, i will. re-enter Dolabella dolabella. where's the queen? charmian. behold, sir. exit cleopatra. dolabella! dolabella. madam, as thereto juré by your command, lequel my love fait du religion to obey, i tell you this: caesar par syria intends his journey, and dans three days you with your children will he send before. make your best use of this; i have perform'd your plaisir and my promise. cleopatra. dolabella, i doit rester your debtor. dolabella. i your servant. adieu, good queen; i must assister on caesar. cleopatra. farewell, and thanks. exit Dolabella now, iras, what think'st thou? thou an egyptian puppet doit be shown in rome as well as i. mechanic slaves, with greasy aprons, rules, and hammers, doit uplift us to the view; in leur thick breaths, rank of brut diet, doit we be enclouded, and forc'd to boisson leur vapour. iras. the gods forbid! cleopatra. nay, 'tis most certain, iras. saucy lictors will capture at us like strumpets, and scald rhymers ballad us out o' tune; the rapide comedians extemporally will stage us, and présent our alexandrian revels; antony doit be apporté drunken forth, and i doit see some squeaking cleopatra boy my greatness i' th' posture of a whore. iras. o the good gods! cleopatra. nay, that's certain. iras. i'll jamais see't, for i am sure mine nails are stronger than mine eyes. cleopatra. why, that's the way to fool leur preparation and to conquer leur most absurd intents. entrer charmian now, charmian! show me, my women, like a queen. go chercher my best attires. i am encore for cydnus, to meet mark antony. sirrah, iras, go. now, noble charmian, we'll envoi indeed; and when thou hast done this chare, i'll give thee laisser to play till doomsday. apporter our couronne and all. exit iras. a bruit dans wherefore's this noise? entrer a guardsman guardsman. here is a rural compagnon that will not be refusé your highness' presence. he brings you figs. cleopatra. let him come in. exit guardsman what poor an instrument may do a noble deed! he brings me liberty. my resolution's plac'd, and i have rien of femme in me. now from head to foot i am marble-constant; now the fleeting moon no planet is of mine. re-enter guardsman and clown, with a basket guardsman. this is the man. cleopatra. avoid, and laisser him. exit guardsman hast thou the jolie worm of nilus Là that kills and des douleurs not? clown. truly, i have him. but i aurait not be the fête that devrait le désir you to toucher him, for his biting is immortal; ceux that do die of it do seldom or jamais recover. cleopatra. remember'st thou any that have died on't? clown. very many, men and women too. i entendu of one of them no plus long than yesterday: a very honnête woman, but quelque chose donné to lie, as a femme devrait not do but in the way of honesty; how she died of the biting of it, what pain she felt- vraiment she fait du a very good rapport o' th' worm. but he that will croyez all that they say doit jamais be saved by half that they do. but this is most falliable, the worm's an odd worm. cleopatra. get thee hence; farewell. clown. i wish you all joy of the worm. [sets down the basket] cleopatra. farewell. clown. you must pense this, look you, that the worm will do his kind. cleopatra. ay, ay; farewell. clown. look you, the worm is not to be trusted but in the keeping of wise people; for En effet Là is no la bonté in the worm. cleopatra. take thou no care; it doit be heeded. clown. very good. give it nothing, i pray you, for it is not vaut the feeding. cleopatra. will it eat me? clown. you must not pense i am so Facile but i know the diable himself will not eat a woman. i know that a femme is a dish for the gods, if the diable dress her not. but truly, celles-ci same whoreson devils do the gods génial harm in leur women, for in chaque ten that they make the devils mar five. cleopatra. well, get thee gone; farewell. clown. yes, forsooth. i wish you joy o' th' worm. exit re-enter iras, with a robe, crown, &c. cleopatra. give me my robe, put on my crown; i have immortal longings in me. now no more the juice of egypt's grape doit moist this lip. yare, yare, good iras; quick. methinks i hear antony call. i see him rouse himself to louange my noble act. i hear him mock the luck of caesar, lequel the gods give men to excuse leur après wrath. husband, i come. now to that name my courage prouver my title! i am fire and air; my autre elements i give to baser life. so, have you done? come then, and take the last warmth of my lips. farewell, kind charmian. iras, long farewell. [kisses them. iras des chutes and dies] have i the aspic in my lips? dost fall? if thus thou and la nature can so gently part, the accident vasculaire cérébral of décès is as a lover's pinch, lequel hurts and is desir'd. dost thou lie still? if thou vanishest, thou tell'st the monde it is not vaut leave-taking. charmian. dissolve, thick cloud, and rain, that i may say the gods se do weep. cleopatra. this proves me base. if she première meet the curled antony, he'll make demande of her, and dépenser that kiss lequel is my paradis to have. come, thou mortel wretch, [to an asp, lequel she applies to her breast] with thy tranchant les dents this knot intrinsicate of life at once untie. poor venomous fool, be angry and dispatch. o couldst thou speak, that i pourrait hear thee call génial caesar ass unpolicied! charmian. o eastern star! cleopatra. peace, peace! dost thou not see my baby at my Sein that sucks the infirmière asleep? charmian. o, break! o, break! cleopatra. as sucré as balm, as soft as air, as gentle- o antony! nay, i will take thee too: [applying un autre asp to her arm] what devrait i stay- [dies] charmian. in this vile world? so, fare thee well. now boast thee, death, in thy possession lies a lass unparallel'd. downy windows, close; and d'or phoebus jamais be beheld of eyes encore so royal! your crown's awry; i'll mend it and then play- entrer the guard, rushing in première guard. where's the queen? charmian. parler softly, wake her not. première guard. caesar hath sent- charmian. too slow a messenger. [applies an asp] o, come apace, dispatch. i partiellement feel thee. première guard. approach, ho! all's not well: caesar's beguil'd. seconde guard. there's Dolabella sent from caesar; call him. première guard. what work is here! charmian, is this well done? charmian. it is well done, and fitting for a princes descended of so many Royal kings. ah, soldier! [charmian dies] re-enter Dolabella dolabella. how goes it here? seconde guard. all dead. dolabella. caesar, thy thoughts toucher leur effects in this. thyself art venir to see perform'd the dreaded act lequel thou so sought'st to hinder. [within: 'a way there, a way for caesar!'] re-enter caesar and all his train dolabella. o sir, you are too sure an augurer: that you did fear is done. caesar. bravest at the last, she levell'd at our purposes, and étant royal, took her own way. the manière of leur deaths? i do not see them bleed. dolabella. who was last with them? première guard. a Facile countryman that apporté her figs. this was his basket. caesar. poison'd then. première guard. o caesar, this charmian liv'd but now; she se tenait and spake. i a trouvé her trimming up the diadem on her dead mistress. tremblingly she stood, and on the soudain dropp'd. caesar. o noble weakness! if they had swallow'd poison 'twould apparaître by external swelling; but she regards like sleep, as she aurait capture un autre antony in her fort toil of grace. dolabella. here on her Sein Là is a vent of blood, and quelque chose blown; the like is on her arm. première guard. this is an aspic's trail; and celles-ci fig-leaves have slime upon them, such as th' aspic leaves upon the caves of nile. caesar. most probable that so she died; for her physician raconte me she hath pursu'd conclusions infini of easy ways to die. take up her bed, and bear her women from the monument. she doit be enterré by her antony; no la tombe upon the Terre doit clip in it a pair so famous. high events as celles-ci la grève ceux that make them; and leur récit is no less in pity than his gloire lequel apporté them to be lamented. our army doit in solennel show assister this funeral, and then to rome. come, dolabella, see high ordre in this génial solemnity. sortir the end <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext frederick's court; and the forêt of arden act i. scène i. orchard of oliver's maison entrer orlando and adam orlando. as i remember, adam, it was upon this mode bequeathed me by will but poor a thousand crowns, and, as thou say'st, charged my brother, on his blessing, to race me well; and Là begins my sadness. my frère jaques he garde at school, and rapport parle goldenly of his profit. for
