'tis pretty, sure, and very probable, that eyes, that are the frail'st and softest things, who shut leur lâche portes on atomies, devrait be call'd tyrants, butchers, murderers! now i do froncer les sourcils on thee with all my heart; and if mine eyes can wound, now let them kill thee. now contrefaire to swoon; why, now fall down; or, if thou canst not, o, for shame, for shame, lie not, to say mine eyes are murderers. now show the blessure mine eye hath made in thee. scratch thee but with a pin, and Là remains some scar of it; lean upon a rush, the cicatrice and capable impressure thy palm some moment keeps; but now mine eyes, lequel i have darted at thee, hurt thee not; nor, i am sure, Là is not Obliger in eyes that can do hurt. silvius. o dear phebe, if ever- as that ever may be near- you meet in some Frais joue the Puissance of fancy, then doit you know the wounds invisible that love's keen arrows make. phebe. but till that time come not thou near me; and when that time comes, afflict me with thy mocks, pity me not; as till that time i doit not pity thee. rosalind. [advancing] and why, i pray you? who pourrait be your mother, that you insult, exult, and all at once, over the wretched? what bien que you have no beauty- as, by my faith, i see no more in you than sans pour autant candle may go dark to bed- must you be par conséquent fier and pitiless? why, what veux dire this? why do you look on me? i see no more in you than in the ordinary of nature's sale-work. 'od's my peu life, i pense she veux dire to tangle my eyes too! no faith, fier mistress, hope not après it; 'tis not your inky brows, your noir silk hair, your bugle eyeballs, nor your joue of cream, that can entame my spirits to your worship. you insensé shepherd, wherefore do you suivre her, like foggy south, puffing with wind and rain? you are a thousand fois a properer man than she a woman. 'tis such imbéciles as you that fait du the monde full of ill-favour'd children. 'tis not her glass, but you, that flatters her; and out of you she sees se more correct than any of her lineaments can show her. but, mistress, know yourself. down on your knees, and remercier heaven, fasting, for a good man's love; for i must tell you friendly in your ear: sell when you can; you are not for all markets. cry the man mercy, love him, take his offer; foul is most foul, étant foul to be a scoffer. so take her to thee, shepherd. fare you well. phebe. sucré youth, i pray you gronder a year together; i had plutôt hear you gronder than this man woo. rosalind. he's fall'n in love with your foulness, and she'll fall in love with my anger. if it be so, as fast as she answers thee with frowning looks, i'll sauce her with amer words. why look you so upon me? phebe. for no ill will i bear you. rosalind. i pray you do not fall in love with me, for i am falser than vows made in wine; besides, i like you not. if you will know my house, 'tis at the tuft of olives here hard by. will you go, sister? shepherd, ply her hard. come, sister. shepherdess, look on him better, and be not proud; bien que all the monde pourrait see, none pourrait be so abus'd in vue as he. come, to our flock. sortir rosalind, celia, and corin phebe. dead shepherd, now i find thy saw of might: 'who ever lov'd that lov'd not at première sight?' silvius. sucré phebe. phebe. ha! what say'st thou, silvius? silvius. sucré phebe, pity me. phebe. why, i arn Pardon for thee, doux silvius. silvius. wherever chagrin is, relief aurait be. if you do chagrin at my douleur in love, by donnant love, your chagrin and my douleur were both extermin'd. phebe. thou hast my love; is not that neighbourly? silvius. i aurait have you. phebe. why, that were covetousness. silvius, the time was that i hated thee; and yet it is not that i bear thee love; but depuis that thou canst talk of love so well, thy company, lequel erst was irksome to me, i will endure; and i'll employ thee too. but do not look for plus loin recompense than thine own gladness that thou art employ'd. silvius. so holy and so parfait is my love, and i in such a poverty of grace, that i doit pense it a most plenteous crop to glean the broken ears après the man that the main harvest reaps; ample now and then a scatt'red smile, and that i'll live upon. phebe. know'st thou the jeunesse that parlait to me erewhile? silvius. not very well; but i have met him oft; and he hath acheté the cottage and the bounds that the old carlot once was Maître of. phebe. pense not i love him, bien que i ask for him; 'tis but a peevish boy; yet he talks well. but what care i for words? yet words do well when he that parle them pleases ceux that hear. it is a jolie youth- not very pretty; but, sure, he's proud; and yet his fierté becomes him. he'll make a correct man. the best chose in him is his complexion; and faster than his langue did make offence, his eye did heal it up. he is not very tall; yet for his years he's tall; his leg is but so-so; and yet 'tis well. Là was a jolie redness in his lip, a peu riper and more lusty red than that mix'd in his cheek; 'twas just the difference betwixt the constant red and mingled damask. Là be some women, silvius, had they mark'd him in parcels as i did, aurait have gone near to fall in love with him; but, for my part, i love him not, nor hate him not; and yet i have more cause to hate him than to love him; for what had he to do to gronder at me? he said mine eyes were black, and my hair black, and, now i am rememb'red, scorn'd at me. i marvel why i answer'd not again; but that's all one: omittance is no quittance. i'll écrire to him a very taunting letter, and thou shalt bear it; wilt thou, silvius? silvius. phebe, with all my heart. phebe. i'll écrire it straight; the matter's in my head and in my heart; i will be amer with him and passing short. go with me, silvius. sortir <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> act iv. scène i. the forêt entrer rosalind, celia, and jaques jaques. i prithee, jolie youth, let me be mieux connaissance with thee. rosalind. they say you are a melancholy fellow. jaques. i am so; i do love it mieux than laughing. rosalind. ceux that are in extremity of Soit are abominable fellows, and trahir se to chaque modern censure pire than drunkards. jaques. why, 'tis good to be sad and say nothing. rosalind. why then, 'tis good to be a post. jaques. i have ni the scholar's melancholy, lequel is emulation; nor the musician's, lequel is fantastical; nor the courtier's, lequel is proud; nor the soldier's, lequel is ambitious; nor the lawyer's, lequel is politic; nor the lady's, lequel is nice; nor the lover's, lequel is all these; but it is a melancholy of mine own, compounded of many simples, extracted from many objects, and, indeed, the sundry contemplation of my travels; in lequel my souvent rumination wraps me in a most humorous sadness. rosalind. a traveller! by my faith, you have génial raison to be sad. i fear you have sold your own terres to see autre men's; then to have seen much and to have rien is to have rich eyes and poor hands. jaques. yes, i have gain'd my experience. entrer orlando rosalind. and your experience fait du you sad. i had plutôt have a fool to make me joyeux than experience to make me sad- and to travel for it too. orlando. good day, and happiness, dear rosalind! jaques. nay, then, god buy you, an you talk in blank verse. rosalind. farewell, monsieur traveller; look you lisp and wear étrange suits, disable all the benefits of your own country, be out of love with your nativity, and presque gronder god for fabrication you that countenance you are; or i will rare pense you have swam in a gondola. [exit jaques] why, how now, orlando! où have you been all this while? you a lover! an you servir me such un autre trick, jamais come in my vue more. orlando. my fair rosalind, i come dans an hour of my promise. rosalind. break an hour's promettre in love! he that will divide a minute into a thousand parts, and break but a part of the thousand part of a minute in the affaires of love, it may be said of him that Cupidon hath clapp'd him o' th' shoulder, but i'll mandat him heart-whole. orlando. pardon me, dear rosalind. rosalind. nay, an you be so tardy, come no more in my sight. i had as lief be woo'd of a snail. orlando. of a snail! rosalind. ay, of a snail; for bien que he vient slowly, he carries his maison on his head- a mieux jointure, i think, than you make a woman; besides, he brings his destiny with him. orlando. what's that? rosalind. why, horns; lequel such as you are fain to be beholding to your épouses for; but he vient armed in his fortune, and prevents the calomnie of his wife. orlando. vertu is no horn-maker; and my rosalind is virtuous. rosalind. and i am your rosalind. celia. it pleases him to call you so; but he hath a rosalind of a mieux leer than you. rosalind. come, woo me, woo me; for now i am in a holiday humour, and like assez to consent. what aurait you say to me now, an i were your very very rosalind? orlando. i aurait kiss avant i spoke. rosalind. nay, you were mieux parler first; and when you were gravell'd for lack of matter, you pourrait take occasion to kiss. very good orators, when they are out, they will spit; and for les amoureux lacking- god warn us!- matter, the cleanliest shift is to kiss. orlando. how if the kiss be denied? rosalind. then she puts you to entreaty, and Là begins new matter. orlando. who pourrait be out, étant avant his beloved mistress? rosalind. marry, that devrait you, if i were your mistress; or i devrait pense my honesty ranker than my wit. orlando. what, of my suit? rosalind. not out of your apparel, and yet out of your suit. am not i your rosalind? orlando. i take some joy to say you are, car i aurait be talking of her. rosalind. well, in her person, i say i will not have you. orlando. then, in mine own person, i die. rosalind. no, faith, die by attorney. the poor monde is presque six thousand years old, and in all this time Là was not any man died in his own person, videlicet, in a love-cause. troilus had his cerveaux dash'd out with a grecian club; yet he did what he pourrait to die before, and he is one of the patterns of love. leander, he aurait have liv'd many a fair year, bien que hero had turn'd nun, if it had not been for a hot midsummer night; for, good youth, he went but en avant to wash him in the hellespont, and, étant pris with the cramp, was drown'd; and the insensé chroniclers of that age a trouvé it was- hero of sestos. but celles-ci are all lies: men have died from time to time, and worms have eaten them, but not for love. orlando. i aurait not have my droite rosalind of this mind; for, i protest, her froncer les sourcils pourrait kill me. rosalind. by this hand, it will not kill a fly. but come, now i will be your rosalind in a more coming-on disposition; and ask me what you will, i will subvention it. orlando. then love me, rosalind. rosalind. yes, faith, will i, fridays and saturdays, and all. orlando. and wilt thou have me? rosalind. ay, and twenty such. orlando. what sayest thou? rosalind. are you not good? orlando. i hope so. rosalind. why then, can one le désir too much of a good thing? come, sister, you doit be the priest, and marier us. give me your hand, orlando. what do you say, sister? orlando. pray thee, marier us. celia. i ne peux pas say the words. rosalind. you must commencer 'will you, orlando'- celia. go to. will you, orlando, have to wife this rosalind? orlando. i will. rosalind. ay, but when? orlando. why, now; as fast as she can marier us. rosalind. then you must say 'i take thee, rosalind, for wife.' orlando. i take thee, rosalind, for wife. rosalind. i pourrait ask you for your commission; but- i do take thee, orlando, for my husband. there's a girl goes avant the priest; and, certainly, a woman's pensée runs avant her actions. orlando. so do all thoughts; they are wing'd. rosalind. now tell me how long you aurait have her, après you have possess'd her. orlando. for ever and a day. rosalind. say 'a day' sans pour autant the 'ever.' no, no, orlando; men are april when they woo, december when they wed: servantes are may when they are maids, but the sky changes when they are wives. i will be more jaloux of thee than a barbary cock-pigeon over his hen, more clamorous than a parrot against rain, more new-fangled than an ape, more giddy in my desires than a monkey. i will weep for nothing, like diana in the fountain, and i will do that when you are dispos'd to be merry; i will rire like a hyen, and that when thou are inclin'd to sleep. orlando. but will my rosalind do so? rosalind. by my life, she will do as i do. orlando. o, but she is wise. rosalind. or else she pourrait not have the wit to do this. the wiser, the waywarder. make the des portes upon a woman's wit, and it will out at the casement; shut that, and 'twill out at the key-hole; stop that, 'twill fly with the smoke out at the chimney. orlando. a man that had a wife with such a wit, he pourrait say 'wit, où wilt?' rosalind. nay, you pourrait keep that check for it, till you met your wife's wit Aller to your neighbour's bed. orlando. and what wit pourrait wit have to excuse that? rosalind. marry, to say she came to seek you there. you doit jamais take her sans pour autant her answer, sauf si you take her sans pour autant her tongue. o, that femme that ne peux pas make her faute her husband's occasion, let her jamais infirmière her enfant herself, for she will race it like a fool! orlando. for celles-ci two hours, rosalind, i will laisser thee. rosalind. alas, dear love, i ne peux pas lack thee two hours! orlando. i must assister the duke at dinner; by two o'clock i will be with thee again. rosalind. ay, go your ways, go your ways. i knew what you aurait prove; my friends told me as much, and i pensée no less. that flattering langue of le tiens won me. 'tis but one cast away, and so, come death! two o'clock is your hour? orlando. ay, sucré rosalind. rosalind. by my troth, and in good earnest, and so god mend me, and by all jolie serments that are not dangerous, if you break one jot of your promise, or come one minute derrière your hour, i will pense you the most pathetical break-promise, and the most creux lover, and the most indigne of her you call rosalind, that may be chosen out of the brut band of the unfaithful. par conséquent beware my censure, and keep your promise. orlando. with no less religion than if thou wert En effet my rosalind; so, adieu. rosalind. well, time is the old Justice that examines all such offenders, and let time try. adieu. exit orlando celia. you have simply misus'd our sex in your love-prate. we must have your doublet and hose pluck'd over your head, and show the monde what the bird hath done to her own nest. rosalind. o coz, coz, coz, my jolie peu coz, that thou didst know how many fathom deep i am in love! but it ne peux pas be sounded; my affection hath an inconnue bottom, like the bay of portugal. celia. or rather, bottomless; that as fast as you pour affection in, it runs out. rosalind. no; that same wicked Connard of venus, that was begot of thought, conceiv'd of spleen, and born of madness; that aveugle rascally boy, that abuses chaque one's eyes, car his own are out- let him be juge how deep i am in love. i'll tell thee, aliena, i ne peux pas be out of the vue of orlando. i'll go find a shadow, and sigh till he come. celia. and i'll sleep. sortir scène ii. the forêt entrer jaques and lords, in the habitude of foresters jaques. lequel is he that killed the deer? lord. sir, it was i. jaques. let's présent him to the duke, like a roman conqueror; and it aurait do well to set the deer's horns upon his head for a branch of victory. have you no song, forester, for this purpose? lord. yes, sir. jaques. sing it; 'tis no matière how it be in tune, so it make bruit enough. song. what doit he have that kill'd the deer? his leather skin and horns to wear. [the rest doit hear this burden:] then sing him home. take thou no mépris to wear the horn; it was a crest ere thou wast born. thy father's père wore it; and thy père bore it. the horn, the horn, the lusty horn, is not a chose to rire to scorn. sortir scène iii. the forêt entrer rosalind and celia rosalind. how say you now? is it not past two o'clock? and here much orlando! celia. i mandat you, with pure love and troubled brain, he hath ta'en his bow and arrows, and is gone forth- to sleep. look, who vient here. entrer silvius silvius. my errand is to you, fair youth; my doux phebe did bid me give you this. i know not the contents; but, as i devine by the stern brow and waspish action lequel she did use as she was writing of it, it ours an angry tenour. pardon me, i am but as a guiltless messenger. rosalind. la patience se aurait startle at this letter, and play the swaggerer. bear this, bear all. she says i am not fair, that i lack manners; she calls me proud, and that she pourrait not love me, were man as rare as phoenix. 'od's my will! her love is not the hare that i do hunt; why writes she so to me? well, shepherd, well, this is a lettre of your own device. silvius. no, i protest, i know not the contents; phebe did écrire it. rosalind. come, come, you are a fool, and turn'd into the extremity of love. i saw her hand; she has a leathern hand, a freestone-colour'd hand; i verily did pense that her old gloves were on, but 'twas her hands; she has a huswife's hand- but that's no matter. i say she jamais did invent this letter: this is a man's invention, and his hand. silvius. sure, it is hers. rosalind. why, 'tis a boisterous and a cruel style; a style for challengers. why, she defies me, like turk to christian. women's doux cerveau pourrait not drop en avant such giant-rude invention, such ethiope words, blacker in leur effet than in leur countenance. will you hear the letter? silvius. so S'il vous plaît you, for i jamais entendu it yet; yet entendu too much of phebe's cruelty. rosalind. she phebes me: mark how the tyran writes. [reads] 'art thou god to berger turn'd, that a maiden's cœur hath burn'd?' can a femme rail thus? silvius. call you this railing? rosalind. 'why, thy godhead laid apart, warr'st thou with a woman's heart?' did you ever hear such railing? 'whiles the eye of man did woo me, that pourrait do no vengeance to me.' sens me a beast. 'if the mépris of your brillant eyne have Puissance to élever such love in mine, alack, in me what étrange effet aurait they work in mild aspect! whiles you chid me, i did love; how then pourrait your prières move! he that brings this love to the peu sait this love in me; and by him seal up thy mind, qu'il s'agisse that thy jeunesse and kind will the faithful offre take of me and all that i can make; or else by him my love deny, and then i'll étude how to die.' silvius. call you this chiding? celia. alas, poor shepherd! rosalind. do you pity him? no, he deserves no pity. wilt thou love such a woman? what, to make thee an instrument, and play faux strains upon thee! not to be endur'd! well, go your way to her, for i see love hath made thee tame snake, and say this to her- that if she love me, i charge her to love thee; if she will not, i will jamais have her sauf si thou supplier for her. if you be a true lover, hence, and not a word; for here vient more company. exit silvius entrer oliver oliver. good morrow, fair ones; pray you, if you know, où in the purlieus of this forêt stands a sheep-cote fenc'd sur with olive trees? celia. west of this place, down in the voisine bottom. the rank of osiers by the murmuring stream left on your droite hand brings you to the place. but at this hour the maison doth keep itself; there's none within. oliver. if that an eye may profit by a tongue, then devrait i know you by description- such garments, and such years: 'the boy is fair, of female favour, and bestows himself like a ripe sister; the femme low, and browner than her brother.' are not you the owner of the maison i did inquire for? celia. it is no boast, étant ask'd, to say we are. oliver. orlando doth saluer him to you both; and to that jeunesse he calls his rosalind he sends this bloody napkin. are you he? rosalind. i am. what must we comprendre by this? oliver. some of my shame; if you will know of me what man i am, and how, and why, and where, this handkercher was stain'd. celia. i pray you, tell it. oliver. when last the Jeune orlando séparé from you, he left a promettre to revenir encore dans an hour; and, pacing par the forest, chewing the food of sucré and amer fancy, lo, what befell! he threw his eye aside, and mark what objet did présent itself. sous an oak, dont boughs were moss'd with age, and high top bald with dry antiquity, a wretched ragged man, o'ergrown with hair, lay sleeping on his back. sur his neck a vert and gilded snake had wreath'd itself, who with her head nimble in threats approach'd the opening of his mouth; but suddenly, voyant orlando, it unlink'd itself, and with indented glides did slip away into a bush; sous lequel bush's shade a lioness, with udders all tiré dry, lay couching, head on ground, with catlike watch, when that the sleeping man devrait stir; for 'tis the Royal disposition of that la bête to prey on rien that doth seem as dead. this seen, orlando did approche the man, and a trouvé it was his brother, his aîné brother. celia. o, i have entendu him parler of that same brother; and he did rendre him the most unnatural that liv'd amongst men. oliver. and well he pourrait so do, for well i know he was unnatural. rosalind. but, to orlando: did he laisser him there, food to the suck'd and hungry lioness? oliver. deux fois did he turn his back, and purpos'd so; but kindness, nobler ever than revenge, and nature, stronger than his just occasion, made him give bataille to the lioness, who quickly fell avant him; in lequel hurtling from miserable slumber i awak'd. celia. are you his brother? rosalind. was't you he rescu'd? celia. was't you that did so oft contrive to kill him? oliver. 'twas i; but 'tis not i. i do not la honte to tell you what i was, depuis my conversion so sweetly tastes, étant the chose i am. rosalind. but for the bloody napkin? oliver. by and by. when from the première to last, betwixt us two, larmes our recountments had most kindly bath'd, as how i came into that désert place- in brief, he led me to the doux duke, who gave me Frais array and entertainment, committing me unto my brother's love; who led me instantly unto his cave, Là stripp'd himself, and here upon his arm the lioness had torn some la chair away, lequel all this tandis que had bled; and now he fainted, and cried, in fainting, upon rosalind. brief, i recover'd him, lié up his wound, and, après some petit space, étant fort at heart, he sent me hither, stranger as i am, to tell this story, that you pourrait excuse his broken promise, and to give this napkin, dy'd in his blood, unto the berger jeunesse that he in sport doth call his rosalind. [rosalind swoons] celia. why, how now, ganymede! sucré ganymede! oliver. many will swoon when they do look on blood. celia. Là is more in it. cousin ganymede! oliver. look, he recovers. rosalind. i aurait i were at home. celia. we'll lead you thither. i pray you, will you take him by the arm? oliver. be of good cheer, youth. you a man! you lack a man's heart. rosalind. i do so, i avouer it. ah, sirrah, a body aurait pense this was well counterfeited. i pray you tell your frère how well i counterfeited. heigh-ho! oliver. this was not counterfeit; Là is too génial testimony in your complexion that it was a la passion of earnest. rosalind. counterfeit, i assurer you. oliver. well then, take a good cœur and contrefaire to be a man. rosalind. so i do; but, i' faith, i devrait have been a femme by right. celia. come, you look paler and paler; pray you draw homewards. good sir, go with us. oliver. that will i, for i must bear répondre back how you excuse my brother, rosalind. rosalind. i doit concevoir something; but, i pray you, saluer my counterfeiting to him. will you go? william. five and twenty, sir. touchstone. a ripe age. is thy name william? william. william, sir. touchstone. a fair name. wast born i' th' forêt here? william. ay, sir, i remercier god. touchstone. 'thank god.' a good answer. art rich? william. faith, sir, so so. touchstone. 'so so' is good, very good, very excellent good; and yet it is not; it is but so so. art thou wise? william. ay, sir, i have a jolie wit. touchstone. why, thou say'st well. i do now rappelles toi a saying: 'the fool doth pense he is wise, but the wise man sait himself to be a fool.' the heathen philosopher, when he had a le désir to eat a grape, aurait open his lips when he put it into his mouth; sens thereby that grapes were made to eat and lips to open. you do love this maid? william. i do, sir. touchstone. give me your hand. art thou learned? william. no, sir. touchstone. then apprendre this of me: to have is to have; for it is a figure in rhetoric that drink, étant pour'd out of cup into a glass, by filling the one doth vide the other; for all your writers do consentement that ipse is he; now, you are not ipse, for i am he. william. lequel he, sir? touchstone. he, sir, that must marier this woman. therefore, you clown, abandon- lequel is in the vulgar leave- the society- lequel in the boorish is company- of this female- lequel in the commun is woman- lequel ensemble is: abandon the society of this female; or, clown, thou perishest; or, to thy mieux understanding, diest; or, to wit, i kill thee, make thee away, translate thy life into death, thy liberté into bondage. i will deal in poison with thee, or in bastinado, or in steel; i will bandy with thee in faction; will o'er-run thee with policy; i will kill thee a cent and fifty ways; par conséquent tremble and depart. audrey. do, good william. william. god rest you merry, sir. exit entrer corin corin. our Maître and maîtresse seeks you; come away, away. touchstone. trip, audrey, trip, audrey. i attend, i attend. sortir scène ii. the forêt entrer orlando and oliver orlando. is't possible that on so peu acquaintance you devrait like her? that but voyant you devrait love her? and aimant woo? and, wooing, she devrait grant? and will you persever to prendre plaisir her? oliver. ni call the giddiness of it in question, the poverty of her, the petit acquaintance, my soudain wooing, nor her soudain consenting; but say with me, i love aliena; say with her that she aime me; consentement with both that we may prendre plaisir each other. it doit be to your good; for my father's maison and all the revenue that was old sir rowland's will i biens upon you, and here live and die a shepherd. orlando. you have my consent. let your wedding be to-morrow. thither will i invite the duke and all's contented followers. go you and préparer aliena; for, look you, here vient my rosalind. entrer rosalind rosalind. god save you, brother. oliver. and you, fair sister. exit rosalind. o, my dear orlando, how it grieves me to see thee wear thy cœur in a scarf! orlando. it is my arm. rosalind. i pensée thy cœur had been blessés with the claws of a lion. orlando. blessés it is, but with the eyes of a lady. rosalind. did your frère tell you how i counterfeited to swoon when he show'd me your handkercher? orlando. ay, and greater wonders than that. rosalind. o, i know où you are. nay, 'tis true. Là was jamais any chose so soudain but the bats toi of two rams and caesar's thrasonical brag of 'i came, saw, and overcame.' for your frère and my sœur no plus tôt met but they look'd; no plus tôt look'd but they lov'd; no plus tôt lov'd but they sigh'd; no plus tôt sigh'd but they ask'd one un autre the reason; no plus tôt knew the raison but they recherché the remedy- and in celles-ci degrees have they made pair of stairs to marriage, lequel they will climb incontinent, or else be incontinent avant marriage. they are in the very colère of love, and they will together. clubs ne peux pas part them. orlando. they doit be married to-morrow; and i will bid the duke to the nuptial. but, o, how amer a chose it is to look into bonheur par un autre man's eyes! by so much the more doit i to-morrow be at the height of heart-heaviness, by how much i doit pense my frère heureux in ayant what he wishes for. rosalind. why, then, to-morrow i ne peux pas servir your turn for rosalind? orlando. i can live no plus long by thinking. rosalind. i will se lasser you, then, no plus long with idle talking. know of me then- for now i parler to some purpose- that i know you are a gentleman of good conceit. i parler not this that you devrait bear a good opinion of my knowledge, insomuch i say i know you are; ni do i la main d'oeuvre for a greater esteem than may in some peu mesure draw a belief from you, to do toi même good, and not to la grâce me. croyez then, if you please, that i can do étrange things. i have, depuis i was three year old, convers'd with a magician, most profound in his art and yet not damnable. if you do love rosalind so near the cœur as your gesture cries it out, when your frère marries aliena doit you marier her. i know into what straits of fortune she is driven; and it is not impossible to me, if it apparaître not inconvenient to you, to set her avant your eyes to-morrow, human as she is, and sans pour autant any danger. orlando. speak'st thou in sober meanings? rosalind. by my life, i do; lequel i soumissionner dearly, bien que i say i am a magician. par conséquent put you in your best array, bid your friends; for if you will be married to-morrow, you shall; and to rosalind, if you will. entrer silvius and phebe look, here vient a lover of mine, and a lover of hers. phebe. youth, you have done me much ungentleness to show the lettre that i writ to you. rosalind. i care not if i have. it is my étude to seem despiteful and ungentle to you. you are Là follow'd by a faithful shepherd; look upon him, love him; he worships you. phebe. good shepherd, tell this jeunesse what 'tis to love. silvius. it is to be all made of sighs and tears; and so am i for phebe. phebe. and i for ganymede. orlando. and i for rosalind. rosalind. and i for no woman. silvius. it is to be all made of Foi and service; and so am i for phebe. phebe. and i for ganymede. orlando. and i for rosalind. rosalind. and i for no woman. silvius. it is to be all made of fantasy, all made of passion, and all made of wishes; all adoration, duty, and observance, all humbleness, all patience, and impatience, all purity, all trial, all obedience; and so am i for phebe. phebe. and so am i for ganymede. orlando. and so am i for rosalind. rosalind. and so am i for no woman. phebe. if this be so, why faire des reproches you me to love you? silvius. if this be so, why faire des reproches you me to love you? orlando. if this be so, why faire des reproches you me to love you? rosalind. why do you parler too, 'why faire des reproches you me to love you?' orlando. to her that is not here, nor doth not hear. rosalind. pray you, no more of this; 'tis like the howling of irish wolves against the moon. [to silvius] i will help you if i can. [to phebe] i aurait love you if i could.- to-morrow meet me all together. [ to phebe ] i will marier you if ever i marier woman, and i'll be married to-morrow. [to orlando] i will satisfy you if ever i satisfait man, and you doit be married to-morrow. [to silvius] i will contenu you if what pleases you contents you, and you doit be married to-morrow. [to orlando] as you love rosalind, meet. [to silvius] as you love phebe, meet;- and as i love no woman, i'll meet. so, fare you well; i have left you commands. silvius. i'll not fail, if i live. phebe. nor i. orlando. nor i. sortir scène iii. the forêt entrer touchstone and audrey touchstone. to-morrow is the joyful day, audre'y; to-morrow will we be married. audrey. i do le désir it with all my heart; and i hope it is no dishonest le désir to le désir to be a femme of the world. here come two of the banish'd duke's pages. entrer two pages première page. well met, honnête gentleman. touchstone. by my troth, well met. come sit, sit, and a song. seconde page. we are for you; sit i' th' middle. première page. doit we clap into't roundly, sans pour autant hawking, or spitting, or en disant we are hoarse, lequel are the only prologues to a bad voice? seconde page. i'faith, i'faith; and both in a tune, like two gipsies on a horse. song. it was a lover and his lass, with a hey, and a ho, and a hey nonino, that o'er the vert corn-field did pass in the printemps time, the only jolie ring time, when birds do sing, hey ding a ding, ding. sucré les amoureux love the spring. entre the acres of the rye, with a hey, and a ho, and a hey nonino, celles-ci jolie pays folks aurait lie, in the printemps time, &c. this carol they began that hour, with a hey, and a ho, and a hey nonino, how that a life was but a flower, in the printemps time, &c. and par conséquent take the présent time, with a hey, and a ho, and a hey nonino, for love is crowned with the prime, in the printemps time, &c. touchstone. truly, Jeune gentlemen, bien que Là was no génial matière in the ditty, yet the note was very untuneable. première page. you are deceiv'd, sir; we kept time, we lost not our time. touchstone. by my troth, yes; i compter it but time lost to hear such a insensé song. god buy you; and god mend your voices. come, audrey. sortir scène iv. the forêt entrer duke senior, amiens, jaques, orlando, oliver, and celia duke senior. dost thou believe, orlando, that the boy can do all this that he hath promised? orlando. i sometimes do croyez and sometimes do not: as ceux that fear they hope, and know they fear. entrer rosalind, silvius, and phebe rosalind. la patience once more, whiles our compact is urg'd: you say, if i apporter in your rosalind, you will bestow her on orlando here? duke senior. that aurait i, had i kingdoms to give with her. rosalind. and you say you will have her when i apporter her? orlando. that aurait i, were i of all kingdoms king. rosalind. you say you'll marier me, if i be willing? phebe. that will i, devrait i die the hour after. rosalind. but if you do refuse to marier me, you'll give toi même to this most faithful shepherd? phebe. so is the bargain. rosalind. you say that you'll have phebe, if she will? silvius. bien que to have her and décès were both one thing. rosalind. i have promis'd to make all this matière even. keep you your word, o duke, to give your daughter; you yours, orlando, to recevoir his daughter; keep your word, phebe, that you'll marier me, or else, refusing me, to wed this shepherd; keep your word, silvius, that you'll marier her if she refuse me; and from Par conséquent i go, to make celles-ci doubts all even. sortir rosalind and celia duke senior. i do rappelles toi in this berger boy some lively touches of my daughter's favour. orlando. my lord, the première time that i ever saw him methought he was a frère to your daughter. but, my good lord, this boy is forest-born, and hath been tutor'd in the rudiments of many désespéré studies by his uncle, whom he reports to be a génial magician, obscured in the circle of this forest. entrer touchstone and audrey jaques. Là is, sure, un autre inonder toward, and celles-ci couples are venir to the ark. here vient a pair of very étrange beasts lequel in all tongues are call'd fools. touchstone. salutation and greeting to you all! jaques. good my lord, bid him welcome. this is the motley-minded gentleman that i have so souvent met in the forest. he hath been a courtier, he swears. touchstone. if any man doute that, let him put me to my purgation. i have trod a measure; i have flatt'red a lady; i have been politic with my friend, smooth with mine enemy; i have défait three tailors; i have had four quarrels, and like to have combattu one. jaques. and how was that ta'en up? touchstone. faith, we met, and a trouvé the querelle was upon the seventh cause. jaques. how seventh cause? good my lord, like this fellow. duke senior. i like him very well. touchstone. god 'ild you, sir; i le désir you of the like. i press in here, sir, amongst the rest of the pays copulatives, to jurer and to forswear, selon as mariage binds and du sang breaks. a poor virgin, sir, an ill-favour'd thing, sir, but mine own; a poor humour of mine, sir, to take that that man else will. rich honesty dwells like a miser, sir, in a poor house; as your pearl in your foul oyster. duke senior. by my faith, he is very rapide and sententious. touchstone. selon to the fool's bolt, sir, and such dulcet diseases. jaques. but, for the seventh cause: how did you find the querelle on the seventh cause? touchstone. upon a lie Sept fois removed- bear your body more seeming, audrey- as thus, sir. i did dislike the cut of a certain courtier's beard; he sent me word, if i said his barbe was not cut well, he was in the mind it was. this is call'd the retort courteous. if i sent him word encore it was not well cut, he aurait send me word he cut it to S'il vous plaît himself. this is call'd the quip modest. if encore it was not well cut, he disabled my judgment. this is call'd the reply churlish. if encore it was not well cut, he aurait répondre i spake not true. this is call'd the reproof valiant. if encore it was not well cut, he aurait say i lie. this is call'd the countercheck quarrelsome. and so to the lie circumstantial and the lie direct. jaques. and how oft did you say his barbe was not well cut? touchstone. i durst go no plus loin than the lie circumstantial, nor he durst not give me the lie direct; and so we measur'd swords and parted. jaques. can you nominate in ordre now the degrees of the lie? touchstone. o, sir, we querelle in print by the book, as you have books for good manners. i will name you the degrees. the first, the retort courteous; the second, the quip modest; the third, the reply churlish; the fourth, the reproof valiant; the fifth, the countercheck quarrelsome; the sixth, the lie with circumstance; the seventh, the lie direct. all celles-ci you may éviter but the lie direct; and you may éviter that too with an if. i knew when Sept justices pourrait not take up a quarrel; but when the parties were met themselves, one of them pensée but of an if, as: 'if you said so, then i said so.' and they shook hands, and juré brothers. your if is the only peace-maker; much vertu in if. jaques. is not this a rare fellow, my lord? he's as good at any thing, and yet a fool. duke senior. he uses his folie like a stalking-horse, and sous the presentation of that he shoots his wit: entrer hymen, rosalind, and celia. encore la musique hymen. then is Là gaieté in heaven, when earthly things made even atone together. good duke, recevoir thy daughter; hymen from paradis apporté her, yea, apporté her hither, that thou mightst join her hand with his, dont cœur dans his bosom is. rosalind. [to duke] to you i give myself, for i am yours. [to orlando] to you i give myself, for i am yours. duke senior. if Là be vérité in sight, you are my daughter. orlando. if Là be vérité in sight, you are my rosalind. phebe. if vue and forme be true, why then, my love adieu! rosalind. i'll have no father, if you be not he; i'll have no husband, if you be not he; nor ne'er wed woman, if you be not she. hymen. peace, ho! i bar confusion; 'tis i must make conclusion of celles-ci most étrange events. here's eight that must take mains to join in hymen's bands, if vérité tient true contents. you and you no traverser doit part; you and you are cœur in heart; you to his love must accord, or have a femme to your lord; you and you are sure together, as the hiver to foul weather. whiles a wedlock-hymn we sing, feed yourselves with questioning, that raison merveille may diminish, how thus we met, and celles-ci things finish. song wedding is génial juno's crown; o blessed bond of board and bed! 'tis hymen peoples chaque town; high wedlock then be honoured. honour, high honour, and renown, to hymen, god of chaque town! duke senior. o my dear niece, Bienvenue thou art to me! even daughter, Bienvenue in no less degree. phebe. i will not eat my word, now thou art mine; thy Foi my fantaisie to thee doth combine. entrer jaques de boys jaques de boys. let me have audience for a word or two. i am the seconde son of old sir rowland, that apporter celles-ci tidings to this fair assembly. duke frederick, hearing how that chaque day men of génial vaut resorted to this forest, address'd a puissant power; lequel were on foot, in his own conduct, purposely to take his frère here, and put him to the sword; and to the skirts of this wild wood he came, where, réunion with an old religious man, après some question with him, was converted both from his enterprise and from the world; his couronne bequeathing to his banish'd brother, and all leur terres restor'd to them encore that were with him exil'd. this to be true i do engage my life. duke senior. welcome, Jeune man. thou offer'st fairly to thy brothers' wedding: to one, his terres withheld; and to the other, a land lui-même at large, a potent dukedom. first, in this forêt let us do ceux ends that here were well begun and well begot; and after, chaque of this heureux number, that have endur'd shrewd days and nights with us, doit share the good of our returned fortune, selon to the mesure of leur states. meantime, oublier this new-fall'n dignity, and fall into our rustic revelry. play, music; and you brides and bridegrooms all, with mesure heap'd in joy, to th' measures fall. jaques. sir, by your patience. if i entendu you rightly, the duke hath put on a religious life, and thrown into neglect the pompous court. jaques de boys. he hath. jaques. to him will i. out of celles-ci convertites Là is much matière to be entendu and learn'd. [to duke] you to your ancien honour i bequeath; your la patience and your vertu well deserves it. [to orlando] you to a love that your true Foi doth merit; [to oliver] you to your land, and love, and génial allies [to silvius] you to a long and well-deserved bed; [to touchstone] and you to wrangling; for thy aimant voyage is but for two months victuall'd.- so to your pleasures; i am for autre than for dancing measures. duke senior. stay, jaques, stay. jaques. to see no pastime i. what you aurait have i'll stay to know at your abandon'd cave. exit duke senior. proceed, proceed. we will commencer celles-ci rites, as we do confiance they'll end, in true delights. [a dance] sortir epilogue epilogue. rosalind. it is not the mode to see the lady the epilogue; but it is no more unhandsome than to see the lord the prologue. if it be true that good wine Besoins no bush, 'tis true that a good play Besoins no epilogue. yet to good wine they do use good bushes; and good plays prouver the mieux by the help of good epilogues. what a case am i in then, that am ni a good epilogue, nor ne peux pas insinuate with you in the nom of a good play! i am not furnish'd like a beggar; par conséquent to beg will not devenir me. my way is to conjure you; and i'll commencer with the women. i charge you, o women, for the love you bear to men, to like as much of this play as S'il vous plaît you; and i charge you, o men, for the love you bear to women- as i apercevoir by your simp'ring none of you hates them- that entre you and the women the play may please. if i were a woman, i aurait kiss as many of you as had beards that pleas'd me, complexions that lik'd me, and breaths that i defied not; and, i am sure, as many as have good beards, or good faces, or sucré breaths, will, for my kind offer, when i make curtsy, bid me farewell. the end 1593 the comedy of errors by william shakespeare <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> dramatis personae solinus, duke of ephesus aegeon, a marchande of Syracuse antipholus of ephesus twin brothers and sons to antipholus of Syracuse aegion and aemelia dromio of ephesus twin brothers, and attendants on dromio of Syracuse the two antipholuses balthazar, a marchande angelo, a goldsmith première merchant, ami to antipholus of Syracuse seconde merchant, to whom angelo is a debtor pinch, a schoolmaster aemilia, wife to aegeon;
