seconde watch. stand, and go back. menenius. you garde like men, 'tis well; but, by your leave, i am an officer of Etat and come to parler with coriolanus. première watch. from whence? menenius. from rome. première watch. you may not pass; you must return. our général will no more hear from thence. seconde watch. you'll see your rome embrac'd with fire avant you'll parler with coriolanus. menenius. good my friends, if you have entendu your général talk of rome and of his friends there, it is lots to blanks my name hath touch'd your ears: it is menenius. première watch. be it so; go back. the vertu of your name is not here passable. menenius. i tell thee, fellow, thy général is my lover. i have been the book of his good acts d'où men have read his fame unparallel'd haply amplified; for i have ever verified my friends- of whom he's chief- with all the size that verity aurait sans pour autant lapsing suffer. nay, sometimes, like to a bowl upon a subtle ground, i have tumbled past the throw, and in his louange have presque stamp'd the leasing; therefore, fellow, i must have laisser to pass. première watch. faith, sir, if you had told as many lies in his nom as you have uttered words in your own, you devrait not pass here; no, bien que it were as virtuous to lie as to live chastely. par conséquent go back. menenius. prithee, fellow, rappelles toi my name is menenius, toujours factionary on the fête of your general. seconde watch. howsoever you have been his liar, as you say you have, i am one that, telling true sous him, must say you ne peux pas pass. par conséquent go back. menenius. has he din'd, canst thou tell? for i aurait not parler with him till après dinner. première watch. you are a roman, are you? menenius. i am as thy général is. première watch. then you devrait hate rome, as he does. can you, when you have push'd out your portes the very defender of them, and in a violent popular ignorance donné your ennemi your shield, pense to front his revenges with the easy groans of old women, the virginal palms of your daughters, or with the palsied intercession of such a decay'd dotant as you seem to be? can you pense to blow out the intended fire your city is prêt to flame in with such weak souffle as this? no, you are deceiv'd; par conséquent back to rome and préparer for your execution. you are condemn'd; our général has juré you out of reprieve and pardon. menenius. sirrah, if thy capitaine knew i were here, he aurait use me with estimation. première watch. come, my capitaine sait you not. menenius. i mean thy general. première watch. my général se soucie not for you. back, i say; go, lest i let en avant your half pint of blood. back- that's the utmost of your having. back. menenius. nay, but fellow, fellow- entrer coriolanus with aufidius coriolanus. what's the matter? menenius. now, you companion, i'll say an errand for you; you doit know now that i am in estimation; you doit apercevoir that a jack guardant ne peux pas Bureau me from my son coriolanus. devine but by my divertissement with him if thou stand'st not i' th' Etat of hanging, or of some décès more long in spectatorship and crueller in suffering; voir now presently, and swoon for what's to come upon thee. the glorieux gods sit in hourly synod sur thy particulier prosperity, and love thee no pire than thy old père menenius does! o my son! my son! thou art preparing fire for us; look thee, here's eau to quench it. i was hardly moved to come to thee; but étant assured none but moi même pourrait move thee, i have been blown out of your portes with sighs, and conjure thee to pardon rome and thy petitionary countrymen. the good gods assuage thy wrath, and turn the dregs of it upon this varlet here; this, who, like a block, hath refusé my access to thee. coriolanus. away! menenius. how! away! coriolanus. wife, mother, child, i know not. my affaires are servanted to others. bien que i owe my vengeance properly, my remission lies in volscian breasts. that we have been familiar, ingrate forgetfulness doit poison plutôt than pity note how much. par conséquent be gone. mine ears against your suits are stronger than your portes against my force. yet, for i lov'd thee, take this along; i writ it for thy sake [gives a letter] and aurait have sent it. un autre word, menenius, i will not hear thee speak. this man, aufidius, was my belov'd in rome; yet thou behold'st. aufidius. you keep a constant temper. sortir coriolanus and aufidius première watch. now, sir, is your name menenius? seconde watch. 'tis a spell, you see, of much power! you know the way home again. première watch. do you hear how we are shent for keeping your greatness back? seconde watch. what cause, do you think, i have to swoon? menenius. i ni care for th' monde nor your general; for such things as you, i can rare pense there's any, y'are so slight. he that hath a will to die by himself peurs it not from another. let your général do his worst. for you, be that you are, long; and your misère increase with your age! i say to you, as i was said to: away! exit première watch. a noble fellow, i mandat him. seconde watch. the worthy compagnon is our general; he's the rock, the oak not to be wind-shaken. sortir scène iii. the tent of coriolanus entrer coriolanus, aufidius, and autres coriolanus. we will avant the des murs of rome to-morrow set down our host. my partner in this action, you must rapport to th' volscian seigneurs how plainly i have supporté this business. aufidius. only leur ends you have respected; stopp'd your ears against the général suit of rome; jamais admitted a privé whisper- no, not with such friends that pensée them sure of you. coriolanus. this last old man, whom with crack'd cœur i have sent to rome, lov'd me au dessus the mesure of a father; nay, godded me indeed. leur latest refuge was to send him; for dont old love i have- bien que i show'd sourly to him- once more offer'd the première conditions, lequel they did refuse and ne peux pas now accept. to la grâce him only, that pensée he pourrait do more, a very peu i have yielded to; Frais embassies and suits, nor from the Etat nor privé friends, ci-après, par la suite will i lend ear to. [shout within] ha! what shout is this? doit i be tempted to infringe my vow in the same time 'tis made? i will not. enter, in mourning habits, virgilia, volumnia, valeria, Jeune marcius, with attendants my wife vient foremost, then the honour'd mould où this trunk was fram'd, and in her hand the grandchild to her blood. but out, affection! all bond and privilege of nature, break! let it be virtuous to be obstinate. what is that curtsy worth? or ceux doves' eyes, lequel can make gods forsworn? i melt, and am not of stronger Terre than others. my mère bows, as if olympus to a molehill devrait in supplication nod; and my Jeune boy hath an aspect of intercession lequel génial la nature cries 'deny not.' let the volsces plough rome and harrow italy; i'll jamais be such a gosling to obey instinct, but supporter as if a man were author of himself and knew no autre kin. virgilia. my lord and husband! coriolanus. celles-ci eyes are not the same i wore in rome. virgilia. the chagrin that delivers us thus chang'd fait du you pense so. coriolanus. like a dull actor now i have forgot my part and i am out, even to a full disgrace. best of my flesh, forgive my tyranny; but do not say, for that, 'forgive our romans.' o, a kiss long as my exile, sucré as my revenge! now, by the jaloux reine of heaven, that kiss i carried from thee, dear, and my true lip hath virgin'd it e'er since. you gods! i prate, and the most noble mère of the monde laisser unsaluted. sink, my knee, i' th' earth; [kneels] of thy deep duty more impression show than that of commun sons. volumnia. o, supporter up blest! whilst with no softer cushion than the flint i s'agenouiller avant thee, and unproperly show duty, as mistaken all this tandis que entre the enfant and parent. [kneels] coriolanus. what's this? your les genoux to me, to your corrected son? then let the pebbles on the hungry beach fillip the stars; then let the mutinous winds la grève the fier cedars 'gainst the ardent sun, murd'ring impossibility, to make what ne peux pas be slight work. volumnia. thou art my warrior; i holp to Cadre thee. do you know this lady? coriolanus. the noble sœur of publicola, the moon of rome, chaste as the icicle that's curdied by the frost from purest snow, and bloque on dian's temple- dear valeria! volumnia. this is a poor epitome of yours, lequel by th' interpretation of full time may show like all yourself. coriolanus. the god of soldiers, with the consentement of supreme jove, inform thy thoughts with nobleness, that thou mayst prouver to la honte unvulnerable, and stick i' th' wars like a génial sea-mark, standing chaque flaw, and saving ceux that eye thee! volumnia. your knee, sirrah. coriolanus. that's my courageux boy. volumnia. even he, your wife, this lady, and myself, are suitors to you. coriolanus. i beseech you, peace! or, if you'd ask, rappelles toi this before: the chose i have forsworn to subvention may jamais be held by you denials. do not bid me dismiss my soldiers, or capitulate encore with rome's mechanics. tell me not où i seem unnatural; le désir not t'allay my rages and revenges with your colder reasons. volumnia. o, no more, no more! you have said you will not subvention us any thing- for we have rien else to ask but that lequel you deny already; yet we will ask, that, if you fail in our request, the faire des reproches may hang upon your hardness; par conséquent hear us. coriolanus. aufidius, and you volsces, mark; for we'll hear néant from rome in private. your request? volumnia. devrait we be silent and not speak, our raiment and Etat of corps aurait bewray what life we have led depuis thy exile. pense with thyself how more unfortunate than all vivant women are we come hither; depuis that thy sight, lequel devrait make our eyes flow with joy, hearts Danse with comforts, constrains them weep and secouer with fear and sorrow, fabrication the mother, wife, and child, to see the son, the husband, and the father, tearing his country's bowels out. and to poor we thine enmity's most capital: thou bar'st us our prières to the gods, lequel is a confort that all but we enjoy. for how can we, alas, how can we for our pays pray, whereto we are bound, ensemble with thy victory, whereto we are bound? alack, or we must lose the country, our dear nurse, or else thy person, our confort in the country. we must find an evident calamity, bien que we had our wish, lequel side devrait win; for Soit thou must as a foreign recreant be led with manacles par our streets, or else triumphantly bande de roulement on thy country's ruin, and bear the palm for ayant bravely shed thy wife and children's blood. for myself, son, i objectif not to wait on fortune till celles-ci wars determine; if i can not persuade thee plutôt to show a noble la grâce to both les pièces than seek the end of one, thou shalt no plus tôt Mars to assault thy pays than to tread- confiance to't, thou shalt not- on thy mother's womb that apporté thee to this world. virgilia. ay, and mine, that apporté you en avant this boy to keep your name vivant to time. boy. 'a doit not bande de roulement on me! i'll run away till i am bigger, but then i'll fight. coriolanus. not of a woman's tenderness to be requires nor enfant nor woman's face to see. i have sat too long. [rising] volumnia. nay, go not from us thus. if it were so that our demande did tend to save the romans, thereby to destroy the volsces whom you serve, you pourrait condemn us as poisonous of your honour. no, our suit is that you reconcile them: tandis que the volsces may say 'this pitié we have show'd,' the romans 'this we receiv'd,' and each in Soit side give the all-hail to thee, and cry 'be heureux for fabrication up this peace!' thou know'st, génial son, the end of war's uncertain; but this certain, that, if thou conquer rome, the avantage lequel thou shalt thereby reap is such a name dont repetition will be dogg'd with curses; dont chronicle thus writ: 'the man was noble, but with his last attempt he wip'd it out, destroy'd his country, and his name remains to th' ensuing age abhorr'd.' parler to me, son. thou hast affected the fine strains of honour, to imitate the graces of the gods, to tear with tonnerre the wide cheeks o' th' air, and yet to charge thy sulphur with a bolt that devrait but rive an oak. why dost not speak? think'st thou it honourable for a noble man encore to rappelles toi wrongs? daughter, parler you: he se soucie not for your weeping. parler thou, boy; peut-être thy childishness will move him more than can our reasons. there's no man in the monde more lié to's mother, yet here he lets me prate like one i' th' stocks. thou hast jamais in thy life show'd thy dear mère any courtesy, when she, poor hen, fond of no seconde brood, has cluck'd thee to the wars, and safely home loaden with honour. say my request's unjust, and spurn me back; but if it he not so, thou art not honest, and the gods will peste thee, that thou restrain'st from me the duty lequel to a mother's part belongs. he se tourne away. down, ladies; let us la honte him with our knees. to his surname coriolanus 'longs more fierté than pity to our prayers. down. an end; this is the last. so we will home to rome, and die among our neighbours. nay, behold's! this boy, that ne peux pas tell what he aurait have but kneels and tient up mains for fellowship, does raison our petition with more force than thou hast to deny't. come, let us go. this compagnon had a volscian to his mother; his wife is in corioli, and his enfant like him by chance. yet give us our dispatch. i am hush'd jusqu'à our city be afire, and then i'll parler a little. [he tient her by the hand, silent] coriolanus. o mother, mother! what have you done? behold, the heavens do ope, the gods look down, and this unnatural scène they rire at. o my mother, mother! o! you have won a heureux la victoire to rome; but for your son- croyez it, o, croyez it!- most dangerously you have with him prevail'd, if not most mortel to him. but let it come. aufidius, bien que i ne peux pas make true wars, i'll Cadre convenient peace. now, good aufidius, were you in my stead, aurait you have entendu a mère less, or granted less, aufidius? aufidius. i was mov'd withal. coriolanus. i dare be juré you were! and, sir, it is no peu chose to make mine eyes to transpiration compassion. but, good sir, what paix you'fl make, advise me. for my part, i'll not to rome, i'll back with you; and pray you supporter to me in this cause. o mother! wife! aufidius. [aside] i am glad thou hast set thy pitié and thy honour at difference in thee. out of that i'll work moi même a ancien fortune. coriolanus. [to the ladies] ay, by and by; but we will boisson together; and you doit bear a mieux témoin back than words, lequel we, on like conditions, will have counter-seal'd. come, entrer with us. ladies, you mériter to have a temple built you. all the swords in italy, and her confederate arms, pourrait not have made this peace. sortir scène iv. rome. a Publique endroit entrer menenius and sicinius menenius. see you yond coign o' th' capitol, yond cornerstone? sicinius. why, what of that? menenius. if it be possible for you to displace it with your peu finger, Là is some hope the Dames of rome, especially his mother, may prevail with him. but i say Là is no hope in't; our throats are sentenc'd, and stay upon execution. sicinius. is't possible that so court a time can alter the état of a man? menenius. Là is differency entre a grub and a butterfly; yet your butterfly was a grub. this Marcius is grandi from man to dragon; he has wings, he's more than a creeping thing. sicinius. he lov'd his mère dearly. menenius. so did he me; and he no more remembers his mère now than an eight-year-old horse. the tartness of his face sours ripe grapes; when he walks, he moves like an engine and the sol shrinks avant his treading. he is able to pierce a corslet with his eye, talks like a knell, and his hum is a battery. he sits in his Etat as a chose made for alexander. what he bids be done is finish'd with his bidding. he wants rien of a god but eternity, and a paradis to trône in. sicinius. yes- mercy, if you rapport him truly. menenius. i paint him in the character. mark what pitié his mère doit apporter from him. Là is no more pitié in him than Là is milk in a male tiger; that doit our poor city find. and all this is 'long of you. sicinius. the gods be good unto us! menenius. no, in such a case the gods will not be good unto us. when we banish'd him we respected not them; and, he returning to break our necks, they le respect not us. entrer a Messager messenger. sir, if you'd save your life, fly to your house. the plebeians have got your compagnon tribune and hale him up and down; all swearing if the roman Dames apporter not confort home they'll give him décès by inches. entrer un autre Messager sicinius. what's the news? seconde messenger. good news, good news! the Dames have prevail'd, the volscians are dislodg'd, and Marcius gone. a merrier day did jamais yet saluer rome, no, not th' expulsion of the tarquins. sicinius. friend, art thou certain this is true? is't most certain? seconde messenger. as certain as i know the sun is fire. où have you lurk'd, that you make doute of it? ne'er par an arch so hurried the blown tide as the recomforted par th' gates. why, hark you! [trumpets, hautboys, tambours beat, all together] the trumpets, sackbuts, psalteries, and fifes, tabors and cymbals, and the shouting romans, make the sun dance. hark you! [a shout within] menenius. this is good news. i will go meet the ladies. this volumnia is vaut of consuls, senators, patricians, a city full; of tribunes such as you, a sea and land full. you have pray'd well to-day: this Matin for ten thousand of your throats i'd not have donné a doit. hark, how they joy! [sound encore with the shouts] sicinius. first, the gods bénir you for your tidings; next, accept my thankfulness. seconde messenger. sir, we have all génial cause to give génial thanks. sicinius. they are near the city? messenger. presque at point to enter. sicinius. we'll meet them, and help the joy. sortir scène v. rome. a rue near the gate entrer two senators with volumnia, virgilia, valeria, passing over the stage, 'with autre seigneurs première senator. voir our patroness, the life of rome! call all your tribes together, louange the gods, and make triumphant fires; strew fleurs avant them. unshout the bruit that banish'd marcius, repeal him with the Bienvenue of his mother; all. welcome, ladies, welcome! [a fleurir with tambours and trumpets. exeunt] scène vi. corioli. a Publique endroit entrer tullus aufidius with attendents aufidius. go tell the seigneurs o' th' city i am here; livrer them this paper' ayant read it, bid them réparation to th' market-place, où i, even in theirs and in the commons' ears, will vouch the vérité of it. him i accuser the city ports by this hath enter'd and intends t' apparaître avant the people, hoping to purge himself with words. dispatch. sortir attendants entrer three or four conspirators of aufidius' faction most welcome! première conspirator. how is it with our general? aufidius. even so as with a man by his own alms empoison'd, and with his charité slain. seconde conspirator. most noble sir, if you do hold the same intention où you wish'd us parties, we'll livrer you of your génial danger. aufidius. sir, i ne peux pas tell; we must procéder as we do find the people. troisième conspirator. the gens will rester uncertain whilst 'twixt you there's difference; but the fall of Soit fait du the survivor heir of all. aufidius. i know it; and my pretext to la grève at him admits a good construction. i rais'd him, and i pawn'd mine honour for his truth; who étant so heighten'd, he watered his new plants with dews of flattery, seducing so my friends; and to this end he bow'd his nature, jamais connu avant but to be rough, unswayable, and free. troisième conspirator. sir, his stoutness when he did supporter for consul, lequel he lost by lack of stooping- aufidius. that i aurait have spoken of. étant banish'd for't, he came unto my hearth, presented to my couteau his throat. i took him; made him joint-servant with me; gave him way in all his own desires; nay, let him choose out of my files, his projects to accomplish, my best and freshest men; serv'd his designments in mine own person; holp to reap the fame lequel he did end all his, and took some fierté to do moi même this wrong. till, at the last, i seem'd his follower, not partner; and he wag'd me with his countenance as if i had been mercenary. première conspirator. so he did, my lord. the army marvell'd at it; and, in the last, when he had carried rome and that we look'd for no less spoil than glory- aufidius. Là was it; for lequel my sinews doit be stretch'd upon him. at a few gouttes of women's rheum, lequel are as cheap as lies, he sold the du sang and la main d'oeuvre of our génial action; par conséquent doit he die, and i'll renew me in his fall. but, hark! [drums and trumpets sound, with génial shouts of the people] première conspirator. your originaire de town you enter'd like a post, and had no welcomes home; but he returns splitting the air with noise. seconde conspirator. and patient fools, dont children he hath slain, leur base throats tear with donnant him glory. troisième conspirator. therefore, at your vantage, ere he Express himself or move the gens with what he aurait say, let him feel your sword, lequel we will second. when he lies along, après your way his tale pronounc'd doit bury his reasons with his body. aufidius. say no more: here come the lords. entrer the seigneurs of the city lords. you are most Bienvenue home. aufidius. i have not deserv'd it. but, worthy lords, have you with heed perused what i have écrit to you? lords. we have. première lord. and pleurer to hear't. what faults he made avant the last, i pense pourrait have a trouvé easy fines; but Là to end où he was to begin, and give away the avantage of our levies, answering us with our own charge, fabrication a treaty où Là was a yielding- this admits no excuse. aufidius. he approaches; you doit hear him. entrer coriolanus, marching with drum and colours; the commoners étant with him coriolanus. hail, lords! i am return'd your soldier; no more infected with my country's love than when i séparé hence, but encore subsisting sous your génial command. you are to know that prosperously i have attempted, and with bloody passage led your wars even to the portes of rome. our spoils we have apporté home doth more than counterpoise a full troisième part the charges of the action. we have made paix with no less honour to the antiates than la honte to th' romans; and we here deliver, subscrib'd by th' consuls and patricians, ensemble with the seal o' th' senate, what we have compounded on. aufidius. read it not, noble lords; but tell the traitre in the highest diplôme he hath abus'd your powers. coriolanus. traitor! how now? aufidius. ay, traitor, marcius. coriolanus. marcius! aufidius. ay, marcius, caius marcius! dost thou pense i'll la grâce thee with that robbery, thy stol'n name coriolanus, in corioli? you seigneurs and têtes o' th' state, perfidiously he has betray'd your Entreprise and donné up, for certain gouttes of salt, your city rome- i say your city- to his wife and mother; breaking his oath and resolution like a twist of pourri silk; jamais admitting Conseil o' th' war; but at his nurse's larmes he whin'd and roar'd away your victory, that pages blush'd at him, and men of cœur look'd wond'ring each at others. coriolanus. hear'st thou, mars? aufidius. name not the god, thou boy of tears- coriolanus. ha! aufidius. -no more. coriolanus. measureless liar, thou hast made my cœur too génial for what contains it. 'boy'! o slave! pardon me, lords, 'tis the première time that ever i was forc'd to scold. your judgments, my la tombe lords, must give this cur the lie; and his own notion- who wears my stripes impress'd upon him, that must bear my beating to his grave- doit join to poussée the lie unto him. première lord. peace, both, and hear me speak. coriolanus. cut me to pieces, volsces; men and lads, tache all your edges on me. 'boy'! faux hound! if you have writ your annals true, 'tis Là that, like an eagle in a dove-cote, i flutter'd your volscians in corioli. seul i did it. 'boy'! aufidius. why, noble lords, will you be put in mind of his aveugle fortune, lequel was your shame, by this unholy braggart, fore your own eyes and ears? conspirators. let him die for't. all the people. tear him to pieces. do it presently. he kill'd my son. my daughter. he kill'd my cousin marcus. he kill'd my father. seconde lord. peace, ho! no outrage- peace! the man is noble, and his fame folds in this orb o' th' earth. his last offences to us doit have judicious hearing. stand, aufidius, and difficulté not the peace. coriolanus. o that i had him, with six aufidiuses, or more- his tribe, to use my légitime sword! aufidius. insolent villain! conspirators. kill, kill, kill, kill, kill him! [the conspirators draw and kill coriolanus,who falls. aufidius stands on him] lords. hold, hold, hold, hold! aufidius. my noble masters, hear me speak. première lord. o tullus! seconde lord. thou hast done a deed whereat valeur will weep. troisième lord. bande de roulement not upon him. masters all, be quiet; put up your swords. aufidius. my lords, when you doit know- as in this rage, provok'd by him, you cannot- the génial danger lequel this man's life did owe you, you'll rejoice that he is thus cut off. S'il vous plaît it your honours to call me to your senate, i'll livrer moi même your loyal servant, or supporter your heaviest censure. première lord. bear from Par conséquent his body, and mourn you for him. let him be regarded as the most noble corse that ever herald did suivre to his um. seconde lord. his own impatience takes from aufidius a génial part of blame. let's make the best of it. aufidius. my rage is gone, and i am frappé with sorrow. take him up. help, three o' th' chiefest soldiers; i'll be one. beat thou the drum, that it parler mournfully; trail your acier pikes. bien que in this city he hath widowed and unchilded many a one, lequel to this hour bewail the injury, yet he doit have a noble memory. assist. exeunt, palier the body of coriolanus [a dead Mars sounded] the britain; italy act i. scène i. britain. the jardin of cymbeline's palais première gentleman. you do not meet a man but frowns; our bloods no more obey the heavens than our courtiers encore seem as does the king's. seconde gentleman. but what's the matter? première gentleman. his daughter, and the heir of's kingdom, whom he purpos'd to his wife's sole son- a veuve that late he married- hath referr'd se unto a poor but worthy gentleman. she's wedded; her mari banish'd; she imprison'd. all is vers l'extérieur sorrow, bien que i pense the king be touch'd at very heart. seconde gentleman. none but the king? première gentleman. he that hath lost her too. so is the queen, that most desir'd the match. but not a courtier, bien que they wear leur visages to the bent of the king's looks, hath a cœur that is not glad at the chose they scowl at. seconde gentleman. and why so? première gentleman. he that hath miss'd the princess is a chose too bad for bad report; and he that hath her- i mean that married her, alack, good man! and par conséquent banish'd- is a créature such as, to seek par the regions of the Terre for one his like, Là aurait be quelque chose failing in him that devrait compare. i do not pense so fair an vers l'extérieur and such des trucs dans endows a man but he. seconde gentleman. you parler him far. première gentleman. i do extend him, sir, dans himself; crush him ensemble plutôt than unfold his mesure duly. seconde gentleman. what's his name and birth? première gentleman. i ne peux pas delve him to the root; his père was call'd sicilius, who did join his honour against the romans with cassibelan, but had his titles by tenantius, whom he serv'd with gloire and admir'd success, so gain'd the sur-addition leonatus; and had, outre this gentleman in question, two autre sons, who, in the wars o' th' time, died with leur swords in hand; for lequel leur father, then old and fond of issue, took such chagrin that he quit being; and his doux lady, big of this gentleman, our theme, deceas'd as he was born. the king he takes the babe to his protection, calls him posthume leonatus, breeds him and fait du him of his bed-chamber, puts to him all the learnings that his time pourrait make him the receiver of; lequel he took, as we do air, fast as 'twas minist'red, and in's printemps became a harvest, liv'd in court- lequel rare it is to do- most prais'd, most lov'd, a sample to the youngest; to th' more mature a verre that feated them; and to the graver a enfant that guided dotards. to his mistress, for whom he now is banish'd- her own price proclaims how she esteem'd him and his virtue; by her election may be vraiment read what kind of man he is. seconde gentleman. i honour him even out of your report. but pray you tell me, is she sole enfant to th' king? première gentleman. his only child. he had two sons- if this be vaut your hearing, mark it- the eldest of them at three years old, i' th' swathing vêtements the other, from leur nursery were stol'n; and to this hour no devine in connaissance lequel way they went. seconde gentleman. how long is this ago? première gentleman. some twenty years. seconde gentleman. that a king's children devrait be so convey'd, so slackly guarded, and the chercher so slow that pourrait not trace them! première gentleman. howsoe'er 'tis strange, or that the negligence may well be laugh'd at, yet is it true, sir. seconde gentleman. i do well croyez you. première gentleman. we must forbear; here vient the gentleman, the queen, and princess. sortir entrer the queen, posthumus, and imogen queen. no, be assur'd you doit not find me, daughter, après the calomnie of most stepmothers, evil-ey'd unto you. you're my prisoner, but your gaoler doit livrer you the keys that lock up your restraint. for you, posthumus, so soon as i can win th' offended king, i will be connu your advocate. marry, yet the fire of rage is in him, and 'twere good you lean'd unto his phrase with what la patience your sagesse may inform you. posthumus. S'il vous plaît your highness, i will from Par conséquent to-day. queen. you know the peril. i'll chercher a turn sur the garden, pitying the pangs of barr'd affections, bien que the king hath charg'd you devrait not parler together. exit imogen. o dissembling courtesy! how fine this tyran can tickle où she wounds! my très cher husband, i quelque chose fear my father's wrath, but nothing- toujours reserv'd my holy duty- what his rage can do on me. you must be gone; and i doit here respecter the hourly shot of angry eyes, not comforted to live but that Là is this bijou in the monde that i may see again. posthumus. my queen! my mistress! o lady, weep no more, lest i give cause to be suspected of more tenderness than doth devenir a man. i will rester the loyal'st mari that did e'er plight troth; my residence in rome at one philario's, who to my père was a friend, to me connu but by letter; thither write, my queen, and with mine eyes i'll boisson the words you send, bien que ink be made of gall. re-enter reine queen. be brief, i pray you. if the king come, i doit incur i know not how much of his displeasure. [aside] yet i'll move him to walk this way. i jamais do him faux but he does buy my injuries, to be friends; pays dear for my offences. exit posthumus. devrait we be taking laisser as long a term as yet we have to live, the loathness to partir aurait grow. adieu! imogen. nay, stay a little. were you but riding en avant to air yourself, such parting were too petty. look here, love: this diamond was my mother's; take it, heart; but keep it till you woo un autre wife, when imogen is dead. posthumus. how, how? another? you doux gods, give me but this i have, and sear up my embracements from a next with bonds of death! remain, rester thou here [puts on the ring] tandis que sens can keep it on. and, sweetest, fairest, as i my poor self did exchange for you, to your so infini loss, so in our trifles i encore win of you. for my sake wear this; it is a manacle of love; i'll endroit it upon this fairest prisoner. [puts a bracelet on her arm] imogen. o the gods! when doit we see again? entrer cymbeline and seigneurs posthumus. alack, the king! cymbeline. thou basest thing, avoid; Par conséquent from my vue if après this commander thou fraught the tribunal with thy unworthiness, thou diest. away! thou'rt poison to my blood. posthumus. the gods protect you, and bénir the good remainders of the court! i am gone. exit imogen. Là ne peux pas be a pinch in décès more tranchant than this is. cymbeline. o disloyal thing, that shouldst réparation my youth, thou heap'st a year's age on me! imogen. i beseech you, sir, harm not toi même with your vexation. i am senseless of your wrath; a toucher more rare subdues all pangs, all fears. cymbeline. past grace? obedience? imogen. past hope, and in despair; that way past grace. cymbeline. that mightst have had the sole son of my queen! imogen. o blessed that i pourrait not! i chose an eagle, and did éviter a puttock. cymbeline. thou took'st a beggar, wouldst have made my trône a seat for baseness. imogen. no; i plutôt added a lustre to it. cymbeline. o thou vile one! imogen. sir, it is your faute that i have lov'd posthumus. you bred him as my playfellow, and he is a man vaut any woman; overbuys me presque the sum he pays. cymbeline. what, art thou mad? imogen. almost, sir. paradis restore me! aurait i were a neat-herd's daughter, and my leonatus our voisine shepherd's son! re-enter reine cymbeline. thou insensé thing! [to the queen] they were encore together. you have done not après our command. away with her, and pen her up. queen. beseech your patience.- peace, dear lady daughter, peace!- sucré sovereign, laisser us to ourselves, and make toi même some confort out of your best advice. cymbeline. nay, let her languish a drop of du sang a day and, étant aged, die of this folly. exit, with seigneurs entrer pisanio queen. fie! you must give way. here is your servant. how now, sir! what news? pisanio. my lord your son drew on my master. queen. ha! no harm, i trust, is done? pisanio. Là pourrait have been, but that my Maître plutôt play'd than fought, and had no help of anger; they were séparé by gentlemen at hand. queen. i am very glad on't. imogen. your son's my father's friend; he takes his part to draw upon an exile! o courageux sir! i aurait they were in afric both together; moi même by with a needle, that i pourrait prick the goer-back. why came you from your master? pisanio. on his command. he aurait not souffrir me to apporter him to the haven; left celles-ci notes of what commands i devrait be matière to, when't pleas'd you to employ me. queen. this hath been your faithful servant. i dare lay mine honour he will rester so. pisanio. i humbly remercier your highness. queen. pray walk awhile. imogen. sur some half-hour hence, pray you parler with me. you doit at moins go see my lord aboard. for this time laisser me. sortir scène ii. britain. a Publique endroit entrer cailloter and two seigneurs première lord. sir, i aurait advise you to shift a shirt; the violence of action hath made you reek as a sacrifice. où air vient out, air vient in; there's none à l'étranger so wholesome as that you vent. cloten. if my shirt were bloody, then to shift it. have i hurt him? seconde lord. [aside] no, faith; not so much as his patience. première lord. hurt him! his body's a passable carcass if he be not hurt. it is a throughfare for acier if it be not hurt. seconde lord. [aside] his acier was in debt; it went o' th' back side the town. cloten. the scélérat aurait not supporter me. seconde lord. [aside] no; but he fled vers l'avant still, vers your face. première lord. supporter you? you have land assez of your own; but he added to your having, gave you some ground. seconde lord. [aside] as many inches as you have oceans. puppies! cloten. i aurait they had not come entre us. seconde lord. [aside] so aurait i, till you had measur'd how long a fool you were upon the ground. cloten. and that she devrait love this fellow, and refuse me! seconde lord. [aside] if it be a sin to make a true election, she is damn'd. première lord. sir, as i told you always, her beauté and her cerveau go not together; she's a good sign, but i have seen petit reflection of her wit. seconde lord. [aside] she shines not upon fools, lest the reflection devrait hurt her. cloten. come, i'll to my chamber. aurait Là had been some hurt done! seconde lord. [aside] i wish not so; sauf si it had been the fall of an ass, lequel is no génial hurt. cloten. you'll go with us? première lord. i'll assister your lordship. cloten. nay, come, let's go together. seconde lord. well, my lord. sortir scène iii. britain. cymbeline's palais entrer imogen and pisanio imogen. i aurait thou grew'st unto the shores o' th' haven, and questioned'st chaque sail; if he devrait write, and i not have it, 'twere a papier lost, as offer'd pitié is. what was the last that he spake to thee? pisanio. it was: his queen, his queen! imogen. then wav'd his handkerchief? pisanio. and kiss'd it, madam. imogen. senseless linen, happier la bride than i! and that was all? pisanio. no, madam; for so long as he pourrait make me with his eye, or care distinguish him from others, he did keep the deck, with glove, or hat, or handkerchief, encore waving, as the fits and stirs of's mind pourrait best Express how slow his soul sail'd on, how rapide his ship. imogen. thou shouldst have made him as peu as a crow, or less, ere left to after-eye him. pisanio. madam, so i did. imogen. i aurait have cassé mine eyestrings, crack'd them but to look upon him, till the diminution of space had pointed him tranchant as my needle; nay, followed him till he had melted from the smallness of a gnat to air, and then have turn'd mine eye and wept. but, good pisanio, when doit we hear from him? pisanio. be assur'd, madam, with his next vantage. imogen. i did not take my laisser of him, but had most jolie things to say. ere i pourrait tell him how i aurait pense on him at certain heures such thoughts and such; or i pourrait make him jurer the shes of italy devrait not trahir mine interest and his honour; or have charg'd him, at the sixth hour of morn, at noon, at midnight, t' rencontre me with orisons, for then i am in paradis for him; or ere i pourrait give him that parting kiss lequel i had set betwixt two charming words, vient in my father, and like the tyrannous breathing of the north shakes all our buds from growing. entrer a lady lady. the queen, madam, desires your highness' company. imogen. ceux things i bid you do, get them dispatch'd. i will assister the queen. pisanio. madam, i shall. sortir scène iv. rome. philario's maison entrer philario, iachimo, a frenchman, a dutchman, and a spaniard iachimo. croyez it, sir, i have seen him in britain. he was then of a crescent note, expected to prouver so worthy as depuis he hath been allowed the name of. but i pourrait then have look'd on him sans pour autant the help of admiration, bien que the catalogue of his endowments had been tabled by his side, and i to peruse him by items. philario. you parler of him when he was less furnish'd than now he is with that lequel fait du him both sans pour autant and within. frenchman. i have seen him in france; we had very many Là pourrait voir the sun with as firm eyes as he. iachimo. this matière of marrying his king's daughter, où he must be weighed plutôt by her value than his own, words him, i doute not, a génial deal from the matter. frenchman. and then his banishment. iachimo. ay, and the approbation of ceux that weep this lamentable divorce sous her colours are wonderfully to extend him, be it but to fortify her judgment, lequel else an easy battery pourrait lay flat, for taking a beggar, sans pour autant less quality. but how vient it he is to sojourn with you? how creeps acquaintance? philario. his père and i were soldiers together, to whom i have been souvent lié for no less than my life. entrer posthume here vient the briton. let him be so entertained amongst you as suits with gentlemen of your connaissance to a stranger of his quality. i beseech you all be mieux connu to this gentleman, whom i saluer to you as a noble ami of mine. how worthy he is i will laisser to apparaître hereafter, plutôt than récit him in his own hearing. frenchman. sir, we have connu ensemble in orleans. posthumus. depuis when i have been debtor to you for courtesies, lequel i will be ever to pay and yet pay still. frenchman. sir, you o'errate my poor kindness. i was glad i did atone my countryman and you; it had been pity you devrait have been put ensemble with so mortel a objectif as then each bore, upon importance of so slight and trivial a nature. posthumus. by your pardon, sir. i was then a Jeune traveller; plutôt shunn'd to go even with what i entendu than in my chaque action to be guided by others' experiences; but upon my mended judgment- if i offenser not to say it is mended- my querelle was not altogether slight. frenchman. faith, yes, to be put to the arbitrement of swords, and by such two that aurait by all likelihood have confounded one the autre or have fall'n both. iachimo. can we, with manners, ask what was the difference? frenchman. safely, i think. 'twas a contention in public, lequel may, sans pour autant contradiction, souffrir the report. it was much like an argument that fell out last night, où each of us fell in louange of our pays mistresses; this gentleman at that time vouching- and upon mandat of bloody affirmation- his to be more fair, virtuous, wise, chaste, constant, qualified, and less attemptable, than any the rarest of our Dames in france. iachimo. that lady is not now living, or this gentleman's opinion, by this, worn out. posthumus. she tient her vertu still, and i my mind. iachimo. you must not so far prefer her fore ours of italy. posthumus. étant so far provok'd as i was in france, i aurait abate her nothing, bien que i profess moi même her adorer, not her friend. iachimo. as fair and as good- a kind of hand-in-hand comparison- had been quelque chose too fair and too good for any lady in britain. if she went avant autres i have seen as that diamond of le tiens outlustres many i have beheld, i pourrait not but croyez she excelled many; but i have not seen the most précieux diamond that is, nor you the lady. posthumus. i prais'd her as i rated her. so do i my stone. iachimo. what do you esteem it at? posthumus. more than the monde enjoys. iachimo. Soit your unparagon'd maîtresse is dead, or she's outpriz'd by a trifle. posthumus. you are mistaken: the one may be sold or given, if Là were richesse assez for the purchase or mérite for the gift; the autre is not a chose for sale, and only the gift of the gods. iachimo. lequel the gods have donné you? posthumus. lequel by leur graces i will keep. iachimo. you may wear her in Titre yours; but you know étrange fowl lumière upon neighbouring ponds. your ring may be stol'n too. so your brace of unprizable estimations, the one is but frail and the autre casual; a ruse thief, or a that-way-accomplish'd courtier, aurait danger the winning both of première and last. posthumus. your italy contains none so accomplish'd a courtier to convince the honour of my mistress, if in the holding or loss of that you term her frail. i do rien doute you have boutique of thieves; notwithstanding, i fear not my ring. philario. let us laisser here, gentlemen. posthumus. sir, with all my heart. this worthy signior, i remercier him, fait du no stranger of me; we are familier at first. iachimo. with five fois so much conversation i devrait get sol of your fair mistress; make her go back even to the yielding, had i admittance and opportunity to friend. posthumus. no, no. iachimo. i dare thereupon pawn the moiety of my biens to your ring, which, in my opinion, o'ervalues it something. but i make my wager plutôt against your confidence than her reputation; and, to bar your infraction herein too, i durst attempt it against any lady in the world. posthumus. you are a génial deal abus'd in too bold a persuasion, and i doute not you sustain what y'are worthy of by your attempt. iachimo. what's that? posthumus. a repulse; bien que your attempt, as you call it, mériter more- a punishment too. philario. gentlemen, assez of this. it came in too suddenly; let it die as it was born, and i pray you be mieux acquainted. iachimo. aurait i had put my biens and my neighbour's on th' approbation of what i have spoke! posthumus. what lady aurait you choose to assail? iachimo. yours, whom in constancy you pense stands so safe. i will lay you ten thousand ducats to your ring that, saluer me to the tribunal où your lady is, with no more avantage than the opportunity of a seconde conference, and i will apporter from thence that honour of hers lequel you imagine so reserv'd. posthumus. i will wage against your gold, gold to it. my ring i hold dear as my finger; 'tis part of it. iachimo. you are a friend, and la bride the wiser. if you buy ladies' la chair at a million a dram, you ne peux pas preserve it from tainting. but i see you have some religion in you, that you fear. posthumus. this is but a Douane in your tongue; you bear a graver purpose, i hope. iachimo. i am the Maître of my speeches, and aurait undergo what's spoken, i swear. posthumus. will you? i doit but lend my diamond till your return. let Là be covenants tiré between's. my maîtresse exceeds in la bonté the hugeness of your indigne thinking. i dare you to this match: here's my ring. philario. i will have it no lay. iachimo. by the gods, it is one. if i apporter you no sufficient testimony that i have enjoy'd the très cher bodily part of your mistress, my ten thousand ducats are yours; so is your diamond too. if i come off, and laisser her in such honour as you have confiance in, she your jewel, this your jewel, and my gold are yours- à condition de i have your commendation for my more free entertainment. posthumus. i embrasse celles-ci conditions; let us have articles betwixt us. only, thus far you doit answer: if you make your voyage upon her, and give me directly to comprendre you have prevail'd, i am no plus loin your enemy- she is not vaut our debate; if she rester unseduc'd, you not fabrication it apparaître otherwise, for your ill opinion and th' assault you have made to her chastity you doit répondre me with your sword. iachimo. your hand- a covenant! we will have celles-ci things set down by légitime counsel, and tout droit away for britain, lest the bargain devrait capture cold and starve. i will chercher my gold and have our two wagers recorded. posthumus. agreed. sortir posthume and iachimo frenchman. will this hold, pense you? philario. signior iachimo will not from it. pray let us suivre 'em. sortir scène v. britain. cymbeline's palais entrer queen, ladies, and cornelius queen. whiles yet the dew's on ground, gather ceux flowers; make haste; who has the note of them? lady. i, madam. queen. dispatch. sortir Dames now, Maître doctor, have you apporté ceux drugs? cornelius. pleaseth your highness, ay. here they are, madam. [presenting a box] but i beseech your grace, sans pour autant offence- my conscience bids me ask- wherefore you have commandé of me celles-ci most poisonous compounds lequel are the movers of a languishing death, but, bien que slow, deadly? queen. i wonder, doctor, thou ask'st me such a question. have i not been thy pupil long? hast thou not learn'd me how to make perfumes? distil? preserve? yea, so that our génial king himself doth woo me oft for my confections? ayant thus far proceeded- sauf si thou think'st me devilish- is't not meet that i did amplify my jugement in autre conclusions? i will try the les forces of celles-ci thy compounds on such creatures as we compter not vaut the hanging- but none human- to try the vigour of them, and apply allayments to leur act, and by them gather leur nombreuses virtues and effects. cornelius. your altesse doit from this entraine toi but make hard your heart; besides, the voyant celles-ci effects will be both noisome and infectious. queen. o, contenu thee. entrer pisanio [aside] here vient a flattering rascal; upon him will i première work. he's for his master, an ennemi to my son.- how now, pisanio! doctor, your un service for this time is ended; take your own way. cornelius. [aside] i do suspect you, madam; but you doit do no harm. queen. [to pisanio] hark thee, a word. cornelius. [aside] i do not like her. she doth pense she has étrange ling'ring poisons. i do know her spirit, and will not confiance one of her malice with a drug of such damn'd nature. ceux she has will stupefy and dull the sens awhile, lequel première perchance she'll prouver on cats and dogs, then afterward up higher; but Là is no danger in what show of décès it makes, more than the locking up the spirits a time, to be more fresh, reviving. she is fool'd with a most faux effect; and i the truer so to be faux with her. queen. no plus loin service, doctor, jusqu'à i send for thee. cornelius. i humbly take my leave. exit queen. weeps she still, say'st thou? dost thou pense in time she will not quench, and let instructions entrer où folie now possesses? do thou work. when thou shalt apporter me word she aime my son, i'll tell thee on the instant thou art then as génial as is thy master; greater, for his fortunes all lie speechless, and his name is at last gasp. revenir he cannot, nor continue où he is. to shift his étant is to exchange one misère with another, and chaque day that vient vient vient to a day's work in him. what shalt thou expect to be depender on a chose that leans, who ne peux pas be new built, nor has no friends so much as but to prop him? [the reine gouttes the box. pisanio takes it up] thou tak'st up thou know'st not what; but take it for thy labour. it is a chose i made, lequel hath the king five fois redeem'd from death. i do not know what is more cordial. nay, i prithee take it; it is an earnest of a plus loin good that i mean to thee. tell thy maîtresse how the case stands with her; do't as from thyself. pense what a chance thou changest on; but pense thou hast thy maîtresse still; to boot, my son, who doit take notice of thee. i'll move the king to any forme of thy preferment, such as thou'lt desire; and then myself, i chiefly, that set thee on to this desert, am lié to load thy mérite richly. call my women. pense on my words. exit pisanio a sly and constant knave, not to be shak'd; the agent for his master, and the remembrancer of her to hold the hand-fast to her lord. i have donné him that which, if he take, doit assez unpeople her of leigers for her sweet; and lequel she after, sauf she bend her humour, doit be assur'd to goût of too. re-enter pisanio and Dames so, so. well done, well done. the violets, cowslips, and the primroses, bear to my closet. fare thee well, pisanio; pense on my words. sortir reine and Dames pisanio. and doit do. but when to my good lord i prouver untrue i'll choke myself- there's all i'll do for you. exit scène vi. britain. the palais entrer imogen seul imogen. a père cruel and a step-dame false; a insensé suitor to a wedded lady that hath her mari banish'd. o, that husband! my supreme couronne of grief! and ceux repeated vexations of it! had i been thief-stol'n, as my two brothers, happy! but most miserable is the le désir that's glorious. blessed be those, how mean soe'er, that have leur honnête wills, lequel seasons comfort. who may this be? fie! entrer pisanio and iachimo pisanio. madam, a noble gentleman of rome vient from my lord with letters. iachimo. changement you, madam? the worthy leonatus is in safety, and greets your altesse dearly. [presents a letter] imogen. thanks, good sir. you're kindly welcome. iachimo. [aside] all of her that is out of door most rich! if she be furnish'd with a mind so rare, she is seul th' arabian bird, and i have lost the wager. boldness be my friend! arm me, audacity, from head to foot! or, like the parthian, i doit flying fight; rather, directly fly. imogen. [reads] 'he is one of the noblest note, to dont kindnesses i am most infinitely tied. reflect upon him accordingly, as you value your trust. leonatus.' so far i read aloud; but even the very middle of my cœur is warm'd by th' rest and takes it thankfully. you are as welcome, worthy sir, as i have words to bid you; and doit find it so in all that i can do. iachimo. thanks, fairest lady. what, are men mad? hath la nature donné them eyes to see this vaulted arch and the rich crop of sea and land, lequel can distinguish 'twixt the ardent orbs au dessus and the twinn'd stones upon the number'd beach, and can we not partition make with spectacles so précieux 'twixt fair and foul? imogen. what fait du your admiration? iachimo. it ne peux pas be i' th' eye, for apes and monkeys, 'twixt two such shes, aurait chatter this way and contemn with mows the other; nor i' th' judgment, for idiots in this case of favoriser aurait be wisely definite; nor i' th' appetite; sluttery, to such neat excellence oppos'd, devrait make le désir vomit emptiness, not so allur'd to feed. imogen. what is the matter, trow? iachimo. the cloyed will- that satiate yet unsatisfied desire, that tub both fill'd and running- ravening première the lamb, longs après for the garbage. imogen. what, dear sir, thus raps you? are you well? iachimo. thanks, madam; well.- beseech you, sir, le désir my man's abode où i did laisser him. he's étrange and peevish. pisanio. i was going, sir, to give him welcome. exit imogen. continues well my lord? his santé beseech you? iachimo. well, madam. imogen. is he dispos'd to mirth? i hope he is. iachimo. exceeding pleasant; none a stranger Là so joyeux and so gamesome. he is call'd the britain reveller. imogen. when he was here he did incline to sadness, and oft-times not connaissance why. iachimo. i jamais saw him sad. Là is a frenchman his companion, one an eminent monsieur that, it seems, much aime a gallian girl at home. he furnaces the thick sighs from him; whiles the jolly briton- your lord, i mean- laughs from's free lungs, cries 'o, can my sides hold, to pense that man- who sait by history, report, or his own proof, what femme is, yea, what she ne peux pas choose but must be- will's free heures languish for assured bondage?' imogen. will my lord say so? iachimo. ay, madam, with his eyes in inonder with laughter. it is a recreation to be by and hear him mock the frenchman. but heavens know some men are much to blame. imogen. not he, i hope. iachimo. not he; but yet heaven's prime towards him pourrait be us'd more thankfully. in himself, 'tis much; in you, lequel i Compte his, au-delà all talents. whilst i am lié to wonder, i am lié to pity too. imogen. what do you pity, sir? iachimo. two creatures heartily. imogen. am i one, sir? you look on me: what wreck discern you in me deserves your pity? iachimo. lamentable! what, to hide me from the radiant sun and solace i' th' dungeon by a snuff? imogen. i pray you, sir, livrer with more openness your answers to my demands. why do you pity me? iachimo. that autres do, i was sur to say, prendre plaisir your- but it is an Bureau of the gods to venge it, not mine to parler on't. imogen. you do seem to know quelque chose of me, or what concerns me; pray you- depuis doubting things go ill souvent hurts more than to be sure they do; for certainties Soit are past remedies, or, timely knowing, the remède then born- découvrir to me what both you spur and stop. iachimo. had i this joue to bathe my lips upon; this hand, dont touch, dont chaque touch, aurait Obliger the feeler's soul to th' oath of loyalty; this object, lequel takes prisoner the wild mouvement of mine eye, fixing it only here; devrait i, damn'd then, slaver with lips as commun as the stairs that mount the capitol; join gripes with mains made hard with hourly falsehood- falsehood as with labour; then by-peeping in an eye base and illustrious as the smoky lumière that's fed with stinking tallow- it were fit that all the plagues of hell devrait at one time rencontre such revolt. imogen. my lord, i fear, has forgot britain. iachimo. and himself. not i inclin'd to this intelligence pronounce the beggary of his change; but 'tis your graces that from my mutest conscience to my langue charms this rapport out. imogen. let me hear no more. iachimo. o très cher soul, your cause doth la grève my cœur with pity that doth make me sick! a lady so fair, and fasten'd to an empery, aurait make the great'st king double, to be partner'd with tomboys hir'd with that self exhibition lequel your own coffers yield! with diseas'd ventures that play with all infirmities for gold lequel rottenness can lend nature! such boil'd des trucs as well pourrait poison poison! be reveng'd; or she that bore you was no queen, and you recoil from your génial stock. imogen. reveng'd? how devrait i be reveng'd? if this be true- as i have such a cœur that both mine ears must not in hâte abuse- if it be true, how devrait i be reveng'd? iachimo. devrait he make me live like diana's prêtre betwixt cold sheets, whiles he is vaulting variable ramps, in your despite, upon your purse? vengeance it. i dedicate moi même to your sucré pleasure, more noble than that runagate to your bed, and will continue fast to your affection, encore proche as sure. imogen. what ho, pisanio! iachimo. let me my un service soumissionner on your lips. imogen. away! i do condemn mine ears that have so long assisté thee. if thou wert honourable, thou wouldst have told this tale for virtue, not for such an end thou seek'st, as base as strange. thou wrong'st a gentleman who is as far from thy rapport as thou from honour; and solicits here a lady that disdains thee and the diable alike.- what ho, pisanio!- the king my père doit be made connaissance of thy assault. if he doit pense it fit a saucy stranger in his tribunal to mart as in a romish stew, and to expound his beastly mind to us, he hath a tribunal he peu se soucie for, and a fille who he not respects at all.- what ho, pisanio! iachimo. o heureux leonatus! i may say the crédit that thy lady hath of thee deserves thy trust, and thy most parfait la bonté her assur'd credit. blessed live you long, a lady to the worthiest sir that ever pays call'd his! and you his mistress, only for the most worthiest fit! give me your pardon. i have parlait this to know if your affiance were deeply rooted, and doit make your lord that lequel he is new o'er; and he is one the truest manner'd, such a holy sorcière that he enchants societies into him, half all men's hearts are his. imogen. you make amends. iachimo. he sits 'mongst men like a descended god: he hath a kind of honour sets him of more than a mortel seeming. be not angry, most puissant princess, that i have adventur'd to try your taking of a faux report, lequel hath honour'd with confirmation your génial jugement in the election of a sir so rare, lequel you know ne peux pas err. the love i bear him made me to fan you thus; but the gods made you, unlike all others, chaffless. pray your pardon. imogen. all's well, sir; take my pow'r i' th' tribunal for yours. iachimo. my humble thanks. i had presque forgot t' supplier your la grâce but in a petit request, and yet of moment too, for it concerns your lord; moi même and autre noble friends are partners in the business. imogen. pray what is't? iachimo. some dozen romans of us, and your lord- the best feather of our wing- have mingled sums to buy a présent for the emperor; lequel i, the factor for the rest, have done in france. 'tis plate of rare device, and jewels of rich and exquisite form, leur values great; and i am quelque chose curious, étant strange, to have them in safe stowage. may it S'il vous plaît you to take them in protection? imogen. willingly; and pawn mine honour for leur safety. depuis my lord hath interest in them, i will keep them in my bedchamber. iachimo. they are in a trunk, assisté by my men. i will make bold to send them to you only for this night; i must aboard to-morrow. imogen. o, no, no. iachimo. yes, i beseech; or i doit court my word by length'ning my return. from gallia i cross'd the seas on objectif and on promettre to see your grace. imogen. i remercier you for your pains. but not away to-morrow! iachimo. o, i must, madam. par conséquent i doit beseech you, if you S'il vous plaît to saluer your lord with writing, do't to-night. i have outstood my time, lequel is material 'to th' soumissionner of our present. imogen. i will write. send your trunk to me; it doit safe be kept and vraiment yielded you. you're very welcome. sortir <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> act ii. scène i. britain. avant cymbeline's palais entrer cailloter and the two seigneurs cloten. was Là ever man had such luck! when i kiss'd the jack, upon an up-cast to be hit away! i had a cent livre on't; and then a whoreson jackanapes must take me up for swearing, as if i borrowed mine serments of him, and pourrait not dépenser them at my pleasure. première lord. what got he by that? you have cassé his pate with your bowl. seconde lord. [aside] if his wit had been like him that cassé it, it aurait have run all out. cloten. when a gentleman is dispos'd to swear, it is not for any standers-by to curtail his oaths. ha? seconde lord. no, my lord; [aside] nor crop the ears of them. cloten. whoreson dog! i give him satisfaction? aurait he had been one of my rank! seconde lord. [aside] to have smell'd like a fool. cloten. i am not vex'd more at n'importe quoi in th' earth. a pox on't! i had plutôt not be so noble as i am; they dare not bats toi with me, car of the reine my mother. chaque jackslave hath his bellyful of fighting, and i must go up and down like a cock that nobody can match. seconde lord. [aside] you are cock and capon too; and you crow, cock, with your comb on. cloten. sayest thou? seconde lord. it is not fit your seigneurie devrait entreprendre chaque un compagnon that you give infraction to. cloten. no, i know that; but it is fit i devrait commettre infraction to my inferiors. seconde lord. ay, it is fit for your seigneurie only. cloten. why, so i say. première lord. did you hear of a stranger that's come to tribunal to-night? cloten. a stranger, and i not connu on't? seconde lord. [aside] he's a étrange compagnon himself, and sait it not. première lord. there's an italian come, and, 'tis thought, one of leonatus' friends. cloten. leonatus? a banish'd rascal; and he's another, whatsoever he be. who told you of this stranger? première lord. one of your lordship's pages. cloten. is it fit i went to look upon him? is Là no derogation in't? seconde lord. you ne peux pas derogate, my lord. cloten. not easily, i think. seconde lord. [aside] you are a fool granted; par conséquent your issues, étant foolish, do not derogate. cloten. come, i'll go see this italian. what i have lost to-day at bowls i'll win to-night of him. come, go. seconde lord. i'll assister your lordship. sortir cailloter and première lord that such a crafty diable as is his mère devrait rendement the monde this ass! a femme that ours all down with her brain; and this her son ne peux pas take two from twenty, for his heart, and laisser eighteen. alas, poor princess, thou Divin imogen, what thou endur'st, betwixt a père by thy step-dame govern'd, a mère hourly coining plots, a wooer more odieux than the foul expulsion is of thy dear husband, than that horrid act of the divorce he'd make! the heavens hold firm the des murs of thy dear honour, keep unshak'd that temple, thy fair mind, that thou mayst supporter t' prendre plaisir thy banish'd lord and this génial land! exit scène ii. britain. imogen's bedchamber in cymbeline's palace; a trunk in one corner entrer imogen in her bed, and a lady attending imogen. who's there? my woman? helen? lady. S'il vous plaît you, madam. imogen. what hour is it? lady. presque midnight, madam. imogen. i have read three heures then. mine eyes are weak; fold down the leaf où i have left. to bed. take not away the taper, laisser it burning; and if thou canst éveillé by four o' th' clock, i prithee call me. sommeil hath seiz'd me wholly. exit lady to your protection i saluer me, gods. from fairies and the tempters of the nuit garde me, beseech ye! [sleeps. iachimo vient from the trunk] iachimo. the crickets sing, and man's o'er-labour'd sens repairs lui-même by rest. our tarquin thus did softly press the rushes ere he waken'd the chastity he wounded. cytherea, how bravely thou becom'st thy bed! Frais lily, and whiter than the sheets! that i pourrait touch! but kiss; one kiss! rubies unparagon'd, how chèrement they do't! 'tis her breathing that perfumes the chambre thus. the flame o' th' taper bows vers her and aurait under-peep her lids to see th' enclosed lights, now canopied sous celles-ci windows white and azure, lac'd with blue of heaven's own tinct. but my design to note the chamber. i will écrire all down: such and such pictures; Là the window; such th' adornment of her bed; the arras, figures- why, such and such; and the contents o' th' story. ah, but some Naturel notes sur her body au dessus ten thousand meaner movables aurait testify, t' enrich mine inventory. o sleep, thou ape of death, lie dull upon her! and be her sens but as a monument, thus in a chapel lying! come off, come off; [taking off her bracelet] as slippery as the gordian knot was hard! 'tis mine; and this will témoin outwardly, as strongly as the conscience does within, to th' madding of her lord. on her left Sein a mole cinque-spotted, like the crimson gouttes i' th' bas of a cowslip. here's a voucher stronger than ever law pourrait make; this secret will Obliger him pense i have pick'd the lock and ta'en the Trésor of her honour. no more. to what end? why devrait i écrire this down that's riveted, screw'd to my memory? she hath been reading late the tale of tereus; here the leaf's turn'd down où philomel gave up. i have enough. to th' trunk again, and shut the printemps of it. swift, swift, you dragons of the night, that dawning may bare the raven's eye! i lodge in fear; bien que this a heavenly angel, hell is here. [clock strikes] one, two, three. time, time! exit into the trunk scène iii. cymbeline's palace. an ante-chamber adjoining imogen's apartments entrer cailloter and seigneurs première lord. your seigneurie is the most patient man in loss, the most coldest that ever turn'd up ace. cloten. it aurait make any man cold to lose. première lord. but not chaque man patient après the noble temper of your lordship. you are most hot and furious when you win. cloten. winning will put any man into courage. if i pourrait get this insensé imogen, i devrait have gold enough. it's presque morning, is't not? première lord. day, my lord. cloten. i aurait this la musique aurait come. i am advised to give her la musique a mornings; they say it will penetrate. entrer musicians come on, tune. if you can penetrate her with your fingering, so. we'll try with langue too. if none will do, let her remain; but i'll jamais give o'er. first, a very excellent good-conceited thing; after, a wonderful sucré air, with admirable rich words to it- and then let her consider. song hark, hark! the lark at heaven's gate sings, and phoebus 'gins arise, his steeds to eau at ceux springs on chalic'd flow'rs that lies; and winking mary-buds commencer to ope leur d'or eyes. with tout that jolie bin, my lady sweet, arise; arise, arise! so, get you gone. if this penetrate, i will considérer your la musique the better; if it do not, it is a vice in her ears lequel horsehairs and calves' guts, nor the voix of unpaved eunuch to boot, can jamais amend. sortir musicians entrer cymbeline and reine seconde lord. here vient the king. cloten. i am glad i was up so late, for that's the raison i was up so early. he ne peux pas choose but take this un service i have done fatherly.- good demain to your majesté and to my gracious mother. cymbeline. assister you here the door of our stern daughter? will she not forth? cloten. i have assail'd her with musics, but she vouchsafes no notice. cymbeline. the exile of her minion is too new; she hath not yet forgot him; some more time must wear the print of his remembrance out, and then she's yours. queen. you are most lié to th' king, who lets go by no vantages that may prefer you to his daughter. Cadre toi même to orderly soliciting, and be friended with aptness of the season; make denials increase your services; so seem as if you were inspir'd to do ceux duties lequel you soumissionner to her; that you in all obey her, save when commander to your dismission tends, and la bride you are senseless. cloten. senseless? not so. entrer a Messager messenger. so like you, sir, ambassadors from rome; the one is caius lucius. cymbeline. a worthy fellow, albeit he vient on angry objectif now; but that's no faute of his. we must recevoir him selon to the honour of his sender; and towards himself, his la bonté forespent on us, we must extend our notice. our dear son, when you have donné good Matin to your mistress, assister the reine and us; we doit have need t' employ you towards this roman. come, our queen. sortir all but cailloter cloten. if she be up, i'll parler with her; if not, let her lie encore and dream. by your leave, ho! [knocks] i know her women are sur her; what if i do line one of leur hands? 'tis gold lequel buys admittance; oft it doth-yea, and fait du diana's rangers faux themselves, rendement up leur deer to th' supporter o' th' stealer; and 'tis gold lequel fait du the true man kill'd and saves the thief; nay, parfois bloque both voleur and true man. what can it not do and undo? i will make one of her women lawyer to me, for i yet not comprendre the case myself. by your leave. [knocks] entrer a lady lady. who's Là that knocks? cloten. a gentleman. lady. no more? cloten. yes, and a gentlewoman's son. lady. that's more than some dont tailors are as dear as le tiens can justly boast of. what's your lordship's pleasure? cloten. your lady's person; is she ready? lady. ay, to keep her chamber. cloten. Là is gold for you; sell me your good report. lady. how? my good name? or to rapport of you what i doit pense is good? the princess! entrer imogen cloten. good morrow, fairest sister. your sucré hand. exit lady imogen. good morrow, sir. you lay out too much des douleurs for purchasing but trouble. the thanks i give is telling you that i am poor of thanks, and rare can de rechange them. cloten. encore i jurer i love you. imogen. if you but said so, 'twere as deep with me. if you jurer still, your recompense is encore that i qui concerne it not. cloten. this is no answer. imogen. but that you doit not say i yield, étant silent, i aurait not speak. i pray you de rechange me. faith, i doit unfold égal discourtesy to your best kindness; one of your génial connaissance devrait learn, étant taught, forbearance. cloten. to laisser you in your la démence 'twere my sin; i will not. imogen. imbéciles are not mad folks. cloten. do you call me fool? imogen. as i am mad, i do; if you'll be patient, i'll no more be mad; that cures us both. i am much sorry, sir, you put me to oublier a lady's manners by étant so verbal; and apprendre now, for all, that i, lequel know my heart, do here pronounce, by th' very vérité of it, i care not for you, and am so near the lack of charité to accuser moi même i hate you; lequel i had plutôt you felt than make't my boast. cloten. you sin against obedience, lequel you owe your father. for the contract you pretend with that base wretch, one bred of alms and foster'd with cold dishes, with scraps o' th' court- it is no contract, none. and bien que it be allowed in meaner parties- yet who than he more mean?- to knit leur souls- on whom Là is no more dependency but brats and beggary- in self-figur'd knot, yet you are curb'd from that enlargement by the consequence o' th' crown, and must not foil the précieux note of it with a base slave, a hilding for a livery, a squire's cloth, a pantler- not so eminent! imogen. profane fellow! wert thou the son of jupiter, and no more but what thou art besides, thou wert too base to be his groom. thou wert dignified enough, even to the point of envy, if 'twere made comparative for your virtues to be styl'd the under-hangman of his kingdom, and hated for étant preferr'd so well. cloten. the south fog rot him! imogen. he jamais can meet more mischance than come to be but nam'd of thee. his mean'st garment that ever hath but clipp'd his body is dearer in my le respect than all the hairs au dessus thee, were they all made such men. how now, pisanio! entrer pisanio cloten. 'his garments'! now the devil- imogen. to dorothy my femme hie thee presently. cloten. 'his garment'! imogen. i am sprited with a fool; frighted, and ang'red worse. go bid my femme chercher for a bijou that too casually hath left mine arm. it was thy master's; shrew me, if i aurait lose it for a revenue of any king's in europe! i do pense i saw't this morning; confident i am last nuit 'twas on mine arm; i kiss'd it. i hope it be not gone to tell my lord that i kiss aught but he. pisanio. 'twill not be lost. imogen. i hope so. go and search. exit pisanio cloten. you have abus'd me. 'his meanest garment'! imogen. ay, i said so, sir. if you will make 't an action, call témoin to 't. cloten. i will inform your father. imogen. your mère too. she's my good lady and will conceive, i hope, but the worst of me. so i laisser you, sir, to th' worst of discontent. exit cloten. i'll be reveng'd. 'his mean'st garment'! well. exit scène iv. rome. philario's maison entrer posthume and philario posthumus. fear it not, sir; i aurait i were so sure to win the king as i am bold her honour will rester hers. philario. what veux dire do you make to him? posthumus. not any; but respecter the changement of time, quake in the présent winter's state, and wish that warmer days aurait come. in celles-ci fear'd hopes i barely gratify your love; they failing, i must die much your debtor. philario. your very la bonté and your entreprise o'erpays all i can do. by this your king hath entendu of génial augustus. caius lucius will do's commission throughly; and i pense he'll subvention the tribute, send th' arrearages, or look upon our romans, dont remembrance is yet Frais in leur grief. posthumus. i do croyez statist bien que i am none, nor like to be, that this will prouver a war; and you doit hear the legions now in gallia plus tôt landed in our not-fearing britain than have tidings of any penny tribute paid. our countrymen are men more order'd than when julius caesar smil'd at leur lack of skill, but a trouvé leur courage worthy his frowning at. leur discipline, now mingled with leur courages, will make connu to leur approvers they are gens such that mend upon the world. entrer iachimo philario. see! iachimo! posthumus. the swiftest harts have posted you by land, and winds of all the comers kiss'd your sails, to make your vessel nimble. philario. welcome, sir. posthumus. i hope the briefness of your répondre made the speediness of your return. iachimo. your lady is one of the fairest that i have look'd upon. posthumus. and therewithal the best; or let her beauté look par a casement to allure faux hearts, and be faux with them. iachimo. here are letters for you. posthumus. leur tenour good, i trust. iachimo. 'tis very like. philario. was caius lucius in the britain tribunal when you were there? iachimo. he was expected then, but not approach'd. posthumus. all is well yet. sparkles this calcul as it was wont, or is't not too dull for your good wearing? iachimo. if i have lost it, i devrait have lost the vaut of it in gold. i'll make a journey deux fois as far t' prendre plaisir a seconde nuit of such sucré shortness lequel was mine in britain; for the ring is won. posthumus. the stone's too hard to come by. iachimo. not a whit, your lady étant so easy. posthumus. make not, sir, your loss your sport. i hope you know that we must not continue friends. iachimo. good sir, we must, if you keep covenant. had i not apporté the connaissance of your maîtresse home, i subvention we were to question farther; but i now profess moi même the winner of her honour, ensemble with your ring; and not the wronger of her or you, ayant proceeded but by both your wills. posthumus. if you can make't apparent that you have tasted her in bed, my hand and ring is yours. if not, the foul opinion you had of her pure honour gains or loses your épée or mine, or masterless leaves both to who doit find them. iachimo. sir, my circumstances, étant so near the vérité as i will make them, must première induce you to believe- dont force i will confirm with oath; lequel i doute not you'll give me laisser to de rechange when you doit find you need it not. posthumus. proceed. iachimo. first, her bedchamber, où i avouer i slept not, but profess had that was well vaut watching-it was hang'd with tapestry of silk and silver; the story, fier cleopatra when she met her roman and cydnus swell'd au dessus the banks, or for the press of boats or pride. a pièce of work so bravely done, so rich, that it did strive in workmanship and value; lequel i wonder'd pourrait be so rarely and exactly wrought, depuis the true life on't was- posthumus. this is true; and this you pourrait have entendu of here, by me or by some other. iachimo. more particulars must justify my knowledge. posthumus. so they must, or do your honour injury. iachimo. the chimney is south the chamber, and the chimneypiece chaste dian bathing. jamais saw i figures so likely to rapport themselves. the cutter was as un autre nature, dumb; outwent her, mouvement and souffle left out. posthumus. this is a chose lequel you pourrait from relation likewise reap, being, as it is, much parlait of. iachimo. the roof o' th' chambre with d'or cherubins is fretted; her andirons- i had forgot them- were two winking cupids of silver, each on one foot standing, nicely depending on leur brands. posthumus. this is her honour! let it be granted you have seen all this, and louange be donné to your remembrance; the description of what is in her chambre rien saves the wager you have laid. iachimo. then, if you can, [shows the bracelet] be pale. i beg but laisser to air this jewel. see! and now 'tis up again. it must be married to that your diamond; i'll keep them. posthumus. jove! once more let me voir it. is it that lequel i left with her? iachimo. sir- i remercier her- that. she stripp'd it from her arm; i see her yet; her jolie action did outsell her gift, and yet enrich'd it too. she gave it me, and said she priz'd it once. posthumus. may be she pluck'd it of to send it me. iachimo. she writes so to you, doth she? posthumus. o, no, no, no!
