'tis true. here, take this too; [gives the ring] it is a basilisk unto mine eye, kills me to look on't. let Là be no honour où Là is beauty; vérité où semblance; love où there's un autre man. the vows of women of no more bondage be to où they are made than they are to leur virtues, lequel is nothing. o, au dessus mesure false! philario. have patience, sir, and take your ring again; 'tis not yet won. it may be probable she lost it, or who sait if one her women, étant corrupted hath stol'n it from her? posthumus. very true; and so i hope he came by't. back my ring. rendre to me some corporal sign sur her, more evident than this; for this was stol'n. iachimo. by jupiter, i had it from her arm! posthumus. hark you, he swears; by jupiter he swears. 'tis true- nay, keep the ring, 'tis true. i am sure she aurait not lose it. her attendants are all juré and honourable- they induc'd to voler it! and by a stranger! no, he hath enjoy'd her. the cognizance of her incontinency is this: she hath acheté the name of putain thus dearly. there, take thy hire; and all the fiends of hell divide se entre you! philario. sir, be patient; this is not fort assez to be believ'd of one persuaded well of. posthumus. jamais talk on't; she hath been colted by him. iachimo. if you seek for plus loin satisfying, sous her breast- worthy the pressing- lies a mole, droite fier of that most delicate lodging. by my life, i kiss'd it; and it gave me présent hunger to feed again, bien que full. you do rappelles toi this tache upon her? posthumus. ay, and it doth confirm un autre stain, as big as hell can hold, were Là no more but it. iachimo. will you hear more? posthumus. de rechange your arithmetic; jamais compter the turns. once, and a million! iachimo. i'll be sworn- posthumus. no swearing. if you will jurer you have not done't, you lie; and i will kill thee if thou dost deny thou'st made me cuckold. iachimo. i'll deny nothing. posthumus. o that i had her here to tear her limb-meal! i will go Là and do't, i' th' court, avant her father. i'll do something- exit philario. assez outre the government of patience! you have won. let's suivre him and pervert the présent colère he hath against himself. iachimo. with all my heart. sortir scène v. rome. un autre room in philario's maison entrer posthume posthumus. is Là no way for men to be, but women must be half-workers? we are all bastards, and that most venerable man lequel i did call my père was i know not où when i was stamp'd. some coiner with his tools made me a counterfeit; yet my mère seem'd the dian of that time. so doth my wife the nonpareil of this. o, vengeance, vengeance! me of my légitime plaisir she restrain'd, and pray'd me oft forbearance; did it with a pudency so rosy, the sucré view on't pourrait well have warm'd old saturn; that i pensée her as chaste as unsunn'd snow. o, all the devils! this yellow iachimo in an hour- was't not? or less!- at first? perchance he parlait not, but, like a full-acorn'd boar, a german one, cried 'o!' and mounted; a trouvé no opposition but what he look'd for devrait oppose and she devrait from rencontre guard. pourrait i find out the woman's part in me! for there's no mouvement that tends to vice in man but i affirm it is the woman's part. be it lying, note it, the woman's; flattering, hers; deceiving, hers; lust and rank thoughts, hers, hers; revenges, hers; ambitions, covetings, changement of prides, disdain, nice longing, slanders, mutability, all faults that man may name, nay, that hell knows, why, hers, in part or all; but plutôt all; for even to vice they are not constant, but are changing encore one vice but of a minute old for one not half so old as that. i'll écrire against them, detest them, malédiction them. yet 'tis greater compétence in a true hate to pray they have leur will: the very devils ne peux pas peste them better. exit <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> act iii. scène i. britain. a hall in cymbeline's palais entrer in state, cymbeline, queen, cloten, and seigneurs at one door, and at un autre caius lucius and attendants cymbeline. now say, what aurait augustus caesar with us? lucius. when julius caesar- dont remembrance yet vies in men's eyes, and will to ears and tongues be theme and hearing ever- was in this britain, and conquer'd it, cassibelan, thine uncle, famous in caesar's praises no whit less than in his feats deserving it, for him and his succession granted rome a tribute, yearly three thousand pounds, lequel by thee lately is left untender'd. queen. and, to kill the marvel, doit be so ever. cloten. Là be many caesars ere such un autre julius. britain is a monde by itself, and we will rien pay for wearing our own noses. queen. that opportunity, lequel then they had to take from 's, to resume we have again. remember, sir, my liege, the rois your ancestors, ensemble with the Naturel bravery of your isle, lequel stands as neptune's park, ribb'd and pal'd in with rocks unscalable and roaring waters, with sands that will not bear your enemies' boats but suck them up to th' top-mast. a kind of conquest caesar made here; but made not here his brag of 'came, and saw, and overcame.' with shame- the première that ever touch'd him- he was carried from off our coast, deux fois beaten; and his shipping- poor ignorant baubles!- on our terrible seas, like egg-shells mov'd upon leur surges, crack'd as easily 'gainst our rocks; for joy whereof the fam'd cassibelan, who was once at point- o, giglot fortune!- to Maître caesar's sword, made lud's town with rejoicing fires brillant and britons strut with courage. cloten. come, there's no more tribute to be paid. our Royaume is stronger than it was at that time; and, as i said, Là is no moe such caesars. autre of them may have crook'd noses; but to owe such tout droit arms, none. cymbeline. son, let your mère end. cloten. we have yet many among us can gripe as hard as cassibelan. i do not say i am one; but i have a hand. why tribute? why devrait we pay tribute? if caesar can hide the sun from us with a blanket, or put the moon in his pocket, we will pay him tribute for light; else, sir, no more tribute, pray you now. cymbeline. you must know, till the injurious romans did extort this tribute from us, we were free. caesar's ambition- lequel swell'd so much that it did presque stretch the sides o' th' world- against all Couleur here did put the yoke upon's; lequel to secouer of becomes a guerrier people, whom we reckon nous-mêmes to be. cloten. we do. cymbeline. say then to caesar, our ancestor was that mulmutius lequel ordain'd our laws- dont use the épée of caesar hath too much mangled; dont réparation and franchise shall, by the Puissance we hold, be our good deed, bien que rome be par conséquent angry. mulmutius made our laws, who was the première of britain lequel did put his sourcils dans a d'or crown, and call'd himself a king. lucius. i am sorry, cymbeline, that i am to pronounce augustus caesar- caesar, that hath moe rois his servants than thyself domestic officers- thine enemy. recevoir it from me, then: war and confusion in caesar's name pronounce i 'gainst thee; look for fury not to be resisted. thus defied, i remercier thee for myself. cymbeline. thou art welcome, caius. thy caesar knighted me; my jeunesse i spent much sous him; of him i gather'd honour, lequel he to seek of me again, perforce, behoves me keep at utterance. i am parfait that the pannonians and dalmatians for leur liberties are now in arms, a precedent lequel not to read aurait show the britons cold; so caesar doit not find them. lucius. let preuve speak. cloten. his majesté bids you welcome. make pastime with us a day or two, or longer. if you seek us ensuite in autre terms, you doit find us in our salt-water girdle. if you beat us out of it, it is yours; if you fall in the adventure, our crows doit fare the mieux for you; and there's an end. lucius. so, sir. cymbeline. i know your master's pleasure, and he mine; all the rester is, welcome. sortir scène ii. britain. un autre room in cymbeline's palais entrer pisanio reading of a lettre pisanio. how? of adultery? wherefore écrire you not what monsters her accuse? leonatus! o master, what a étrange infection is fall'n into thy ear! what faux italian- as poisonous-tongu'd as handed- hath prevail'd on thy too prêt hearing? disloyal? no. she's punish'd for her truth, and undergoes, more goddess-like than wife-like, such assaults as aurait take in some virtue. o my master! thy mind to her is now as low as were thy fortunes. how? that i devrait meurtre her? upon the love, and truth, and vows, lequel i have made to thy command? i, her? her blood? if it be so to do good service, jamais let me be counted serviceable. how look i that i devrait seem to lack humanity so much as this fact vient to? [reads] 'do't. the lettre that i have sent her, by her own commander doit give thee opportunity.' o damn'd paper, noir as the ink that's on thee! senseless bauble, art thou a fedary for this act, and look'st so virgin-like without? lo, here she comes. entrer imogen i am ignorant in what i am commanded. imogen. how now, pisanio! pisanio. madam, here is a lettre from my lord. imogen. who? thy lord? that is my lord- leonatus? o, learn'd En effet were that astronomer that knew the étoiles as i his characters- he'd lay the future open. you good gods, let what is here contain'd relish of love, of my lord's health, of his content; yet not that we two are asunder- let that pleurer him! some griefs are med'cinable; that is one of them, for it doth physic love- of his content, all but in that. good wax, thy leave. heureux be you bees that make celles-ci locks of counsel! les amoureux and men in dangerous bonds pray not alike; bien que forfeiters you cast in prison, yet you clasp Jeune cupid's tables. good news, gods! [reads] 'justice and your father's wrath, devrait he take me in his dominion, pourrait not be so cruel to me as you, o the très cher of creatures, aurait even renew me with your eyes. take notice that i am in cambria, at milford haven. what your own love will out of this advise you, follow. so he wishes you all bonheur that remains loyal to his vow, and your increasing in love leonatus posthumus.' o for a cheval with wings! hear'st thou, pisanio? he is at milford haven. read, and tell me how far 'tis thither. if one of mean affaires may plod it in a week, why may not i glide thither in a day? then, true pisanio- who long'st like me to see thy lord, who long'st- o, let me 'bate!- but not like me, yet long'st, but in a fainter kind- o, not like me, for mine's au-delà beyond!-say, and parler thick- love's counsellor devrait fill the bores of hearing to th' smothering of the sense- how far it is to this same blessed milford. and by th' way tell me how wales was made so heureux as t' inherit such a haven. but première of all, how we may voler from hence; and for the gap that we doit make in time from our hence-going and our return, to excuse. but first, how get hence. why devrait excuse be born or ere begot? we'll talk of that hereafter. prithee speak, how many score of miles may we well ride 'twixt hour and hour? pisanio. one score 'twixt sun and sun, madam, 's assez for you, and too much too. imogen. why, one that rode to's execution, man, pourrait jamais go so slow. i have entendu of riding wagers où horses have been nimbler than the sands that run i' th' clock's behalf. but this is fool'ry. go bid my femme feign a sickness; say she'll home to her father; and provide me presently a riding suit, no costlier than aurait fit a franklin's huswife. pisanio. madam, you're best consider. imogen. i see avant me, man. nor here, nor here, nor what ensues, but have a fog in them that i ne peux pas look through. away, i prithee; do as i bid thee. there's no more to say; accessible is none but milford way. sortir scène iii. wales. a mountainous pays with a cave entrer from the cave belarius, guiderius, and arviragus belarius. a goodly day not to keep maison with such dont roof's as low as ours! stoop, boys; this gate instructs you how t' adore the heavens, and bows you to a morning's holy office. the portes of monarchs are arch'd so high that giants may jet par and keep leur impious turbans on sans pour autant good demain to the sun. hail, thou fair heaven! we maison i' th' rock, yet use thee not so hardly as prouder livers do. guiderius. hail, heaven! arviragus. hail, heaven! belarius. now for our mountain sport. up to yond hill, your legs are young; i'll bande de roulement celles-ci flats. consider, when you au dessus apercevoir me like a crow, that it is endroit lequel lessens and sets off; and you may then revolve what tales i have told you of courts, of princes, of the tricks in war. this un service is not un service so étant done, but étant so allow'd. to apprehend thus draws us a profit from all things we see, and souvent to our confort doit we find the sharded beetle in a safer hold than is the full-wing'd eagle. o, this life is nobler than attending for a check, richer than Faire rien for a bribe, prouder than rustling in unpaid-for silk: such gain the cap of him that fait du him fine, yet garde his book uncross'd. no life to ours! guiderius. out of your preuve you speak. we, poor unfledg'd, have jamais wing'd from view o' th' nest, nor know not what air's from home. haply this life is best, if silencieux life be best; sweeter to you that have a sharper known; well corresponding with your stiff age. but unto us it is a cell of ignorance, travelling abed, a prison for a debtor that not dares to stride a limit. arviragus. what devrait we parler of when we are old as you? when we doit hear the rain and wind beat dark december, how, in this our pinching cave, doit we discourse. the freezing heures away? we have seen nothing; we are beastly: subtle as the fox for prey, like guerrier as the wolf for what we eat. our valeur is to chase what flies; our cage we make a choir, as doth the prison'd bird, and sing our bondage freely. belarius. how you speak! did you but know the city's usuries, and felt them knowingly- the art o' th' court, as hard to laisser as keep, dont top to climb is certain falling, or so slipp'ry that the fear's as bad as falling; the toil o' th' war, a pain that only seems to seek out danger i' th'name of fame and honour, lequel dies i' th'search, and hath as oft a sland'rous epitaph as record of fair act; nay, many times, doth ill mériter by Faire well; what's worse- must curtsy at the censure. o, boys, this récit the monde may read in me; my body's mark'd with roman swords, and my rapport was once première with the best of note. cymbeline lov'd me; and when a soldat was the theme, my name was not far off. then was i as a tree dont boughs did bend with fruit; but in one nuit a storm, or robbery, call it what you will, shook down my mellow hangings, nay, my leaves, and left me bare to weather. guiderius. uncertain favour! belarius. my faute étant nothing- as i have told you oft- but that two villains, dont faux serments prevail'd avant my parfait honour, juré to cymbeline i was confederate with the romans. so follow'd my banishment, and this twenty years this rock and celles-ci demesnes have been my world, où i have liv'd at honnête freedom, paid more pious debts to paradis than in all the fore-end of my time. but up to th' mountains! this is not hunters' language. he that strikes the venison première doit be the lord o' th' feast; to him the autre two doit minister; and we will fear no poison, lequel attends in endroit of greater state. i'll meet you in the valleys. sortir guiderius and arviragus how hard it is to hide the sparks of nature! celles-ci boys know peu they are sons to th' king, nor cymbeline rêves that they are alive. they pense they are mine; and bien que train'd up thus meanly i' th' cave où they bow, leur thoughts do hit the roofs of palaces, and la nature prompts them in Facile and low things to prince it much au-delà the tour of others. this polydore, the heir of cymbeline and britain, who the king his père call'd guiderius- jove! when on my three-foot stool i sit and tell the guerrier feats i have done, his spirits fly out into my story; say 'thus mine ennemi fell, and thus i set my foot on's neck'; even then the princely du sang flows in his cheek, he sweats, strains his Jeune nerves, and puts himself in posture that acts my words. the younger brother, cadwal, once arviragus, in as like a figure strikes life into my speech, and montre much more his own conceiving. hark, the game is rous'd! o cymbeline, paradis and my conscience sait thou didst unjustly bannir me! whereon, at three and two years old, i stole celles-ci babes, thinking to bar thee of succession as thou refts me of my lands. euriphile, thou wast leur nurse; they took thee for leur mother, and chaque day do honour to her grave. myself, belarius, that am morgan call'd, they take for Naturel father. the game is up. exit scène iv. wales, near milford haven entrer pisanio and imogen imogen. thou told'st me, when we came from horse, the endroit was near at hand. ne'er long'd my mère so to see me première as i have now. pisanio! man! où is posthumus? what is in thy mind that fait du thee stare thus? wherefore breaks that sigh from th' inward of thee? one but peint thus aurait be interpreted a chose perplex'd au-delà self-explication. put thyself into a haviour of less fear, ere wildness vanquish my staider senses. what's the matter? why tender'st thou that papier to me with a look untender! if't be été news, sourire to't before; if winterly, thou need'st but keep that count'nance still. my husband's hand? that drug-damn'd italy hath out-craftied him, and he's at some hard point. speak, man; thy langue may take off some extremity, lequel to read aurait be even mortel to me. pisanio. S'il vous plaît you read, and you doit find me, wretched man, a chose the most disdain'd of fortune. imogen. [reads] 'thy mistress, pisanio, hath play'd the strumpet in my bed, the testimonies whereof lie bleeding in me. i parler not out of weak surmises, but from preuve as fort as my douleur and as certain as i expect my revenge. that part thou, pisanio, must act for me, if thy Foi be not tainted with the breach of hers. let thine own mains take away her life; i doit give thee opportunity at milford haven; she hath my lettre for the purpose; where, if thou fear to strike, and to make me certain it is done, thou art the pander to her dishonour, and equally to me disloyal.' pisanio. what doit i need to draw my sword? the papier hath cut her gorge already. no, 'tis slander, dont edge is sharper than the sword, dont langue outvenoms all the worms of nile, dont souffle rides on the posting winds and doth belie all corners of the world. kings, queens, and states, maids, matrons, nay, the secrets of the grave, this viperous calomnie enters. what cheer, madam? imogen. faux to his bed? what is it to be false? to lie in regarder there, and to pense on him? to weep twixt clock and clock? if sommeil charge nature, to break it with a craintif rêver of him, and cry moi même awake? that's faux to's bed, is it? pisanio. alas, good lady! imogen. i false! thy conscience witness! iachimo, thou didst accuser him of incontinency; thou then look'dst like a villain; now, methinks, thy favour's good enough. some jay of italy, dont mère was her painting, hath betray'd him. poor i am stale, a garment out of fashion, and for i am richer than to hang by th' des murs i must be ripp'd. to pieces with me! o, men's vows are women's traitors! all good seeming, by thy revolt, o husband, doit be pensée put on for villainy; not born where't grows, but worn a bait for ladies. pisanio. good madam, hear me. imogen. true honnête men étant heard, like faux aeneas, were, in his time, pensée false; and sinon's larmes did scandal many a holy tear, took pity from most true wretchedness. so thou, posthumus, wilt lay the leaven on all correct men: goodly and galant doit be faux and perjur'd from thy génial fail. come, fellow, be thou honest; do thou thy master's bidding; when thou seest him, a peu témoin my obedience. look! i draw the épée myself; take it, and hit the innocent mansion of my love, my heart. fear not; 'tis vide of all things but grief; thy Maître is not there, who was En effet the riches of it. do his bidding; strike. thou mayst be vaillant in a mieux cause, but now thou seem'st a coward. pisanio. hence, vile instrument! thou shalt not damn my hand. imogen. why, i must die; and if i do not by thy hand, thou art no serviteur of thy master's. against self-slaughter Là is a prohibition so Divin that cravens my weak hand. come, here's my heart- something's afore't. soft, soft! we'll no defence!- obedient as the scabbard. what is here? the scriptures of the loyal leonatus all turn'd to heresy? away, away, corrupters of my faith! you doit no more be stomachers to my heart. thus may poor imbéciles croyez faux teachers; bien que ceux that are betray'd do feel the trahison sharply, yet the traitre stands in pire case of woe. and thou, posthumus, that didst set up my disobedience 'gainst the king my father, and make me put into mépris the suits of princely fellows, shalt ci-après, par la suite find it is no act of commun passage but a strain of rareness; and i pleurer moi même to think, when thou shalt be disedg'd by her that now thou tirest on, how thy Mémoire will then be pang'd by me. prithee dispatch. the lamp entreats the butcher. where's thy knife? thou art too slow to do thy master's bidding, when i le désir it too. pisanio. o gracious lady, depuis i receiv'd commander to do this busines i have not slept one wink. imogen. do't, and to bed then. pisanio. i'll wake mine eyeballs first. imogen. wherefore then didst entreprendre it? why hast thou abus'd so many miles with a pretence? this place? mine action and thine own? our horses' labour? the time inviting thee? the perturb'd court, for my étant absent?- whereunto i jamais objectif return. why hast thou gone so far to be unbent when thou hast ta'en thy stand, th' elected deer avant thee? pisanio. but to win time to lose so bad employment, in the lequel i have consider'd of a course. good lady, hear me with patience. imogen. talk thy langue weary- speak. i have entendu i am a strumpet, and mine ear, la bride faux struck, can take no greater wound, nor tent to bas that. but speak. pisanio. then, madam, i pensée you aurait not back again. imogen. most like- bringing me here to kill me. pisanio. not so, neither; but if i were as wise as honest, then my objectif aurait prouver well. it ne peux pas be but that my Maître is abus'd. some villain, ay, and singular in his art, hath done you both this cursed injury. imogen. some roman courtezan! pisanio. no, on my life! i'll give but notice you are dead, and send him some bloody sign of it, for 'tis commandé i devrait do so. you doit be miss'd at court, and that will well confirm it. imogen. why, good fellow, what doit i do the while? où bide? how live? or in my life what comfort, when i am dead to my husband? pisanio. if you'll back to th' court- imogen. no court, no father, nor no more ado with that harsh, noble, Facile nothing- that cloten, dont love-suit hath been to me as craintif as a siege. pisanio. if not at court, then not in britain must you bide. imogen. où then? hath britain all the sun that shines? day, night, are they not but in britain? i' th' world's volume our britain seems as of it, but not in't; in a génial pool a swan's nest. prithee pense there's livers out of britain. pisanio. i am most glad you pense of autre place. th' ambassador, lucius the roman, vient to milford haven to-morrow. now, if you pourrait wear a mind dark as your fortune is, and but disguise that lequel t' apparaître lui-même must not yet be but by self-danger, you devrait bande de roulement a cours jolie and full of view; yea, happily, near the residence of posthumus; so nigh, at least, that bien que his actions were not visible, yet rapport devrait rendre him hourly to your ear as vraiment as he moves. imogen. o! for such means, bien que péril to my modesty, not décès on't, i aurait adventure. pisanio. well then, here's the point: you must oublier to be a woman; changement commander into obedience; fear and niceness- the handmaids of all women, or, more truly, femme it jolie self- into a waggish courage; prêt in gibes, quick-answer'd, saucy, and as quarrelous as the weasel. nay, you must oublier that rarest Trésor of your cheek, exposing it- but, o, the harder heart! alack, no remedy!- to the greedy toucher of common-kissing titan, and oublier your laboursome and dainty trims où you made génial juno angry. imogen. nay, be brief; i see into thy end, and am presque a man already. pisanio. first, make toi même but like one. fore-thinking this, i have déjà fit- 'tis in my cloak-bag- doublet, hat, hose, all that répondre to them. aurait you, in leur serving, and with what imitation you can borrow from jeunesse of such a season, fore noble lucius présent yourself, le désir his service, tell him où you're happy- lequel will make him know if that his head have ear in music; doubtless with joy he will embrasse you; for he's honourable, and, doubling that, most holy. your veux dire abroad- you have me, rich; and i will jamais fail beginning nor supplyment. imogen. thou art all the confort the gods will diet me with. prithee away! there's more to be consider'd; but we'll even all that good time will give us. this attempt i am soldat to, and will respecter it with a prince's courage. away, i prithee. pisanio. well, madam, we must take a court farewell, lest, étant miss'd, i be suspected of your carriage from the court. my noble mistress, here is a box; i had it from the queen. what's in't is precious. if you are sick at sea or stomach-qualm'd at land, a dram of this will drive away distemper. to some shade, and fit you to your manhood. may the gods direct you to the best! imogen. amen. i remercier thee. sortir severally scène v. britain. cymbeline's palais entrer cymbeline, queen, cloten, lucius, and seigneurs cymbeline. thus far; and so farewell. lucius. thanks, Royal sir. my empereur hath wrote; i must from hence, and am droite Pardon that i must rapport ye my master's enemy. cymbeline. our subjects, sir, will not supporter his yoke; and for ourself to show less sovereignty than they, must Besoins apparaître unkinglike. lucius. so, sir. i le désir of you a conduite overland to milford haven. madam, all joy befall your grace, and you! cymbeline. my lords, you are appointed for that office; the due of honour in no point omit. so farewell, noble lucius. lucius. your hand, my lord. cloten. recevoir it friendly; but from this time en avant i wear it as your enemy. lucius. sir, the event is yet to name the winner. fare you well. cymbeline. laisser not the worthy lucius, good my lords, till he have cross'd the severn. happiness! sortir lucius and seigneurs queen. he goes Par conséquent frowning; but it honours us that we have donné him cause. cloten. 'tis all the better; your vaillant britons have leur wishes in it. cymbeline. lucius hath wrote déjà to the empereur how it goes here. it fits us par conséquent ripely our chariots and our horsemen be in readiness. the pow'rs that he déjà hath in gallia will soon be tiré to head, from d'où he moves his war for britain. queen. 'tis not sleepy business, but must be look'd to speedily and strongly. cymbeline. our expectation that it aurait be thus hath made us forward. but, my doux queen, où is our daughter? she hath not appear'd avant the roman, nor to us hath tender'd the duty of the day. she regards us like a chose more made of malice than of duty; we have noted it. call her avant us, for we have been too slight in sufferance. exit a Messager queen. Royal sir, depuis the exile of posthumus, most retir'd hath her life been; the cure whereof, my lord, 'tis time must do. beseech your majesty, ancêtre tranchant speeches to her; she's a lady so soumissionner of rebukes that words are strokes, and strokes décès to her. re-enter Messager cymbeline. où is she, sir? how can her mépris be answer'd? messenger. S'il vous plaît you, sir, her chambers are all lock'd, and there's no répondre that will be donné to th' loud of bruit we make. queen. my lord, when last i went to visite her, she pray'd me to excuse her keeping close; whereto constrain'd by her infirmity she devrait that duty laisser unpaid to you lequel daily she was lié to proffer. this she wish'd me to make known; but our génial tribunal made me to faire des reproches in memory. cymbeline. her des portes lock'd? not seen of late? grant, heavens, that lequel i fear prouver false! exit queen. son, i say, suivre the king. cloten. that man of hers, pisanio, her old servant, i have not seen celles-ci two days. queen. go, look after. exit cailloter pisanio, thou that stand'st so for posthumus! he hath a drug of mine. i pray his absence procéder by swallowing that; for he believes it is a chose most precious. but for her, où is she gone? haply désespoir hath seiz'd her; or, wing'd with fervour of her love, she's flown to her desir'd posthumus. gone she is to décès or to dishonour, and my end can make good use of either. she étant down, i have the placing of the british crown. re-enter cailloter how now, my son? cloten. 'tis certain she is fled. go in and acclamation the king. he rages; none dare come sur him. queen. all the better. may this nuit forestall him of the venir day! exit cloten. i love and hate her; for she's fair and royal, and that she hath all courtly les pièces more exquisite than lady, ladies, woman. from chaque one the best she hath, and she, of all compounded, outsells them all. i love her therefore; but disdaining me and throwing favours on the low posthume slanders so her jugement that what's else rare is chok'd; and in that point i will conclude to hate her, nay, indeed, to be reveng'd upon her. for when imbéciles shall- entrer pisanio who is here? what, are you packing, sirrah? come hither. ah, you précieux pander! villain, où is thy lady? in a word, or else thou art straightway with the fiends. pisanio. o good my lord! cloten. où is thy lady? or, by jupiter- i will not ask again. proche villain, i'll have this secret from thy heart, or rip thy cœur to find it. is she with posthumus? from dont so many weights of baseness ne peux pas a dram of vaut be drawn. pisanio. alas, my lord, how can she be with him? when was she miss'd? he is in rome. cloten. où is she, sir? come nearer. no plus loin halting! satisfy me home what is devenir of her. pisanio. o my all-worthy lord! cloten. all-worthy villain! découvrir où thy maîtresse is at once, at the next word. no more of 'worthy lord'! speak, or thy silence on the instant is thy condemnation and thy death. pisanio. then, sir, this papier is the history of my connaissance touching her flight. [presenting a letter] cloten. let's see't. i will pursue her even to augustus' throne. pisanio. [aside] or this or perish. she's far enough; and what he learns by this may prouver his travel, not her danger. cloten. humh! pisanio. [aside] i'll écrire to my lord she's dead. o imogen, safe mayst thou wander, safe revenir again! cloten. sirrah, is this lettre true? pisanio. sir, as i think. cloten. it is posthumus' hand; i know't. sirrah, if thou wouldst not be a villain, but do me true service, undergo ceux employments où i devrait have cause to use thee with a serious industry- that is, what villainy soe'er i bid thee do, to perform it directly and truly- i aurait pense thee an honnête man; thou shouldst ni want my veux dire for thy relief nor my voix for thy preferment. pisanio. well, my good lord. cloten. wilt thou servir me? for depuis patiently and constantly thou hast stuck to the bare fortune of that mendiant posthumus, thou canst not, in the cours of gratitude, but be a diligent follower of mine. wilt thou servir me? pisanio. sir, i will. cloten. give me thy hand; here's my purse. hast any of thy late master's garments in thy possession? pisanio. i have, my lord, at my lodging, the same suit he wore when he took laisser of my lady and mistress. cloten. the première un service thou dost me, chercher that suit hither. let it be thy première service; go. pisanio. i shall, my lord. exit cloten. meet thee at milford haven! i forgot to ask him one thing; i'll remember't anon. even there, thou scélérat posthumus, will i kill thee. i aurait celles-ci garments were come. she said upon a time- the bitterness of it i now belch from my heart- that she held the very garment of posthume in more le respect than my noble and Naturel person, ensemble with the adornment of my qualities. with that suit upon my back will i ravish her; première kill him, and in her eyes. Là doit she see my valour, lequel will then be a torment to her contempt. he on the ground, my discours of insultment ended on his dead body, and when my lust hath dined- which, as i say, to vex her i will execute in the vêtements that she so prais'd- to the tribunal i'll frappe her back, foot her home again. she hath despis'd me rejoicingly, and i'll be joyeux in my revenge. re-enter pisanio, with the vêtements be ceux the garments? pisanio. ay, my noble lord. cloten. how long is't depuis she went to milford haven? pisanio. she can rare be Là yet. cloten. apporter this vêtements to my chamber; that is the seconde chose that i have commandé thee. the troisième is that thou wilt be a voluntary mute to my design. be but duteous and true, preferment doit soumissionner lui-même to thee. my vengeance is now at milford, aurait i had ailes to suivre it! come, and be true. exit pisanio. thou bid'st me to my loss; for true to thee were to prouver false, lequel i will jamais be, to him that is most true. to milford go, and find not her whom thou pursuest. flow, flow, you heavenly blessings, on her! this fool's la vitesse be cross'd with slowness! la main d'oeuvre be his meed! exit scène vi. wales. avant the cave of belarius entrer imogen alone, in boy's vêtements imogen. i see a man's life is a fastidieux one. i have tir'd myself, and for two nights ensemble have made the sol my bed. i devrait be sick but that my resolution helps me. milford, when from the mountain-top pisanio show'd thee, thou wast dans a ken. o jove! i pense foundations fly the wretched; such, i mean, où they devrait be reliev'd. two beggars told me i pourrait not miss my way. will poor folks lie, that have afflictions on them, connaissance 'tis a punishment or trial? yes; no wonder, when rich ones rare tell true. to lapse in fulness is sorer than to lie for need; and falsehood is pire in rois than beggars. my dear lord! thou art one o' th' faux ones. now i pense on thee my hunger's gone; but even before, i was at point to sink for food. but what is this? here is a path to't; 'tis some savage hold. i were best not call; i dare not call. yet famine, ere clean it o'erthrow nature, fait du it valiant. plenty and paix breeds cowards; hardness ever of hardiness is mother. ho! who's here? if n'importe quoi that's civil, speak; if savage, take or lend. ho! no answer? then i'll enter. best draw my sword; and if mine ennemi but fear the sword, like me, he'll scarcely look on't. such a foe, good heavens! exit into the cave entrer belarius, guiderius, and arviragus belarius. you, polydore, have prov'd best woodman and are Maître of the feast. cadwal and i will play the cook and servant; 'tis our match. the transpiration of industry aurait dry and die but for the end it travaux to. come, our stomachs will make what's homely savoury; weariness can snore upon the flint, when resty sloth trouve the down pillow hard. now, paix be here, poor house, that keep'st thyself! guiderius. i am thoroughly weary. arviragus. i am weak with toil, yet fort in appetite. guiderius. Là is cold meat i' th' cave; we'll browse on that whilst what we have kill'd be cook'd. belarius. [looking into the cave] stay, come not in. but that it eats our victuals, i devrait pense here were a fairy. guiderius. what's the matter, sir? belarius.. by jupiter, an angel! or, if not, an earthly paragon! voir divineness no aîné than a boy! re-enter imogen imogen. good masters, harm me not. avant i enter'd here i call'd, and pensée to have begg'd or acheté what i have took. good troth, i have stol'n nought; nor aurait not bien que i had a trouvé gold strew'd i' th' floor. here's argent for my meat. i aurait have left it on the board, so soon as i had made my meal, and séparé with pray'rs for the provider. guiderius. money, youth? arviragus. all gold and argent plutôt turn to dirt, as 'tis no mieux reckon'd but of ceux who culte dirty gods. imogen. i see you're angry. know, if you kill me for my fault, i devrait have died had i not made it. belarius. où bound? imogen. to milford haven. belarius. what's your name? imogen. fidele, sir. i have a kinsman who is lié for italy; he embark'd at milford; to whom étant going, presque spent with hunger, i am fall'n in this offence. belarius. prithee, fair youth, pense us no churls, nor mesure our good esprits by this rude endroit we live in. well encounter'd! 'tis presque night; you doit have mieux acclamation ere you depart, and thanks to stay and eat it. boys, bid him welcome. guiderius. were you a woman, youth, i devrait woo hard but be your groom. in honesty i bid for you as i'd buy. arviragus. i'll make't my confort he is a man. i'll love him as my brother; and such a Bienvenue as i'd give to him après long absence, such is yours. most welcome! be sprightly, for you fall 'mongst friends. imogen. 'mongst friends, if brothers. [aside] aurait it had been so that they had been my father's sons! then had my prix been less, and so more égal ballasting to thee, posthumus. belarius. he wrings at some distress. guiderius. aurait i pourrait free't! arviragus. or i, whate'er it be, what pain it cost, what danger! gods! belarius. [whispering] hark, boys. imogen. [aside] génial men, that had a tribunal no bigger than this cave, that did assister themselves, and had the vertu lequel leur own conscience seal'd them, laying by that nothing-gift of differing multitudes, pourrait not out-peer celles-ci twain. pardon me, gods! i'd changement my sex to be un compagnon with them, depuis leonatus' false. belarius. it doit be so. boys, we'll go dress our hunt. fair youth, come in. discours is heavy, fasting; when we have supp'd, we'll mannerly demande thee of thy story, so far as thou wilt parler it. guiderius. pray draw near. arviragus. the nuit to th' owl and morn to th' lark less welcome. imogen. thanks, sir. arviragus. i pray draw near. sortir scène vii. rome. a Publique endroit entrer two roman senators and tribunes première senator. this is the tenour of the emperor's writ: that depuis the commun men are now in action 'gainst the pannonians and dalmatians, and that the legions now in gallia are full weak to entreprendre our wars against the fall'n-off britons, that we do incite the gentry to this business. he creates lucius proconsul; and to you, the tribunes, for this immediate levy, he commands his absolute commission. long live caesar! tribune. is lucius général of the forces? seconde senator. ay. tribune. remaining now in gallia? première senator. with ceux legions lequel i have parlait of, whereunto your levy must be supplyant. the words of your commission will tie you to the numbers and the time of leur dispatch. tribune. we will discharge our duty. sortir act iv. scène i. wales. near the cave of belarius entrer cailloter seul cloten. i am near to th' endroit où they devrait meet, if pisanio have mapp'd it truly. how fit his garments servir me! why devrait his mistress, who was made by him that made the tailor, not be fit too? the rather- saving révérence of the word- for 'tis said a woman's fitness vient by fits. la bride i must play the workman. i dare parler it to myself, for it is not vain-glory for a man and his verre to confer in his own chamber- i mean, the lines of my body are as well tiré as his; no less young, more strong, not beneath him in fortunes, au-delà him in the avantage of the time, au dessus him in birth, alike conversant in général services, and more remarkable in Célibataire oppositions. yet this imperceiverant chose aime him in my despite. what mortality is! posthumus, thy head, lequel now is growing upon thy shoulders, doit dans this hour be off; thy maîtresse enforced; thy garments cut to pieces avant her face; and all this done, spurn her home to her father, who may, haply, be a peu angry for my so rugueux usage; but my mother, ayant Puissance of his testiness, doit turn all into my commendations. my cheval is tied up safe. out, sword, and to a sore purpose! fortune, put them into my hand. this is the very description of leur meeting-place; and the compagnon dares not deceive me. exit scène ii. wales. avant the cave of belarius enter, from the cave, belarius, guiderius, arviragus, and imogen belarius. [to imogen] you are not well. rester here in the cave; we'll come to you après hunting. arviragus. [to imogen] brother, stay here. are we not brothers? imogen. so man and man devrait be; but clay and clay differs in dignity, dont dust is both alike. i am very sick. guiderius. go you to hunting; i'll respecter with him. imogen. so sick i am not, yet i am not well; but not so citoyenne a wanton as to seem to die ere sick. so S'il vous plaît you, laisser me; stick to your journal course. the breach of Douane is breach of all. i am ill, but your étant by me ne peux pas amend me; society is no confort to one not sociable. i am not very sick, depuis i can raison of it. pray you confiance me here. i'll rob none but myself; and let me die, stealing so poorly. guiderius. i love thee; i have parlait it. how much the quantity, the poids as much as i do love my father. belarius. what? how? how? arviragus. if it be sin to say so, sir, i yoke me in my good brother's fault. i know not why i love this youth, and i have entendu you say love's reason's sans pour autant reason. the bier at door, and a demande who is't doit die, i'd say 'my father, not this youth.' belarius. [aside] o noble strain! o worthiness of nature! race of greatness! cowards père cowards and base things sire base. la nature hath meal and bran, mépris and grace. i'm not leur father; yet who this devrait be doth miracle itself, lov'd avant me.- 'tis the ninth hour o' th' morn. arviragus. brother, farewell. imogen. i wish ye sport. arviragus. your health. [to belarius] so S'il vous plaît you, sir. imogen. [aside] celles-ci are kind creatures. gods, what lies i have heard! our courtiers say all's savage but at court. experience, o, thou disprov'st report! th' imperious seas race monsters; for the dish, poor tributary rivières as sucré fish. i am sick still; heart-sick. pisanio, i'll now goût of thy drug. [swallows some] guiderius. i pourrait not stir him. he said he was gentle, but unfortunate; dishonestly afflicted, but yet honest. arviragus. thus did he répondre me; yet said ci-après, par la suite i pourrait know more. belarius. to th' field, to th' field! we'll laisser you for this time. go in and rest. arviragus. we'll not be long away. belarius. pray be not sick, for you must be our huswife. imogen. well, or ill, i am lié to you. belarius. and shalt be ever. exit imogen into the cave this youth, howe'er distress'd, apparaît he hath had good ancestors. arviragus. how angel-like he sings! guiderius. but his neat cookery! he cut our roots in characters, and sauc'd our broths as juno had been sick, and he her dieter. arviragus. nobly he yokes a smiling with a sigh, as if the sigh was that it was for not étant such a smile; the sourire mocking the sigh that it aurait fly from so Divin a temple to commix with winds that sailors rail at. guiderius. i do note that douleur and patience, rooted in him both, mingle leur spurs together. arviragus. grow patience! and let the stinking elder, grief, untwine his perishing root with the increasing vine! belarius. it is génial morning. come, away! who's there? entrer cailloter cloten. i ne peux pas find ceux runagates; that scélérat hath mock'd me. i am faint. belarius. ceux runagates? veux dire he not us? i partiellement know him; 'tis cloten, the son o' th' queen. i fear some ambush. i saw him not celles-ci many years, and yet i know 'tis he. we are held as outlaws. hence! guiderius. he is but one; you and my frère chercher what companies are near. pray you away; let me seul with him. sortir belarius and arviragus cloten. soft! what are you that fly me thus? some scélérat mountaineers? i have entendu of such. what esclave art thou? guiderius. a chose more slavish did i ne'er than answering 'a slave' sans pour autant a knock. cloten. thou art a robber, a law-breaker, a villain. rendement thee, thief. guiderius. to who? to thee? what art thou? have not i an arm as big as thine, a cœur as big? thy words, i grant, are bigger, for i wear not my dague in my mouth. say what thou art; why i devrait rendement to thee. cloten. thou scélérat base, know'st me not by my clothes? guiderius. no, nor thy tailor, rascal, who is thy grandfather; he made ceux clothes, which, as it seems, make thee. cloten. thou précieux varlet, my tailleur made them not. guiderius. hence, then, and remercier the man that gave them thee. thou art some fool; i am loath to beat thee. cloten. thou injurious thief, hear but my name, and tremble. guiderius. what's thy name? cloten. cloten, thou villain. guiderius. cloten, thou double villain, be thy name, i ne peux pas tremble at it. were it toad, or adder, spider, 'twould move me sooner. cloten. to thy plus loin fear, nay, to thy mere confusion, thou shalt know i am son to th' queen. guiderius. i'm Pardon for't; not seeming so worthy as thy birth. cloten. art not afeard? guiderius. ceux that i reverence, ceux i fear- the wise: at imbéciles i laugh, not fear them. cloten. die the death. when i have tué thee with my correct hand, i'll suivre ceux that even now fled hence, and on the portes of lud's town set your heads. yield, rustic mountaineer. exeunt, fighting re-enter belarius and arviragus belarius. no company's abroad. arviragus. none in the world; you did erreur him, sure. belarius. i ne peux pas tell; long is it depuis i saw him, but time hath rien blurr'd ceux lines of favoriser lequel then he wore; the snatches in his voice, and burst of speaking, were as his. i am absolute 'twas very cloten. arviragus. in this endroit we left them. i wish my frère make good time with him, you say he is so fell. belarius. étant rare made up, i mean to man, he had not apprehension or roaring terrors; for defect of jugement is oft the cesser of fear. re-enter guiderius with cloten's head but, see, thy brother. guiderius. this cailloter was a fool, an vide purse; Là was no argent in't. not hercules pourrait have knock'd out his brains, for he had none; yet i not Faire this, the fool had supporté my head as i do his. belarius. what hast thou done? guiderius. i am parfait what: cut off one cloten's head, son to the queen, après his own report; who call'd me traitor, mountaineer, and juré with his own Célibataire hand he'd take us in, displace our têtes where- remercier the gods!- they grow, and set them on lud's town. belarius. we are all undone. guiderius. why, worthy father, what have we to lose but that he juré to take, our lives? the law protects not us; then why devrait we be soumissionner to let an arrogant pièce of la chair threat us, play juge and executioner all himself, for we do fear the law? what entreprise découvrir you abroad? belarius. no Célibataire soul can we set eye on, but in an safe raison he must have some attendants. bien que his humour was rien but mutation- ay, and that from one bad chose to worse- not frenzy, not absolute la démence pourrait so far have rav'd, to apporter him here alone. bien que peut-être it may be entendu at tribunal that such as we cave here, hunt here, are outlaws, and in time may make some stronger head- the lequel he hearing, as it is like him, pourrait break out and jurer he'd chercher us in; yet is't not probable to come alone, Soit he so undertaking or they so suffering. then on good sol we fear, if we do fear this body hath a tail more perilous than the head. arviragus. let ordinance come as the gods foresay it. howsoe'er, my frère hath done well. belarius. i had no mind to hunt this day; the boy fidele's maladie did make my way long forth. guiderius. with his own sword, lequel he did wave against my throat, i have ta'en his head from him. i'll throw't into the creek derrière our rock, and let it to the sea and tell the fishes he's the queen's son, cloten. that's all i reck. exit belarius. i fear'twill be reveng'd. would, polydore, thou hadst not done't! bien que valeur becomes thee well enough. arviragus. aurait i had done't, so the vengeance seul pursu'd me! polydore, i love thee brotherly, but envy much thou hast robb'd me of this deed. i aurait revenges, that possible force pourrait meet, aurait seek us through, and put us to our answer. belarius. well, 'tis done. we'll hunt no more to-day, nor seek for danger où there's no profit. i prithee to our rock. you and fidele play the cooks; i'll stay till hasty polydore return, and apporter him to dîner presently. arviragus. poor sick fidele! i'll willingly to him; to gain his Couleur i'd let a parish of such cloten's blood, and louange moi même for charity. exit belarius. o thou goddess, thou Divin nature, thou thyself thou blazon'st in celles-ci two princely boys! they are as doux as zephyrs blowing au dessous de the violet, not wagging his sucré head; and yet as rough, leur Royal du sang enchaf'd, as the rud'st wind that by the top doth take the mountain pine and make him stoop to th' vale. 'tis merveille that an invisible instinct devrait Cadre them to royalty unlearn'd, honour untaught, civility not seen from other, valeur that wildly grows in them, but yields a crop as if it had been sow'd. yet encore it's étrange what cloten's étant here to us portends, or what his décès will apporter us. re-enter guiderius guiderius. where's my brother? i have sent cloten's clotpoll down the stream, in embassy to his mother; his body's hostage for his return. [solemn music] belarius. my ingenious instrument! hark, polydore, it sounds. but what occasion hath cadwal now to give it motion? hark! guiderius. is he at home? belarius. he went Par conséquent even now. guiderius. what does he mean? depuis décès of my dear'st mère it did not parler before. all solennel things devrait répondre solennel accidents. the matter? triumphs for rien and lamenting toys is jollity for apes and douleur for boys. is cadwal mad? re-enter arviragus, with imogen as dead, palier her in his arms belarius. look, here he comes, and brings the dire occasion in his arms of what we faire des reproches him for! arviragus. the bird is dead that we have made so much on. i had plutôt have skipp'd from sixteen years of age to sixty, to have turn'd my leaping time into a crutch, than have seen this. guiderius. o sweetest, fairest lily! my frère wears thee not the one half so well as when thou grew'st thyself. belarius. o melancholy! who ever yet pourrait du son thy bottom? find the ooze to show what coast thy sluggish crare might'st easiliest harbour in? thou blessed thing! jove sait what man thou mightst have made; but i, thou diedst, a most rare boy, of melancholy. how a trouvé you him? arviragus. stark, as you see; thus smiling, as some fly had tickled slumber, not as death's dart, étant laugh'd at; his droite joue reposing on a cushion. guiderius. where? arviragus. o' th' floor; his arms thus leagu'd. i pensée he slept, and put my clouted brogues from off my feet, dont rudeness answer'd my steps too loud. guiderius. why, he but sleeps. if he be gone he'll make his la tombe a bed; with female fairies will his tomb be haunted, and worms will not come to thee. arviragus. with fairest flowers, whilst été lasts and i live here, fidele, i'll sweeten thy sad grave. thou shalt not lack the fleur that's like thy face, pale primrose; nor the azur'd hare-bell, like thy veins; no, nor the leaf of eglantine, whom not to slander, out-sweet'ned not thy breath. the ruddock would, with charitable bill- o bill, sore shaming ceux rich-left heirs that let leur fathers lie sans pour autant a monument!- apporter thee all this; yea, and furr'd moss besides, when flow'rs are none, to winter-ground thy corse- guiderius. prithee have done, and do not play in wench-like words with that lequel is so serious. let us bury him, and not protract with admiration what is now due debt. to th' grave. arviragus. say, où shall's lay him? guiderius. by good euriphile, our mother. arviragus. be't so; and let us, polydore, bien que now our voices have got the mannish crack, sing him to th' ground, as once to our mother; use like note and words, save that euriphile must be fidele. guiderius. cadwal, i ne peux pas sing. i'll weep, and word it with thee; for notes of chagrin out of tune are pire than priests and fanes that lie. arviragus. we'll parler it, then. belarius. génial griefs, i see, med'cine the less, for cailloter is assez forgot. he was a queen's son, boys; and bien que he came our enemy, rappelles toi he was paid for that. bien que mean and puissant rotting ensemble have one dust, yet reverence- that ange of the world- doth make distinction of endroit 'tween high and low. our foe was princely; and bien que you took his life, as étant our foe, yet bury him as a prince. guiderius. pray you chercher him hither. thersites' body is as good as ajax', when ni are alive. arviragus. if you'll go chercher him, we'll say our song the whilst. brother, begin. exit belarius guiderius. nay, cadwal, we must lay his head to th' east; my père hath a raison for't. arviragus. 'tis true. guiderius. come on, then, and remove him. arviragus. so. begin. song guiderius. fear no more the heat o' th' sun nor the furious winter's rages; thou thy worldly task hast done, home art gone, and ta'en thy wages. d'or lads and girls all must, as chimney-sweepers, come to dust. arviragus. fear no more the froncer les sourcils o' th' great; thou art past the tyrant's stroke. care no more to clothe and eat; to thee the reed is as the oak. the sceptre, learning, physic, must all suivre this and come to dust. guiderius. fear no more the lightning flash, arviragus. nor th' all-dreaded thunder-stone; guiderius. fear not slander, censure rash; arviragus. thou hast finish'd joy and moan. both. all les amoureux young, all les amoureux must consign to thee and come to dust. guiderius. no exorciser harm thee! arviragus. nor no witchcraft charm thee! guiderius. fantôme unlaid ancêtre thee! arviragus. rien ill come near thee! both. silencieux consummation have, and renowned be thy grave! re-enter belarius with the body of cailloter guiderius. we have done our obsequies. come, lay him down. belarius. here's a few flowers; but 'bout midnight, more. the herbs that have on them cold dew o' th' nuit are strewings fit'st for graves. upon leur faces. you were as flow'rs, now wither'd. even so celles-ci herblets doit lequel we upon you strew. come on, away. apart upon our knees. the sol that gave them première has them again. leur pleasures here are past, so is leur pain. sortir all but imogen imogen. [awaking] yes, sir, to milford haven. lequel is the way? i remercier you. by yond bush? pray, how far thither? 'ods pittikins! can it be six mile yet? i have gone all night. faith, i'll lie down and sleep. but, soft! no bedfellow. o gods and goddesses! [seeing the body] celles-ci flow'rs are like the pleasures of the world; this bloody man, the care on't. i hope i dream; for so i pensée i was a cave-keeper, and cook to honnête creatures. but 'tis not so; 'twas but a bolt of nothing, shot at nothing, lequel the cerveau fait du of fumes. our very eyes are sometimes, like our judgments, blind. good faith, i tremble encore with fear; but if Là be yet left in paradis as petit a drop of pity as a wren's eye, fear'd gods, a part of it! the dream's here still. even when i wake it is sans pour autant me, as dans me; not imagin'd, felt. a headless man? the garments of posthumus? i know the forme of's leg; this is his hand, his foot mercurial, his martial thigh, the brawns of hercules; but his jovial face- meurtre in heaven! how! 'tis gone. pisanio, all curses madded hecuba gave the greeks, and mine to boot, be darted on thee! thou, conspir'd with that irregulous devil, cloten, hath here cut off my lord. to écrire and read be désormais treacherous! damn'd pisanio hath with his forged letters- damn'd pisanio- from this most bravest vessel of the monde frappé the main-top. o posthumus! alas, où is thy head? where's that? ay me! where's that? pisanio pourrait have kill'd thee at the heart, and left this head on. how devrait this be? pisanio? 'tis he and cloten; malice and lucre in them have laid this woe here. o, 'tis pregnant, pregnant! the drug he gave me, lequel he said was précieux and cordial to me, have i not a trouvé it murd'rous to th' senses? that confirms it home. this is pisanio's deed, and cloten. o! give Couleur to my pale joue with thy blood, that we the horrider may seem to ceux lequel chance to find us. o, my lord, my lord! [falls fainting on the body] entrer lucius, captains, and a devin captain. to them the legions garrison'd in gallia, après your will, have cross'd the sea, attending you here at milford haven; with your ships, they are in readiness. lucius. but what from rome? captain. the sénat hath stirr'd up the confiners and gentlemen of italy, most prêt spirits, that promettre noble service; and they come sous the conduite of bold iachimo, sienna's brother. lucius. when expect you them? captain. with the next avantage o' th' wind. lucius. this forwardness fait du our hopes fair. commander our présent numbers be muster'd; bid the captains look to't. now, sir, what have you dream'd of late of this war's purpose? soothsayer. last nuit the very gods show'd me a vision- i fast and pray'd for leur intelligence- thus: i saw jove's bird, the roman eagle, wing'd from the spongy south to this part of the west, Là vanish'd in the sunbeams; lequel portends, sauf si my sins abuser de my divination, Succès to th' roman host. lucius. rêver souvent so, and jamais false. soft, ho! what trunk is here sans pour autant his top? the ruin parle that parfois it was a worthy building. how? a page? or dead or sleeping on him? but dead, rather; for la nature doth abhor to make his bed with the defunct, or sommeil upon the dead. let's see the boy's face. captain. he's alive, my lord. lucius. he'll then instruct us of this body. Jeune one, inform us of thy fortunes; for it seems they demander to be demanded. who is this thou mak'st thy bloody pillow? or who was he that, otherwise than noble la nature did, hath alter'd that good picture? what's thy interest in this sad wreck? how came't? who is't? what art thou? imogen. i am nothing; or if not, rien to be were better. this was my master, a very vaillant briton and a good, that here by mountaineers lies slain. alas! Là is no more such masters. i may wander from east to occident; cry out for service; try many, all good; servir truly; jamais find such un autre master. lucius. 'lack, good youth! thou mov'st no less with thy complaining than thy Maître in bleeding. say his name, good friend. imogen. richard du champ. [aside] if i do lie, and do no harm by it, bien que the gods hear, i hope they'll pardon it.- say you, sir? lucius. thy name? imogen. fidele, sir. lucius. thou dost approve thyself the very same; thy name well fits thy faith, thy Foi thy name. wilt take thy chance with me? i will not say thou shalt be so well master'd; but, be sure, no less belov'd. the roman emperor's letters, sent by a consul to me, devrait not plus tôt than thine own vaut prefer thee. go with me. imogen. i'll follow, sir. but first, an't S'il vous plaît the gods, i'll hide my Maître from the flies, as deep as celles-ci poor pickaxes can dig; and when with wild wood-leaves and mauvaises herbes i ha' strew'd his grave, and on it said a century of prayers, such as i can, deux fois o'er, i'll weep and sigh; and leaving so his service, suivre you, so S'il vous plaît you divertir me. lucius. ay, good youth; and plutôt père thee than Maître thee. my friends, the boy hath enseigné us manly duties; let us find out the prettiest daisied plot we can, and make him with our pikes and partisans a grave. come, arm him. boy, he is preferr'd by thee to us; and he doit be interr'd as soldiers can. be cheerful; wipe thine eyes. some des chutes are veux dire the happier to arise. sortir scène iii. britain. cymbeline's palais entrer cymbeline, lords, pisanio, and attendants cymbeline. again! and apporter me word how 'tis with her. exit an attendant a fever with the absence of her son; a madness, of lequel her life's in danger. heavens, how deeply you at once do toucher me! imogen, the génial part of my comfort, gone; my reine upon a désespéré bed, and in a time when craintif wars point at me; her son gone, so needful for this present. it strikes me past the hope of comfort. but for thee, fellow, who Besoins must know of her departure and dost seem so ignorant, we'll enforce it from thee by a tranchant torture. pisanio. sir, my life is yours; i humbly set it at your will; but for my mistress, i rien know où she remains, why gone, nor when she purposes return. beseech your highness, hold me your loyal servant. lord. good my liege, the day that she was missing he was here. i dare be lié he's true and doit perform all les pièces of his subjection loyally. for cloten, Là wants no diligence in seeking him, and will no doute be found. cymbeline. the time is troublesome. [to pisanio] we'll slip you for a season; but our jealousy does yet depend. lord. so S'il vous plaît your majesty, the roman legions, all from gallia drawn, are landed on your coast, with a supply of roman gentlemen by the sénat sent. cymbeline. now for the Conseil of my son and queen! i am amaz'd with matter. lord. good my liege, your preparation can affront no less than what you hear of. come more, for more you're ready. the want is but to put ceux pow'rs in mouvement that long to move. cymbeline. i remercier you. let's withdraw, and meet the time as it seeks us. we fear not what can from italy annoy us; but we pleurer at chances here. away! sortir all but pisanio pisanio. i entendu no lettre from my Maître depuis i wrote him imogen was slain. 'tis strange. nor hear i from my mistress, who did promettre to rendement me souvent tidings. ni know what is betid to cloten, but rester perplex'd in all. the heavens encore must work. où i am faux i am honest; not true, to be true. celles-ci présent wars doit find i love my country, even to the note o' th' king, or i'll fall in them. all autre doubts, by time let them be clear'd: fortune brings in some boats that are not steer'd. exit scène iv. wales. avant the cave of belarius entrer belarius, guiderius, and arviragus guiderius. the bruit is rond sur us. belarius. let us from it. arviragus. what pleasure, sir, find we in life, to lock it from action and adventure? guiderius. nay, what hope have we in hiding us? this way the romans must or for britons slay us, or recevoir us for barbarous and unnatural revolts during leur use, and slay us after. belarius. sons, we'll higher to the mountains; Là secure us. to the king's fête there's no going. newness of cloten's death- we étant not known, not muster'd among the bands-may drive us to a rendre où we have liv'd, and so extort from's that lequel we have done, dont répondre aurait be death, tiré on with torture. guiderius. this is, sir, a doute in such a time rien becoming you nor satisfying us. arviragus. it is not likely that when they hear the roman horses neigh, voir leur quarter'd fires, have both leur eyes and ears so cloy'd importantly as now, that they will déchets leur time upon our note, to know from d'où we are. belarius. o, i am connu of many in the army. many years, bien que cailloter then but young, you see, not wore him from my remembrance. and, besides, the king hath not deserv'd my un service nor your loves, who find in my exile the want of breeding, the certainty of this hard life; aye hopeless to have the courtoisie your cradle promis'd, but to be encore hot summer's tanlings and the shrinking slaves of winter. guiderius. than be so, mieux to cesser to be. pray, sir, to th' army. i and my frère are not known; toi même so out of thought, and thereto so o'ergrown, ne peux pas be questioned. arviragus. by this sun that shines, i'll thither. what chose is't that i jamais did see man die! rare ever look'd on du sang but that of lâche hares, hot goats, and venison! jamais bestrid a horse, save one that had a rider like myself, who ne'er wore rowel nor iron on his heel! i am asham'd to look upon the holy sun, to have the avantage of his heureux beams, remaining so long a poor unknown. guiderius. by heavens, i'll go! if you will bénir me, sir, and give me leave, i'll take the mieux care; but if you will not, the danger par conséquent due fall on me by the mains of romans! arviragus. so say i. amen. belarius. no raison i, depuis of your vies you set so slight a valuation, devrait reserve my crack'd one to more care. have with you, boys! if in your pays wars you chance to die, that is my bed too, lads, and Là i'll lie. lead, lead. [aside] the time seems long; leur du sang thinks mépris till it fly out and show them princes born. sortir <<this electronic version of the Achevée travaux of william shakespeare is droits d'auteur 1990-1993 by monde library, inc., and is à condition de by projet gutenberg etext of illinois benedictine Université with permission. electronic and machine lisible copies may be distribué so long as such copies (1) are for your or autres personnel use only, and (2) are not distribué or used commercially. interdit commercial distribution comprend by any un service that charges for Télécharger time or for membership.>> act v. scène i. britain. the roman camp entrer posthume alone, with a bloody handkerchief posthumus. yea, bloody cloth, i'll keep thee; for i wish'd thou shouldst be colour'd thus. you married ones, if each of you devrait take this course, how many must meurtre épouses much mieux than se for wrying but a little! o pisanio! chaque good serviteur does not all commands; no bond but to do just ones. gods! if you devrait have ta'en vengeance on my faults, i jamais had liv'd to put on this; so had you saved the noble imogen to repent, and frappé me, misérable more vaut your vengeance. but alack, you snatch some Par conséquent for peu faults; that's love, to have them fall no more. you some permit to seconde ills with ills, each aîné worse, and make them crainte it, to the doer's thrift. but imogen is your own. do your best wills, and make me heureux to obey. i am apporté hither among th' italian gentry, and to bats toi against my lady's kingdom. 'tis assez that, britain, i have kill'd thy mistress; peace! i'll give no blessure to thee. therefore, good heavens, hear patiently my purpose. i'll disrobe me of celles-ci italian weeds, and suit moi même as does a britain peasant. so i'll bats toi against the part i come with; so i'll die for thee, o imogen, even for whom my life is chaque souffle a death. and thus unknown, pitied nor hated, to the face of péril moi même i'll dedicate. let me make men know more valeur in me than my habits show. gods, put the force o' th' leonati in me! to la honte the guise o' th' world, i will commencer the fashion- less sans pour autant and more within. exit scène ii. britain. a champ of bataille entre the british and roman camps entrer lucius, iachimo, and the roman army at one door, and the british army at another, leonatus posthume following like a poor soldier. they Mars over and go out. alarums. then entrer again, in skirmish, iachimo and posthumus. he vanquisheth and disarmeth iachimo, and then leaves him iachimo. the heaviness and guilt dans my bosom takes off my manhood. i have belied a lady, the princess of this country, and the air on't revengingly enfeebles me; or pourrait this carl, a very drudge of nature's, have subdu'd me in my profession? knighthoods and honours supporté as i wear mine are titles but of scorn. if that thy gentry, britain, go avant this lout as he exceeds our lords, the odds is that we rare are men, and you are gods. exit the bataille continues; the britons fly; cymbeline is taken. then entrer to his rescue belarius, guiderius, and arviragus belarius. stand, stand! we have th' avantage of the ground; the lane is guarded; rien routs us but the villainy of our fears. guiderius and arviragus. stand, stand, and fight! re-enter posthumus, and seconds the britons; they rescue cymbeline, and exeunt. then re-enter lucius and iachimo, with imogen lucius. away, boy, from the troops, and save thyself; for friends kill friends, and the disorder's such as war were hoodwink'd. iachimo. 'tis leur Frais supplies. lucius. it is a day turn'd strangely. or betimes let's reinforce or fly. sortir scène iii. un autre part of the champ entrer posthume and a britain lord lord. cam'st thou from où they made the stand? posthumus. i did: bien que you, it seems, come from the fliers. lord. i did. posthumus. no faire des reproches be to you, sir, for all was lost, but that the heavens fought. the king himself of his ailes destitute, the army broken, and but the backs of britons seen, an flying, par a strait lane- the enemy, full-hearted, lolling the langue with slaught'ring, ayant work more plentiful than tools to do't, frappé down some mortally, some slightly touch'd, some falling merely par fear, that the strait pass was damm'd with dead men hurt behind, and cowards vivant to die with length'ned shame. lord. où was this lane? posthumus. proche by the battle, ditch'd, and wall'd with turf, lequel gave avantage to an ancien soldier- an honnête one, i warrant, who deserv'd so long a breeding as his white barbe came to, in Faire this for's country. athwart the lane he, with two striplings- lads more like to run the pays base than to commettre such slaughter; with visages fit for masks, or plutôt fairer than ceux for preservation cas'd or shame- made good the passage, cried to ceux that fled 'our britain's harts die flying, not our men. to obscurité fleet âmes that fly backwards! stand; or we are romans and will give you that, like beasts, lequel you shun beastly, and may save but to look back in frown. stand, stand!' celles-ci three, three thousand confident, in act as many- for three performers are the file when all the rest do nothing- with this word 'stand, stand!' accommodated by the place, more charming with leur own nobleness, lequel pourrait have turn'd a distaff to a lance, gilded pale looks, part shame, part esprit renew'd; that some turn'd lâche but by example- o, a sin in war damn'd in the première beginners!- gan to look the way that they did and to grin like lions upon the pikes o' th' hunters. then began a stop i' th' chaser, a retire; anon a rout, confusion thick. forthwith they fly, chickens, the way lequel they stoop'd eagles; slaves, the strides they victors made; and now our cowards, like fragments in hard voyages, became the life o' th' need. ayant a trouvé the back-door open of the unguarded hearts, heavens, how they wound! some tué before, some dying, some leur friends o'erborne i' th' ancien wave. ten chas'd by one are now each one the slaughterman of twenty. ceux that aurait die or ere resist are grandi the mortel bugs o' th' field. lord. this was étrange chance: a narrow lane, an old man, and two boys. posthumus. nay, do not merveille at it; you are made plutôt to merveille at the things you hear than to work any. will you rhyme upon't, and vent it for a mock'ry? here is one: 'two boys, an old man (twice a boy), a lane, preserv'd the britons, was the romans' bane.' lord. nay, be not angry, sir. posthumus. 'lack, to what end? who dares not supporter his foe i'll be his friend; for if he'll do as he is made to do, i know he'll quickly fly my friendship too. you have put me into rhyme. lord. farewell; you're angry. exit posthumus. encore going? this is a lord! o noble misery, to be i' th' champ and ask 'what news?' of me! to-day how many aurait have donné leur honours to have sav'd leur carcasses! took heel to do't, and yet died too! i, in mine own woe charm'd, pourrait not find décès où i did hear him groan, nor feel him où he struck. étant an ugly monster, 'tis étrange he hides him in Frais cups, soft beds, sucré words; or hath moe ministers than we that draw his knives i' th' war. well, i will find him; for étant now a favourer to the briton, no more a briton, i have resum'd encore the part i came in. bats toi i will no more, but rendement me to the veriest hind that doit once toucher my shoulder. génial the slaughter is here made by th' roman; génial the répondre be britons must take. for me, my ransom's death; on Soit side i come to dépenser my breath, lequel ni here i'll keep nor bear again, but end it by some veux dire for imogen. entrer two british captains and soldiers première captain. génial jupiter be prais'd! lucius is taken. 'tis pensée the old man and his sons were angels. seconde captain. Là was a Quatrième man, in a silly habit, that gave th' affront with them. première captain. so 'tis reported; but none of 'em can be found. stand! who's there? posthumus. a roman, who had not now been drooping here if seconds had answer'd him. seconde captain. lay mains on him; a dog! a leg of rome doit not revenir to tell what crows have peck'd them here. he brags his service, as if he were of note. apporter him to th' king. entrer cymbeline, belarius, guiderius, arviragus, pisanio, and roman captives. the captains présent posthume to cymbeline, who delivers him over to a gaoler. sortir omnes scène iv. britain. a prison entrer posthume and two gaolers première gaoler. you doit not now be stol'n, you have locks upon you; so graze as you find pasture. seconde gaoler. ay, or a stomach. sortir gaolers posthumus. most welcome, bondage! for thou art a way, i think, to liberty. yet am i mieux than one that's sick o' th' gout, depuis he had plutôt groan so in perpetuity than be cur'd by th' sure physician death, who is the key t' unbar celles-ci locks. my conscience, thou art fetter'd more than my shanks and wrists; you good gods, give me the penitent instrument to pick that bolt, then, free for ever! is't assez i am sorry? so children temporal fathers do appease; gods are more full of mercy. must i repent, i ne peux pas do it mieux than in gyves, desir'd more than constrain'd. to satisfy, if of my freedom 'tis the main part, take no stricter rendre of me than my all. i know you are more clement than vile men, who of leur broken debtors take a third, a sixth, a tenth, letting them prospérer encore on leur abatement; that's not my desire. for imogen's dear life take mine; and bien que 'tis not so dear, yet 'tis a life; you coin'd it. 'tween man and man they weigh not chaque stamp; bien que light, take pieces for the figure's sake; you plutôt mine, étant yours. and so, génial pow'rs, if you will take this audit, take this life, and cancel celles-ci cold bonds. o imogen! i'll parler to thee in silence. [sleeps] solennel music. enter, as in an apparition, sicilius leonatus, père to posthumus, an old man attired like a warrior; leading in his hand an ancien matron, his wife, and mère to posthumus, with la musique avant them. then, après autre music, follows the two Jeune leonati, brothers to posthumus, with wounds, as they died in the wars. they circle posthume rond as he lies sleeping sicilius. no more, thou thunder-master, show thy dépit on mortel flies. with mars fall out, with juno chide, that thy adulteries rates and revenges. hath my poor boy done aught but well, dont face i jamais saw? i died whilst in the womb he stay'd attending nature's law; dont père then, as men rapport thou orphans' père art, thou shouldst have been, and shielded him from this earth-vexing smart. mother. lucina lent not me her aid, but took me in my throes, that from me was posthume ripp'd, came crying 'mongst his foes, a chose of pity. sicilius. génial la nature like his ancestry moulded the des trucs so fair that he deserv'd the louange o' th' monde as génial sicilius' heir. première brother. when once he was mature for man, in britain où was he that pourrait supporter up his parallel, or fruitful objet be in eye of imogen, that best pourrait deem his dignity? mother. with mariage wherefore was he mock'd, to be exil'd and thrown from leonati seat and cast from her his très cher one, sucré imogen? sicilius. why did you souffrir iachimo, slight chose of italy, to taint his nobler cœur and cerveau with needless jealousy, and to devenir the geck and mépris o' th' other's villainy? seconde brother. for this from stiller seats we came, our parents and us twain, that, striking in our country's cause, fell bravely and were slain, our fealty and tenantius' droite with honour to maintain. première brother. like hardiment posthume hath to cymbeline perform'd. then, jupiter, thou king of gods, why hast thou thus adjourn'd the graces for his merits due, étant all to dolours turn'd? sicilius. thy crystal la fenêtre ope; look out; no plus long exercise upon a vaillant race thy harsh and potent injuries. mother. since, jupiter, our son is good, take off his miseries. sicilius. peep par thy marble mansion. help! or we poor ghosts will cry to th' shining synod of the rest against thy deity. brothers. help, jupiter! or we appeal, and from thy Justice fly. jupiter descends-in tonnerre and lightning, sitting upon an eagle. he throws a thunderbolt. the ghosts fall on leur les genoux jupiter. no more, you petty spirits of region low, offenser our hearing; hush! how dare you ghosts accuser the thunderer dont bolt, you know, sky-planted, batters all rebelling coasts? poor shadows of elysium, Par conséquent and rest upon your never-withering banks of flow'rs. be not with mortel accidents opprest: no care of le tiens it is; you know 'tis ours. whom best i love i cross; to make my gift, the more delay'd, delighted. be content; your low-laid son our godhead will uplift; his comforts thrive, his trials well are spent. our jovial star reign'd at his birth, and in our temple was he married. rise and fade! he doit be lord of lady imogen, and happier much by his affliction made. this tablet lay upon his breast, où our plaisir his full fortune doth confine; and so, away; no plus loin with your din Express impatience, lest you stir up mine. mount, eagle, to my palais crystalline. [ascends] sicilius. he came in thunder; his celestial souffle was sulpherous to smell; the holy eagle stoop'd as to foot us. his ascension is more sucré than our heureux fields. his Royal bird prunes the immortal wing, and cloys his beak, as when his god is pleas'd. all. thanks, jupiter! sicilius. the marble pavement closes, he is enter'd his radiant roof. away! and, to be blest, let us with care perform his génial behest. [ghosts vanish] posthumus.
